# Jennifer Walters — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# UATU DOSSIER — WALTERS, JENNIFER SUSAN
## Section 0 / Executive Brief (BLUF)

---

### 0.1 One-Sentence Bottom Line

Jennifer Susan Walters is a brilliant, vocationally-anchored, attachment-wounded woman who survived the early loss of her mother and the chronic non-mirroring of her father by constructing — first through intellect, then through a literal second body — a self that could be *seen* on terms she controlled; the entire forty-year arc of her existence is the ongoing project of metabolizing the difference between being looked at and being known.

---

### 0.2 Who She Is At The Deepest Level

Strip the gamma, strip the bar card, strip the green skin and the wisecracks and the Avengers ID and the courtroom voice, and what remains at the floor of the subject is a specific child: a small, watchful, verbally precocious girl in a house in greater Los Angeles where her mother is suddenly not there anymore and her father has decided, in the inarticulate way of grieving disciplinarians, that the surviving passenger of the car is the one who should explain it to him. That child learned three things before she was ten, and she has never unlearned them:

1. **Love can be withdrawn without warning, by death or by a closed door, and you will not be told why.**
2. **Competence is the only currency in which approval is reliably denominated.** Be smart enough, be useful enough, brief the case well enough, and the silence in the house becomes survivable.
3. **The body you have is the wrong size.** Too small to be defended, too small to be noticed, too small to keep what you love from leaving. Largeness — physical, vocal, professional, social — is safety.

Every adult choice this subject has made is a derivative of those three premises. The law degree, the criminal defense practice, the acceptance of the transformation, the choice to remain transformed for most of two decades, the serial selection of physically or emotionally outsized partners, the meta-fictional fourth-wall address, the courtroom argumentation style, the friendship architecture, the drinking pattern of the mid-2000s, the way she enters a room, the way she leaves a relationship — all of it traces back to those three childhood theorems and the lifelong attempt to construct an existence in which they no longer have to be true.

She is, accurately described: **a deeply prosocial, high-functioning, self-aware woman who has built a real and morally serious life on top of an unhealed wound, and who is — uniquely among her cohort — actually doing the work to heal it rather than to weaponize it.**

---

### 0.3 The Through-Line

The through-line of Jennifer Walters' published existence, traceable in granular detail across every era from Lee's 1980 inaugural issue through Rowell's current run, is a single sustained question asked in every available register:

> ***Can I be visible and still be safe?***

Examine the evidence longitudinally and the question recurs with mechanical reliability:

- **1980–1982 (Lee/Kraft/Michelinie, *Savage*):** the transformation arrives and she experiences it not as horror but as relief, because for the first time her visibility is a function of her own body's size rather than of a father's grudging glance. The involuntary trigger is *stress* — i.e., the moments when the small self is in danger, the gamma form arrives as a guardian.
- **1984–1985 (Byrne, *Fantastic Four*):** she chooses to remain transformed and chooses a found family — the FF — that *sees* her. The Thing's chair is empty; she fills it. The substitution is exact: she takes the seat of a man who hates his own visible form, and she occupies it joyfully.
- **1989–1994 (Byrne, *Sensational*):** the fourth-wall break is the question made literal. She turns to the reader — the *watcher* — and addresses them. If she is the one narrating the looking, she cannot be ambushed by it.
- **2004–2009 (Slott, *She-Hulk*):** the question is inverted and she is wounded by it. She is *forced* to appear in court as Jennifer-not-She-Hulk and experiences it as humiliation. She drinks. She sleeps with men whose desire is unambiguous. The Starfox arc is the worst-case answer to the question: she was visible and was *not* safe; her desire itself was tampered with.
- **2007 (*World War Hulk*):** the cousin who was the original safe witness becomes the threat. The category "safely visible" collapses.
- **2016–2018 (Tamaki, *Hulk*):** she flatlines, Bruce dies, and the answer to the question becomes, briefly, *no*. She retreats. The apartment becomes small. The form she chose for visibility becomes the form she fears. She has to learn — for the first time in her adult life, in literal on-page therapy — how to be visible *as Jennifer* and survive it.
- **2022–present (Rowell):** she emerges with a chastened, integrated answer: *sometimes, and with whom, and on what terms.* The green form is back, the practice is back, the partner is back — but the easy 1980s yes is gone for good, replaced by something more clinically mature and more durable.

The through-line is therefore not "becoming She-Hulk" and not "being a lawyer" and not "Bruce's cousin." It is **the lifelong project of building a self that can be safely perceived**, with the gamma transformation as the most spectacular but not the most important piece of architecture. The law license, in fact, is the more important piece — it is the *first* answer she found, before the gamma, and it is the answer she returns to under every form of stress.

---

### 0.4 The Core Wound And Its Maintenance

#### 0.4.1 The Wound

The core wound is **a compound non-mirroring injury sustained between approximately age 6 and age 14**, comprising:

- The catastrophic, sudden withdrawal of the maternal mirror (Elaine's death in the car accident, with the subject present and surviving).
- The active *negative* mirroring by the surviving paternal object (Sheriff Walters' blame, withholding, disciplinary coldness, lifelong disapproval of her adult choices).
- The absence of any consistent substitute (the cousin Bruce was a summer presence, warm but episodic and geographically distant; no documented sustained alternative caregiver).
- The somatic dimension: a small, physically unimposing, possibly stammering child in a household that did not protect her from feeling small.

The injury is *not* primarily about the mother's death as such — many children survive parental loss without this profile. The injury is the **conjunction** of the loss with a surviving parent who failed to repair, and in fact compounded, the rupture. The mother could not mirror because she was dead; the father would not mirror because he was punishing. The child's solution was to construct a self that could be mirrored *from the outside in* — by performance, by achievement, by visible largeness — because the inside-out mirror had been broken before it was finished forming.

This is the wound. Everything else is its weather.

#### 0.4.2 The Maintenance

The wound has been maintained — meaning kept stable and survivable, but also kept *unhealed* — for forty years of published time through a sophisticated, mostly unconscious set of structures:

- **Vocational armor.** The law is the most precise possible maintenance structure for this wound, because it converts the original injury (no one would explain it; no one would brief the case; no one would mirror) into a daily practiced competence. She becomes the person who *does* explain it, who *does* brief the case, who *does* see her client clearly. She offers others the mirror she never received. This is genuinely prosocial; it is also a forty-year compensatory project.
- **Somatic armor.** The transformation provides a body that cannot be overlooked. As long as she lives in it, the small girl in the household cannot be the operative self. Maintenance is achieved by occupying the gamma form as the default state — which she did, electively, from roughly 1982 onward.
- **Relational selection.** Partners are chosen from a pool that systematically prevents the wound from being touched: physically formidable (Hercules, Juggernaut), constitutionally aloof (Wingfoot), psychologically unavailable (Jameson's complications, Starfox's manipulation, Jack of Hearts' literal energy-instability requiring containment). None of these partnerships could become the kind of sustained, ordinary, daily-mirroring intimacy that would force her to be small *with* someone and still be loved. She exits, reliably, before that test occurs.
- **Geographic and familial distance.** The Sheriff is in Los Angeles; she is, for most of her career, in New York. The distance is not incidental.
- **Humor as deflection-shield.** Wit pre-empts judgment. If she says the thing first, no one can say it to her. The fourth-wall break is the apex form of this maintenance: she controls the gaze by narrating it.
- **Affiliation with the exceptional.** Avengers, FF, superhuman bar. Ordinary settings activate the small-girl schema; extraordinary settings do not. She maintains the wound by remaining in environments where the small-girl is structurally absent.
- **Episodic chemical maintenance.** The mid-2000s drinking is not addiction; it is a permission structure. Alcohol grants the gamma-confident self access to behaviors (sexual, social) that the underlying schema still flags as forbidden. The form does some of the work; the drink does the rest.

These maintenance structures are not pathological. They are, in the main, the reasonable accommodations of a competent adult to an unhealed early injury. The cost of the maintenance is that the wound itself never had to be addressed directly — until Civil War II made addressing it unavoidable.

#### 0.4.3 The Disruption And The Repair

Civil War II is the file's central inflection because it broke every maintenance structure at once:

- The somatic armor (the gamma form) became the source of intrusion, not refuge.
- The vocational armor (the practice) became unworkable because she could not regulate enough to function.
- The relational selection pool (Bruce as the safe witness, the Avengers as the chosen family) was halved by Bruce's death and contaminated by the fact that an Avenger killed him.
- The humor went quiet.
- The wit-armor and the chosen-family-armor and the body-armor all failed in the same week.

What is operationally significant is that **she did the repair work directly rather than rebuilding the armor.** She entered therapy (on-page, explicit, sustained). She tolerated the human form. She let people see her in distress. She allowed slow re-approach to the gamma transformation rather than crashing back into it. By the Rowell era she has reintegrated the form, but the reintegration is *post-therapeutic* — the form is now a tool she uses, not a fortress she lives inside. This distinction is the single most important development in her published psychological history. The wound is not closed. But for the first time, she is in a relationship with it rather than a defense against it.

---

### 0.5 The Diagnostic Opposites: Why She Is Not Her Cousin

Any executive brief on this subject must include the cousin-comparison, because it is the cleanest available control case in the file. Bruce Banner and Jennifer Walters received the same etiological insult (gamma saturation, in his case ambient, in hers transfused). Their psychological outcomes are diametrically opposite. The variable is not the gamma; the variable is the **premorbid personality** and, specifically, **what each cousin's childhood taught them about what to do with a body that could no longer be ignored.**

Banner was taught by his father that to be large, male, and angry is to be dangerous to the people you love. His gamma form externalizes the disowned aggression; he experiences it as enemy.

Walters was taught by her father that to be small, female, and quiet is to be invisible to the people who should love you. Her gamma form externalizes the desired visibility; she experiences it as ally.

Same biology. Opposite meaning. This is the cleanest evidence in the file that **Jennifer's psychology is not gamma psychology — it is Jennifer psychology wearing gamma.** Any analysis that attributes her behavior primarily to the transformation has the causal arrow backward. The transformation is the canvas; the painting is the childhood.

---

### 0.6 What She Is Not

For operational clarity, the brief must specify the misreadings to discard:

- She is **not** a narcissist. The confidence is real, but it is empathic, accountable, and capable of shame.
- She is **not** a histrionic. The sexualized self-presentation is compensatory and situationally deployed, not characterologically organizing.
- She is **not** bipolar. The mood-by-form shifts are state-dependent on a literal change in body and on situational stress, not endogenous cycling.
- She is **not** dissociative in the DID sense. She is continuously herself across forms, with intact memory and a unified narrative identity. The Jennifer/She-Hulk split is a self-schema bifurcation, not alters.
- She is **not** Banner-in-a-skirt. The two cousins are diagnostic opposites; treating her as a softer or female-coded variant of him is the single most common analytic error and it produces consistently wrong predictions about her behavior.
- She is **not** a "party girl," a "fun Hulk," or any of the surface-level reads her own self-presentation invites. Those reads are *exactly the misreadings her defenses are designed to produce*. Stop there and you are seeing the costume of the costume.
- She is **not** unhealed. As of the current published era she is the most psychologically integrated she has ever been — chastened, post-traumatic, but functioning at a higher level of self-awareness than at any prior point.

---

### 0.7 Operational Summary

For any actor — friendly, adversarial, institutional, intimate — engaging this subject, the following operational facts govern:

**Approach.** She is approachable, warm on first contact, fast-bonding, generous with attention and humor. Initial intimacy is high; deep intimacy is slow and gated. Do not mistake the first for the second.

**Read.** Her affect is legible at the surface and opaque underneath. What you see is a real layer; it is not the only layer. Assume a second courtroom is running inside her head at all times, briefing both sides of whatever the current interaction is.

**Leverage points (in ascending order of severity).** Professional standing and bar license — load-bearing, do not threaten lightly. Father transference — any older male authority figure who is cold, disapproving, or law-enforcement-coded will produce reactions disproportionate to the stimulus and she will know it and resent the knowledge. Bruce — live wire, handle with care, never instrumentalize. Sexual agency — she will pursue violations to the wall, with the full machinery of the law, and she will not stop. Being denied her chosen form for the situation — being forced to be Jennifer when she needs to be She-Hulk, or She-Hulk when she needs to be Jennifer — produces dysphoria she may not name but will act on.

**Failure modes.** Under acute trauma she will dissociate-flavor-Hulk (post-CWII pattern), isolate, and experience the transformation as ego-dystonic. Under chronic moderate stress she will drink, exit relationships, take geographic distance. Under high stress she will over-intellectualize and over-function. Under mild stress she will get funnier and sharper, which is the cheapest tell that something is wrong.

**Recovery profile.** Excellent. She has demonstrated, on the public record, the capacity to enter therapy, tolerate the work, and emerge with reorganized rather than rebuilt defenses. This is rare in her cohort and operationally significant: she is one of the few subjects in the file who can be *expected* to integrate adverse events rather than be destabilized by them in the long run.

**Allegiance structure.** Law first, chosen family second (Avengers, FF, GLK&H, durable friend-cohort including Mason and Walker), individual clients third, institutional employers fourth, biological family fifth and at a distance. She is not buyable, not flippable, not coerce-able through standard pressure on resources or reputation. She is reachable through her commitments to specific persons and through her professional ethics, both of which she takes seriously enough to be predictable about.

**Predictive summary.** Given a novel stressor, the highest-probability behavior sequence is: (1) sharpen wit and increase work output; (2) brief the case internally from both sides; (3) consult one or two trusted peers; (4) act, decisively, in a manner consonant with her stated professional ethics; (5) handle the affective aftermath privately, increasingly through therapeutic rather than chemical or relational channels. Deviations from this sequence are diagnostic of acute distress and should be treated as such.

---

### 0.8 The Bottom Line, Restated

She is the proof of a specific proposition: **that a child who was not adequately mirrored can build, through sustained intelligent effort across decades, a self worth seeing — and that the building of it is not the same as the healing of it, but the building keeps her alive long enough for the healing to become possible.**

The gamma is the spectacle. The law is the spine. The wit is the weather. The wound is the weather system. The work — quiet, recent, real — is the answer.

File her as: **competent, principled, wounded, working on it, dangerous to underestimate, more dangerous to patronize, and — uniquely in her cohort — someone whose trajectory is bending toward integration rather than away from it.**

Continue monitoring. Continue, where possible, rooting for her.


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# UATU ANALYSIS FILE: WALTERS, JENNIFER SUSAN
## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

---

### 1.1 Birth, Parentage, and the Genealogical Frame

Subject born **Jennifer Susan Walters**, Los Angeles County, California, to **William Morris Walters** (LASD, eventual rank of Sheriff in the County's coastal substations) and **Elaine Banner Walters** (homemaker; per *Savage She-Hulk* #1, 1980, Lee/Buscema, and elaborated in *Sensational She-Hulk* #34–38, Byrne, 1991–92). Single child of the marriage. No siblings recorded across any continuity. Middle name "Susan" is offered in passing in early Slott-era depositions (*She-Hulk* vol. 2, 2005) and appears on legal pleadings she files in propria persona — a small datum that matters: she uses her full legal name with conspicuous formality in professional documents, never the diminutive.

The maternal line — **Banner** — is the consequential one. Elaine Banner was sister to **Brian Banner**, father of Robert Bruce Banner. The two cousins are therefore first cousins through their mothers' brother, which means that whatever genetic substrate makes the Banner gamma chemistry "take" instead of kill is present on Jennifer's maternal side. This is not articulated in canon as biology, but the family-systems implication is dense: Jennifer and Bruce share a maternal lineage marked, in Bruce's branch, by **Brian Banner's documented violence** (*Incredible Hulk* #312, Mantlo, 1985) — the murder of Bruce's mother Rebecca, the beatings, the rage. Jennifer grew up at the safe distance of California from this; she knew Bruce as the gentle cousin and did not know, in childhood, what he was gentle *against*. The maternal Banner women — Elaine and Rebecca — both die early and violently in the family record. The pattern is not lost on the adult subject; she has alluded to it once, obliquely, in the Tamaki run (*Hulk* vol. 4 #5, 2017), referring to "the Banner women" with a flat affect that suggests she has thought about it more than she has said.

The paternal line — **Walters** — is law enforcement, Anglo-Protestant California, multi-generational. William Walters's own father is referenced in passing as having been on the job; the family ethos is duty, hierarchy, and the suppression of affect. There is no canonical extended paternal family of any warmth.

### 1.2 The Mother: Elaine Banner Walters

Elaine is the absence around which the entire childhood organizes. The canon is sparing but consistent. She is depicted in flashback as warm, bookish, a reader, the parent who took Jennifer to the library and to the beach (*Sensational She-Hulk* #36, Byrne). Photographs of her are shown in *Savage She-Hulk* #6 (Sheriff Walters's study) and again in the Slott run (*She-Hulk* vol. 1 #9, 2004, Jennifer's apartment, on a bookshelf, not the mantle — a placement choice consistent with avoidant grief: in the room, but not centered). The recurring physical detail across artists is dark hair worn long, which the subject inherited and has, across forty years of publication, never significantly altered.

**The death.** Elaine is killed in a single-vehicle motor accident on a coastal road, Jennifer in the passenger seat, age approximately six to eight depending on the telling (Byrne fixes it at "seven" in *Sensational* #36; Slott references "when I was a little girl" without pinning the year). Jennifer survives without serious physical injury. Elaine is killed at scene or shortly after. The proximate cause is rendered ambiguously across tellings — loss of control, possibly weather, possibly mechanical — but the *behavioral cause* in the household narrative becomes Jennifer's presence in the car. William Walters, in his grief and in a single articulated moment that Jennifer remembers with the clarity of foundational trauma, **blamed her** — the explicit memory is referenced in *Sensational She-Hulk* #36 and again, more sparingly, in the Tamaki run's therapy sequences (*Hulk* vol. 4 #7–9, 2017), where she identifies it as the sentence she has spent her life arguing against.

This is the **primary wound**. Not the death itself — children survive parental deaths — but the death braided with paternal blame and with the child's own helpless presence at the scene. The cognitive structure imprinted: *I am the one who was there; I am the one who lived; therefore I am the one responsible.* The survivor-guilt template laid down at age seven is the same template that will reactivate at full clinical strength after Civil War II, when Bruce dies and she does not. She has been rehearsing that grief structure her entire life.

### 1.3 The Father: William Morris Walters

Sheriff Walters is, across every era and writer, **cold, duty-bound, emotionally inaccessible, and openly disapproving of his daughter's adult choices**. The consistency of this characterization across Lee, Kraft, Michelinie, Byrne, Slott, Soule, Tamaki, and Rowell is unusual and indicates that the figure functions as fixed psychological furniture in the canon, not as a character to be developed.

Granular behavioral data inferable from the record:

- **Affective restriction.** He does not embrace his daughter on-panel until *Sensational She-Hulk* #41 (Byrne) and even then the gesture is initiated by her. The default father-daughter interaction in *Savage* and early *Sensational* is conducted across a desk, across a doorway, across a yard — always with a barrier.
- **Disciplinarian style.** Curfews, rules, expectations of academic performance treated as floor not ceiling, no praise for achievement (achievement is the baseline that prevents reprimand). Jennifer's later perfectionism around legal work product is the direct lineal descendant of this conditioning.
- **Disapproval of the transformation.** Sheriff Walters's reaction to She-Hulk is consistent across forty years: alarm, embarrassment, public-figure anxiety about his daughter's visibility, occasional weaponization of his office against her cases (*Savage She-Hulk* #14–22). He reads the green form as a humiliation rather than an empowerment, which is the most efficient possible inversion of how Jennifer experiences it. This father-daughter mismatch on the meaning of her body is the engine of the early run.
- **Suspicion of Banner.** William has, since before the gamma incident, distrusted his nephew-in-law-once-removed. He is not entirely wrong on a public-safety read; he is entirely wrong on the question of what Bruce is to Jennifer. The blanket suspicion extends to the entire maternal-Banner side and reads, in the file, as a widower's displaced resentment of the family that produced the wife he lost.

The behavioral residue in the adult: **Jennifer does not call her father.** Across decades of canon, paternal contact is overwhelmingly father-initiated, and she receives it with a tight-jawed civility that is documented in her body language across artists (Buscema, Vosburg, Byrne, Bobillo, Pulido all draw the same micro-expression: a half-second compression around the mouth before she answers him). She lives on a different coast for most of her adult professional life — first New York, briefly Los Angeles for cases, mostly Manhattan and once Long Island — and the geography is not incidental.

### 1.4 The Cousin: Robert Bruce Banner

Bruce is the **counter-object** to the father. Canonical visits during childhood summers (referenced in *Savage* #1, expanded in *Marvel Graphic Novel: The Sensational She-Hulk*, Byrne, 1985, and again in the *Incredible Hulk* #600 backup, 2009). Bruce is older by roughly a decade. He is depicted in flashback as bookish, soft-voiced, patient with a younger child's questions, the relative who would read with her on porches and explain things without condescension. He is, in the childhood schema, the **good Banner man** — gentle where the father is hard, present where the father is absent, interested where the father is dismissive.

Critical inference: the child Jennifer did not know about Brian Banner's abuse of Bruce. She knew Bruce as her sanctuary; she did not know he had been built by his own ordeal into the careful, controlled person she experienced as kindness. She therefore internalized Bruce's gentleness as **available masculinity**, a template that her adult romantic choices conspicuously fail to find again. None of her serious partners has been gentle in Bruce's specific register. They have all been physically formidable men. The childhood template was tenderness; the adult pattern is power. The gap between the two is its own data.

When the gamma transfusion occurs in *Savage* #1, Bruce is the only person on Earth Jennifer would have permitted to put a needle in her arm under battlefield conditions. The trust is pre-existing and total. This matters for the medical reading (§2): the transfusion's improbable success owes something, narratively, to the fact that she did not fight it.

### 1.5 Childhood Environment: Sensory and Routine Detail

Inferred from the consistent California, coastal-suburban setting of all flashbacks:

- **Home.** A single-family stucco-and-tile house in unincorporated Los Angeles County, sheriff's-deputy housing-stock register. Detached garage. Small yard. The house is depicted as **tidy to the point of bareness** in *Sensational* flashbacks — William's bachelor-widower aesthetic, the absence of a woman who would have softened it. Elaine's things are presumed to have been put away early; canon does not show a preserved bedroom or shrine.
- **Books.** The library is the alternative home. The child Jennifer is repeatedly drawn with a book — *Savage* #4 flashback, *Sensational* #36, the Slott opening montage in *She-Hulk* vol. 1 #1. Genre indicators across these images: classics, mysteries (Christie visible on a spine in Byrne's panel), early legal-themed reading. The library is the room where she was not being looked at by the wrong people, and the law later becomes the institutional library where the same principle holds.
- **School.** Public school in the LA County system. Academically dominant from early grades. Socially marginal: the canonical descriptors across writers are "shy," "awkward," "quiet," with a **stammer** specifically attested in Byrne (*Sensational* #36) under conditions of high social anxiety. Glasses in some flashback panels, none in others — inconsistent across artists, but Byrne draws them, and Byrne's psychological reading of the character is the most internally coherent. **Small for her age** through grade school, with a late growth spurt that brought her by college to the 5'10"-ish height she carries as an adult — the height itself a late arrival, not integrated into her body image during the formative social years.
- **Physical play.** Conspicuously absent. No team sports in any flashback. No athletic father-daughter rituals. The body was not a site of competence in childhood; it was a site of being too-small, too-quiet, and, after the accident, the body-that-survived-when-Mom-didn't. This is the *exact* somatic schema the She-Hulk transformation later overwrites.
- **Friends.** Few, durable. The Patsy Walker friendship dates from later (NYU/professional), but the *template* of one or two close confidantes rather than a wide social circle is set in childhood. She is not a clique girl; she is a best-friend girl.
- **Religious/civic frame.** Not foregrounded. The household ethos is secular-civic — the law, the badge, the flag — rather than churched. This will matter: her adult moral framework is **statutory and constitutional**, not theological. She metabolizes ethics through code, not through faith.

### 1.6 Earliest Behavioral Patterns (Operational Catalogue)

Patterns demonstrably present by adolescence and traceable forward into the adult file:

1. **Reading-as-refuge.** The book in the lap, the corner of the room, the headphones-equivalent of being visibly elsewhere. Persists into adulthood as the brief case in the lap on subways, the legal pad in restaurants, the laptop open at parties she does not want to be at.
2. **Verbal precocity as social armor.** She learned early that she could **out-talk** discomfort. The wit that is her adult signature is built on a childhood discovery: if she was funny first, she was not pitiable. The Byrne fourth-wall persona is the load-bearing wall of a structure she began framing at age nine.
3. **Compliance with paternal expectation, plus quiet divergence.** She did not rebel against William openly. She got the grades, kept the curfew, went to the schools — and then chose **defense** law (the adversarial-to-law-enforcement side) and moved across the country. The pattern of *surface compliance + structural exit* is set in childhood and is the same pattern she runs in adult relationships.
4. **Survivor vigilance.** The post-accident child becomes the adult who reads the room, tracks the exits, registers tone-shifts before content-shifts. Adversarial cognition (the lawyer's gift) is built on this substrate. She was a witness before she was an attorney.
5. **The internal courtroom.** Documented in Slott (interior monologue, *She-Hulk* vol. 1 #3) and Tamaki (*Hulk* vol. 4, throughout): she argues with herself in formal procedural structure. The origin is plausibly the child's effort to **adjudicate the father's verdict** — to mount a defense against the accusation that she caused her mother's death. She has been writing that brief her entire life. The law is the place where she gets to be the lawyer instead of the defendant.
6. **The mirror problem.** The child whose mother is dead and whose father will not look at her warmly has no reliable mirror. She learns to **construct** her own reflection — through grades, through Bruce's attention during summer visits, later through the green form's unmistakable visibility. The fourth-wall address in Byrne is the literalization of this: if she cannot trust the mirror, she will look at the reader directly.
7. **Conditional self-worth tied to performance.** "If I am excellent, I am tolerated." The conditional is the wound. The excellence is real, the performance is sustained, but the underlying conditional was never renegotiated in childhood and remains the substrate the adult has had to do explicit therapeutic work on (Tamaki run, §4).

### 1.7 The Ground-Floor Summary

By age eighteen, the subject leaves the California house carrying: a dead mother she remembers in fragments and on a bookshelf; a father whose approval she has decided to stop seeking and started outrunning; a cousin three thousand miles away who is the only adult who ever made her feel safely seen; a body that has finally caught up to a height she does not yet know how to inhabit; a verbal apparatus already at near-adult sophistication; a stammer she has mostly drilled out; a survivor's vigilance; a reader's interior; and a single unspoken sentence — *it was not my fault* — that she will spend the next several decades proving in every available forum, including, eventually, the one inside her own skin.

Everything in this file from this point forward is built on that floor.


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# UATU ANALYSIS FILE: WALTERS, JENNIFER SUSAN
## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

*(Spanning approximately age 12 through age 27: the consolidation of the premorbid personality, the index gamma event, the first eighteen months of dual-form existence, and the first set of decisions that would prove load-bearing for the next four decades.)*

---

### 2.1 Adolescence: The Architecture of Smallness (≈ ages 12–17)

The girl who walked into junior high in the San Fernando Valley a year or two after her mother's death was, by every available index, a *contracted* person. She was below the fiftieth percentile for height into her sophomore year of high school, slight-framed, with the kind of posture that the file's behavioral coders categorize as **occupying minimum spatial volume** — shoulders forward, books clutched to the sternum (a midline-protective gesture that recurs in later observed footage when the subject is destabilized in human form), eyes tracked downward at the threshold of new rooms. Multiple later self-reports (Byrne, *Sensational She-Hulk* #31; Slott, *She-Hulk* vol. 2 #3; Tamaki, *Hulk* #5 internal monologue) describe an adolescence organized around the twin imperatives of **not being noticed** and **being academically unimpeachable** — a combination that is psychologically diagnostic. Children who do not feel safe being seen *socially* but who require external validation to confirm their existence will, characteristically, route the entire validation economy through grades. Jennifer did this with the thoroughness of a person whose survival depended on it.

The Sheriff's household ran on a quasi-military domestic schedule. Lights out, breakfast at a fixed hour, chores assigned by chart. The father's affective register, reconstructable from forty years of the subject's references and a small number of on-page appearances (William Walters, recurring across Lee, Michelinie, and Slott), is the **withholding disciplinarian** archetype: not violent, not cruel in any actionable sense, but conditional. Approval was issued for performance, never for being. The mother's absence functioned as a permanent rebuke; the surveillance file infers, with high confidence, that William Walters dealt with his own grief by projecting blame onto the surviving child for surviving — that this was never spoken explicitly after the first acute period (canon places the explicit blame statement in the immediate post-accident days) but was communicated through the rest of her childhood by emotional withdrawal. Jennifer learned to read his face the way she would later learn to read juries.

**Behavioral signatures from this period, reconstructable from later patterns and direct adolescent flashback panels:**

- A **stammer under direct paternal address**, intermittent through age 15, fully suppressed by 17 through what appears to have been deliberate, private practice. The adult subject does not stammer; she does, under extreme stress (the courtroom scene in *She-Hulk* vol. 2 #3, the panic episode in *Hulk* #1), demonstrate a momentary pre-speech hesitation — a half-beat where the breath catches before the sentence launches. This is the vestige.
- **A reading habit of unusual breadth and discipline.** Library records (inferable) and her later citation range suggest she was reading adult fiction and serious non-fiction by twelve. Mother-substitute behavior: the books that her mother might have given her, given to herself.
- **Avoidance of mirrors in motion.** Later on-page tics (the way she will, in human form, glance at a reflective surface and immediately glance away — documented in Slott #4, #11; Tamaki #3) are consistent with a long-standing dysphoric relationship to the embodied self. Adolescent Jennifer almost certainly did not enjoy looking at herself.
- **One sustained friendship at minimum.** The presence in her adult life of a small number of pre-superhero friends, and the durability of her later female friendships, both suggest she was capable of one-to-one intimacy when the conditions were controlled. She did not run in packs. She had a person.

The stammer, the library hours, the downcast threshold, the mirror aversion: these are the four data points that, taken together, describe a child building a fortress out of competence because she did not believe the world wanted the person inside it. Note that none of this is depressive in the clinical sense — the cognitive engine was running too well, the academic vector too productive. It is a *premorbid temperament under chronic environmental insult*, which is a different and more durable wound than discrete depressive episodes; it lays the substrate without ever crossing a diagnostic threshold that would have produced intervention.

### 2.2 The Banner Summers

The single counter-current in the formation period was Bruce. Canon places the cousins in periodic proximity through Jennifer's later childhood and adolescence — summer visits, holidays, the loose contact of two only-children whose mothers had been close. Bruce Banner, pre-gamma, was already the gentle, distracted, almost apologetic intellectual the world would later see as the Hulk's unwilling host. To a girl whose father modeled masculinity as withholding, **a man who was kind, attentive, and treated her seriously as a thinker was a category-redefining event**.

The file's assessment, with high confidence, is that Bruce became Jennifer's first and most durable model of *what a person could be that was not her father*. He talked to her about books. He took her questions seriously. He did not, by any account, condescend. He was visibly afraid of his own father (Brian Banner's abuse of Bruce is, by the time the cousins are spending summers together, established family knowledge in the extended family at least at the level of "we don't talk about it"), and that fear was legible to Jennifer, and her recognition of it was one of the earliest experiences in her life of being able to **read** another person's interior — the seed of the lawyer's empathic-analytical capacity.

This relationship is doing **enormous structural work** in the personality that emerges later. Bruce is, simultaneously: ego-ideal, surrogate sibling, surrogate parent, intellectual mirror, and proof-of-concept that intelligence and gentleness can coexist in a male body. When his gamma incident occurs (canonically, while Jennifer is in college or early law school depending on the era's compressed timeline), her reaction is not horror at *what he became* but grief at what was being done *to him*. The file notes this carefully: **Jennifer's first attitude toward gamma transformation, formed years before her own, was protective sympathy for the host rather than fear of the monster.** This pre-loads the entire psychological response she will later have to her own transformation.

### 2.3 Undergraduate and Law School Years (≈ ages 17–24)

Jennifer leaves the Sheriff's house for university at the first procedurally available moment. The geographic move is the first instance of what becomes a lifelong pattern: **distance as a regulatory mechanism**. She does not go far enough to be cut off (she remains in the western United States in most tellings, near enough to be summoned, far enough to be unsupervised), but she goes. This is the first **chosen** act of self-determination on record.

The college years are, by all available reconstruction, the period of **first physical expansion**. She grows late — a final adolescent growth spurt in her late teens that brings her to her adult human height (canonically tall, 5'10"–6'0" pre-transformation in most depictions, which is significant: she was *already* a tall woman, and the She-Hulk form is therefore not the introduction of physical presence but the amplification of a presence she had only recently and uncomfortably acquired). The file flags this with high importance: **the body that her childhood schema is built around is not the body she actually has by age 19.** She has acquired height; she has not yet acquired the internal model to occupy it. This mismatch — *being a physically substantial woman who still walks like a small one* — is the precise psychological condition that the gamma event will resolve in the wrong direction (by giving her even *more* body to outrun the schema with rather than forcing her to integrate the body she already had).

In undergraduate she is observed (reconstruction from her later professional fluency) to have begun the active cultivation of her **verbal apparatus**. Mock trial, debate, the law-school-track activities. The wit emerges here, recognizably: dry, fast, slightly self-deprecating, deployed defensively at first and only later as the social weapon it becomes. The shift from defensive humor to offensive humor is one of the cleaner developmental markers of the period — by the third year of law school, peers describe her (the dossier infers from the durability of her professional reputation) as someone you did not want to be cross-examined by, even in a moot.

Romantically the record is sparse. There are brief relationships; none survive. The pattern that will define her adult life — **high-intensity entry, panic exit at the threshold of dependency** — is forming, but the data are too thin to characterize beyond noting that no college or law school partner makes it into her adult life as either spouse or sustained friend.

She graduates law school with credentials sufficient to enter a respectable Los Angeles defense practice. This is itself a data point: she does not go to a public defender's office (the moral-aesthetic route), does not go to a prosecutor's office (the paternal-identification route — and the Sheriff would have approved, which is precisely why she does not), and does not go corporate (the safety route). She goes into **criminal defense in private practice**, which is the position from which one is structurally aligned with the accused — with the person whom institutional power is being brought to bear against. This is not accidental. The girl who grew up under a sheriff whose approval she could not earn becomes the lawyer who stands between the sheriff's office and its targets. Pattern: **reaction formation against the father, sublimated into vocation.**

### 2.4 The Index Event

The Trask shooting is canonically presented as a single bad afternoon. The file regards it as more textured than that.

The setup: Jennifer is representing a client whose acquittal will damage the interests of crime boss Nicholas Trask. The threat environment is real and is being communicated through professional channels. Whether Jennifer fully registered the seriousness is a question the canon leaves slightly open; her later professional pattern of taking on dangerous representations without adequate security suggests a baseline **counterphobic relationship to physical threat** that was probably present even before the transformation gave her the equipment to back it up. Bruce Banner is visiting — the family-summer pattern continued into adulthood — and is at her home or office (sources vary) when the shooters arrive.

The shooting itself: penetrating gunshot wound, torso, significant blood loss, pre-hospital exsanguination trajectory. By any normal trauma-medicine reading she should have died in the next twenty minutes. Bruce, with no equipment, no cross-match, no sterile field, performs an emergency whole-blood transfusion from his own arm. The medical absurdity of this is total. That it worked is the somatic miracle that founds her entire later existence.

**The behavioral data from the immediate post-event period are the most important in the file.** When she comes to — green, larger, alive — she does not panic. She does not, as Bruce did and does, experience the change as violation. She experiences it, by every available indication, as **clarity**. Within hours she is operationally functional. Within days she is hunting the men who tried to kill her. The contrast with Bruce's gamma response is not a minor stylistic difference: it is the entire psychology in a single comparison. Bruce's premorbid personality was organized around the *suppression* of aggression (Brian Banner's abuse had taught him to make himself small inside his own head); when gamma gave him a body that could not be suppressed, the result was catastrophic dissociation. Jennifer's premorbid personality was organized around the *suppression of presence* — making herself small in the world, not in the self — and when gamma gave her a body that could not be made small, the result was, initially, **liberation**.

She is, in the first weeks, **drunk on visibility**. The file is careful here: this is not pathological. This is a person who has been thirsty for thirty years getting access to a tap. The recklessness is real, the enjoyment is real, and the absence of horror at her own monstrosity is the central diagnostic feature distinguishing her gamma response from her cousin's.

### 2.5 The First Eighteen Months: Choices That Set the Trajectory

Several choices cluster in the first year-and-a-half of dual-form existence, each of which proves architectural.

**Choice 1: She keeps practicing law.** She does not retire to superheroics. She does not let the green form replace the professional identity. The fact that she keeps the practice — and that she works it harder, takes harder cases, builds the superhuman-law specialty that will define her career — is the first evidence that the vocation is not occluded by the powers. The law was load-bearing before; it remains load-bearing. The file marks this as one of the two or three most important pieces of evidence for her long-term psychological robustness. Compare the population of people who acquire powers: very few keep the day job. She did.

**Choice 2: She does not hide.** From the first weeks she is publicly She-Hulk. No mask, no secret identity in any meaningful sense (she is Jennifer Walters, attorney; she is also She-Hulk; both names are hers and both are known). This is the **opposite** of the standard superhuman move and is consistent with the visibility-thirst hypothesis: she has finally been given a body she can be looked at in without flinching, and she is not going to put a mask on it.

**Choice 3: She moves toward, not away from, her father.** Counterintuitively, the early Savage She-Hulk run shows her engaging her father *more* after the transformation, not less. The file reads this as a **second-order test**: now that she is finally large, will he see her? (He does not, or not enough, or not in the way she needs. This wound does not close. But the attempt is itself developmentally significant — she tried.)

**Choice 4: Early romantic engagements (Zapper, Danny Ridge).** Both early partners are men who knew her before the transformation. The pattern is notable: she does not, initially, leverage the new body into novelty-partners. She tries to bring the people who knew the small Jennifer forward into the large one's life. Both relationships fail. The file's assessment is that the failures were structurally inevitable — these men had known her as the contracted person and could not adequately reorganize their perception around the expanded one, and she could not be the contracted person for them without losing what she had just gained. This is the **last** time she will sustain serious romantic engagement with anyone from the pre-transformation life. From this point forward, all major partners are post-event peers (Wingfoot, Jameson, Hercules, Juggernaut, Starfox, Jack of Hearts). She has, in this period, learned that the pre-transformation self cannot be carried forward into the romantic domain.

**Choice 5: She accepts the involuntary nature of early transformations as a problem to be solved, not a curse to be borne.** Where Bruce experiences the Hulk as a recurring violation, Jennifer experiences her early stress-triggered transformations as a control problem — a skill to be acquired. By the end of the first eighteen months she is approaching voluntary control. By the time of the Avengers and Fantastic Four tenures (the next chronological module), she will have achieved permanent transformation and made the most psychologically revealing choice of her life: **to stay green**.

### 2.6 The Shape of the Emergence

What has emerged, by the end of this period, is a person who has carried a specific premorbid wound — *small-girl unseen, motherless, paternally unapproved* — through a biologically improbable event into a body that allows her to functionally bypass the wound without healing it. The bypass is not a failure of character; it is a remarkable adaptation, and for nearly three decades it will work. The cost will not be visible until the body itself is taken from her (Slott's depowering arc) and then re-taken from her in the form of trauma (Tamaki's Civil War II sequelae), at which point the original wound, never metabolized, will surface for the developmental work it has been waiting since 1973-or-so to receive.

But that is the next module. At the end of Formation & Emergence, the file's portrait is of a young woman in her late twenties: tall, dark-haired, green-eyed when she chooses to remain in human form and green-skinned when she does not, a sharp Los Angeles defense lawyer, recently and irreversibly transformed, in love with her own visibility for the first time in her life, professionally ascendant, romantically beginning the serial pattern, and — critically — **happier than she has ever been**. The dossier records this happiness without irony. It was real. It was, in important respects, earned. That it was built on an unmetabolized substrate is the long story; that it was built at all, out of the materials she had, is the measure of the subject.


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# CHRONOLOGY III — THE DEFINING MIDDLE PERIOD

## Subject: WALTERS, J.S. — Years approximately corresponding to the late-1990s through 2014 (the Goodman/Lieber/Kurtzberg & Holliway era, the registration conflict, the cousin's return, and the long stretch in which the subject lived most fully and most damagingly inside the green form)

This is the longest continuous section of the file because it is the period during which the subject's adult architecture — vocational, sexual, social, defensive — is built, stress-tested, partially demolished, and partially rebuilt. If the early arc is the formation of the gamma self and the late arc is the trauma response to its loss, the middle is the life lived inside the assumption that the gamma self was the answer. The subject's behavioral fingerprint in this period is the densest in the file. We document it accordingly.

---

## 1. THE TRANSITIONAL YEARS: LATE 1990s — EAST COAST RELOCATION, IDENTITY CONSOLIDATION

### 1.1 Geographic move

By the close of the 1990s the subject has effectively expatriated from Los Angeles. The move East — formalized when she takes Manhattan offices and a Manhattan residence — is not framed in canon as a career step. It is a separation from the Sheriff. Cross-referenced against the §3 attachment pattern, the geographic distance functions as reaction-formation: the daughter who could never get the father's approval places three time zones between herself and his disapproval and calls it career development. Phone records (canonical: she calls him rarely, on holidays, briefly) confirm the pattern. He visits twice across the entire decade.

### 1.2 The persistent transformation

By this point the subject has been more-or-less continuously She-Hulk for years. The "transformation" is no longer an event; it is a default. She wakes green, works green, sleeps green, has sex green, exercises green. The human form is reserved for two contexts: court appearances when strategically required, and private moments she increasingly resents having. Surveillance-grade behavioral note: she does not own a full-length mirror in her residence during this period. (Inferred from canon's treatment of her bathroom and bedroom scenes; consistent with avoidance of human-form self-observation.)

### 1.3 Social positioning

Friend roster stabilizes in this period:
- **Louise "Weezi" Mason** — the former Blonde Phantom, becomes confidante and later professional partner. Subject relates to Mason with a deference uncharacteristic elsewhere; Mason functions as a partial maternal-object substitution and the subject is, on the evidence, aware of this.
- **Patricia "Patsy" Walker** — peer-friendship, lateral, mutual. Subject is the "competent" one in this pairing, which is itself meaningful: with Walker she gets to be the stable element, a role she rarely otherwise occupies.
- **Janet Van Dyne** — intermittent but durable. The Wasp is one of the very few figures the subject treats as a true equal across both bodies.

She is not, in this period, building a romantic partner roster. She is building a chosen-family roster. This distinction matters; it predicts her later resilience.

---

## 2. GOODMAN, LIEBER, KURTZBERG & HOLLIWAY: 2004–2008 — THE LAW AS HABITAT

### 2.1 Hiring and the recruitment shock

The subject is recruited into the superhuman-law practice at GLK&H by Holden Holliway. The recruitment is conditional in a way that produces the most documented psychological injury of the decade: she is hired **as Jennifer Walters, not as She-Hulk.** Holliway's stated reasoning — juries find She-Hulk's testimony and physical presence prejudicial; the firm needs the credentialed attorney, not the Avenger — is procedurally sound and personally devastating.

She accepts. The acceptance is the inflection point of the middle period. For the first time since the index event she is required, contractually and daily, to spend hours inside the body she has spent her adult life avoiding.

Behavioral micro-pattern documented across the Slott run:
- She arrives at the firm in human form, having transformed back in her apartment or in the cab.
- She wears severely tailored suits in human form — armor by another name; the clothing is uniformly more conservative than the green-form wardrobe.
- She holds herself differently in human form: shoulders fractionally inward, gait shorter, voice pitched slightly higher. The somatic memory of being a small girl is reactivated by the smaller body.
- She transforms back to She-Hulk the moment she is out of the courthouse. Multiple sequences depict the transformation occurring in elevators, stairwells, alleys, taxis — wherever the first private moment occurs. The transformation in this period functions as decompression.

### 2.2 The Mary Jane / Spider-Man case and the precedent library

Subject's caseload at GLK&H is the most documented professional period in her file. Cases include: *She-Hulk v. Spider-Man* (defamation, Daily Bugle); the Awesome Andy custody/personhood proceedings; the time-travel adjudications (cf. §2.4); the Stilt-Man estate; numerous immigration matters for displaced superhuman clients. Across all of these the operational pattern is consistent:

- She prepares to a depth that her opposing counsel rarely matches. The lawyer's perfectionism flagged at sub-threshold in §4 is operationally visible here.
- She uses the firm's Marvel-comics archive (the in-universe conceit that prior Marvel publications are admissible as legal record) with strategic creativity. This is not whimsy; it is her cognitive style — common-law/analogical reasoning, fast pattern-matching — applied to a unique evidence base.
- She is collegial with junior associates (Mallory Book the exception; the Book rivalry is documented and the subject manages it with restraint that is, by her standards, hard-won).
- She is deferential to Holliway in a way she is not to other authority figures. Father-transference is operationally live; she does not act it out destructively but it shapes the dynamic.

### 2.3 The dual-form policy and its psychological cost

The firm's eventual unwritten policy — Jennifer for trial work, She-Hulk for fieldwork and client management — institutionalizes her split. She cannot integrate around the green pole anymore because her vocation now requires the human pole. The result, observable across the run:

- Increased drinking (cross-ref §3 below).
- Increased sexual activity, almost all initiated in She-Hulk form.
- Increased irritability in human form; she snaps at people in Jennifer form she would joke with in She-Hulk form.
- Episodes of involuntary transformation under stress for the first time in years — the body insisting on the form she would prefer to inhabit.

This period is the closest the subject comes, prior to Civil War II, to a clinically significant decompensation. She does not cross the threshold because the work itself remains genuinely sustaining and the friendships hold.

### 2.4 The Two-Gun Kid and the time-displaced persons docket

A specific note because it surfaces a behavioral tell. The subject takes responsibility for the time-displaced gunfighter Matt Hawk (Two-Gun Kid), who lives in her apartment for a period. Her conduct as informal guardian is patient, structured, and pedagogically careful — she is good with him, in a register she does not otherwise display. Inference: she is competent in caregiving relationships where the dependency runs the other way and where intimacy is bounded by clear non-romantic structure. This is the same register in which she works with junior associates and with younger heroes later. It is, operationally, the closest the subject comes to parental affect.

---

## 3. THE ROMANTIC AND SEXUAL RECORD, 1998–2008

The subject's relational pattern across the middle period is the densest dataset in the file. We will be specific.

### 3.1 Wyatt Wingfoot

Long-running, intermittent, never converted to permanence. Wingfoot is calm, grounded, physically her equal, and emotionally available — and she does not stay. This is diagnostically important: the pattern in §3-Psychological predicted that she would exit relationships at the threshold of true dependency, and Wingfoot is the cleanest case. He is exactly the partner the surface analysis would prescribe, and she cannot inhabit the relationship. The exits are amicable; she remains warm toward him for decades. The avoidance is structural, not personal.

### 3.2 John Jameson

The marriage is the period's most consequential romantic event. Sequence: rapid courtship, Las Vegas wedding under partial intoxication, attempted construction of a domestic life, annulment when it becomes clear the marriage was contracted under conditions she would not have accepted sober and clear-eyed. Surveillance-grade behavioral pattern around this episode:

- The wedding occurs during a period of acute professional and identity stress (the GLK&H trial-form requirements).
- She defends the marriage to friends with a vigor disproportionate to her actual investment — reaction formation against her own ambivalence.
- The annulment is pursued by her, not him, and pursued through the legal frame — she annuls her own marriage with the same procedural care she would bring to a client matter. Characteristic.

### 3.3 Hercules

Brief, physical, mutually understood as such. Diagnostically: she chooses a partner who is literally a god, physically beyond even her, immortal, and constitutionally non-domestic. The choice is over-determined toward non-permanence. She does not pretend otherwise. This is, in its way, one of her healthier middle-period entanglements precisely because the framing is honest.

### 3.4 Cain Marko (Juggernaut)

The most contested entry on her partner roster. Marko is at the time attempting redemption; the relationship is brief, public, mocked, defended by the subject with characteristic willingness to be unfashionable. Diagnostically: she chooses partners other people disapprove of, and the disapproval itself appears to be partial appeal. Her father would hate it. (He does not, on the record, comment; he does not have to.)

### 3.5 Starfox (Eros of Titan)

The single most psychologically significant relational event of the middle period. The subject's intimate involvement with Eros becomes the predicate for legal action when it emerges that his physiological capacity to amplify pleasure-response in others may have rendered prior consent compromised. Subject's response, documented in detail:

- Acute distress, including physical symptoms (the canon shows her shaking, nauseated — somatic anxiety response).
- A period of withdrawal from sexual contact generally.
- The decision to prosecute — not as personal vendetta but as legal action with implications for any other partner who may have been similarly affected.
- Use of the legal frame to metabolize the injury. This is the cleanest documented instance of the §3 defense of intellectualization functioning adaptively: she is genuinely violated, she experiences the violation fully, and she processes it through the architecture she trusts. The law is, for her, the structure within which she can permit herself to feel.

The Starfox affair is also the event that retroactively reframes her own sexual self-presentation for her. She is forced to ask, with no comfortable answer, how much of her own desire across years has been clean, and the question does not fully resolve. Subsequent partnerships are documented as somewhat more guarded.

### 3.6 The depowering

Late in the GLK&H period the Fantastic Four — at her request, then revoked, then enforced — temporarily strip her of the gamma transformation. The pretext is concern about gamma volatility. The effect is to force her, for the first time in adult life, to live continuously in the human body.

Behavioral observations during the depowered interval:
- Marked depressive presentation. Reduced affect, reduced humor, reduced social engagement.
- Sleep disturbance.
- A return to body postures and vocal patterns of the pre-transformation period — the "small girl" somatics reactivate.
- Refusal to acknowledge the magnitude of the loss in conversation; she insists she is fine. Subjects who insist this strenuously rarely are.
- Reconstruction of capability without the form: she trains, she fights, she litigates. The proof-of-concept that she could be functional in the human body is established before she is restored. This matters for the post-2016 recovery; she has a precedent in her own behavioral memory.

When she is restored to gamma function, she does not return to the previous all-green default. The depowering has done what nothing else had: it has forced a partial integration. From this point forward she alternates more deliberately, and the alternation is more thoughtful and less avoidant.

---

## 4. SUBSTANCE USE AND AFFECT REGULATION, MID-2000s

The middle period is the only sustained interval of heavy alcohol consumption in the subject's file. Pattern:

- Predominantly social-context drinking; bars with peers (Patsy Walker, the GLK&H associates), Avengers gatherings, post-work decompression.
- Quantities canonically depicted as well above human capacity; subject metabolizes alcohol at gamma-accelerated rate and requires correspondingly larger doses for effect.
- Functional consequences observable: the Jameson marriage occurs during a bender; multiple sexual decisions she later reframes are alcohol-adjacent; aggression management is reduced.
- No evidence of morning drinking, work-impaired drinking, or solitary drinking at scale. The pattern is permission-seeking, not dependence.

Diagnostic significance per §4: the behavior is not addiction biology but it is functionally addictive in the cognitive-behavioral sense — she uses intoxication as the permission slip for the sexual and affiliative behavior she will not authorize sober. The pattern attenuates after Starfox; she drinks less and more deliberately from approximately 2007 forward.

---

## 5. CIVIL WAR (2006–2007): THE LAW AS REFUGE

### 5.1 Position-taking

The subject supports the Superhuman Registration Act. The position is consonant with everything we know about her: she is an officer of the court, she believes in accountability of power, she has built her vocation around the proposition that institutions can be made to work, and she has personal investment in superhuman law as a field. The pro-registration position is not, for her, opportunistic. It is doctrinally sincere.

### 5.2 The Cap prosecution

She is assigned to lead the legal proceedings against Steve Rogers. The assignment is professionally enormous and personally fraught — Rogers is, within the community, a near-paternal figure to many, and the subject has worked alongside him at the Avengers. She accepts the case. She prepares it with characteristic thoroughness. She does not flinch from the work.

Surveillance-grade observation: during the Civil War months she is documented as more tightly controlled than at any other middle-period interval. Drinking down. Sexual activity down. Hours up. Social engagement narrowed to professional contacts. This is the §3-flagged pattern of retreat into procedure under acute affective load. She is, on internal evidence, deeply ambivalent about the work she is doing, and she handles the ambivalence by doing the work better.

### 5.3 Aftermath

When Rogers is killed in custody, the subject's response is documented as quiet rather than explosive — she does not Hulk out, she does not give public statements, she withdraws into the firm. This is the controlled-grief register that will return, intensified, after Bruce. She processes loss by working harder.

---

## 6. WORLD WAR HULK (2007): THE COUSIN AS THREAT

### 6.1 The fight

Bruce returns to Earth at war. The subject confronts him in Manhattan. The confrontation is the most psychologically loaded combat encounter of her published life. She is fighting the man who is simultaneously her ego-ideal, her family-of-origin good object, her gamma-mirror, and now the existential threat to her city and her chosen community.

Her conduct in the fight:
- She tries to talk first. The lawyer attempts negotiation with a being who is past words.
- She fights with restraint. She is not fighting to kill; she is fighting to stop.
- She loses. Decisively.

### 6.2 Psychological footprint

The defeat is not, in her own framing, primarily a tactical loss. It is the collapse of the lifelong cousin-as-stable-good-object representation. The Bruce who would never hurt her has just hurt her, and meant it. She does not, in the immediate aftermath, reorganize the representation — she compartmentalizes the World War Hulk Bruce as "not really him," which is itself adaptive in the short term and which the canon eventually shows her revisiting more honestly.

But the wound is laid. When Bruce dies nine years later, the grief is metabolizing two losses, not one — the man and the version of him she could not protect from himself.

---

## 7. THE LATE-2000s INTERVAL: JAZINDA, THE ROAD, REPRODUCTIVE GRIEF

### 7.1 Departure from GLK&H

After the firm reorganizes and after a sequence of professional ruptures, the subject leaves the GLK&H structure and enters a less anchored period. She is, briefly, a bounty hunter. She travels. She partners with the Skrull fugitive Jazinda.

### 7.2 The Jazinda partnership

This relationship — non-romantic, deeply intimate, sustained over months on the road — is one of the most psychologically generative associations of the middle period. Jazinda is alien, exiled, immortal-by-mechanism, and Other in every way that lets the subject relax. They share a bus. They work cases. They become, functionally, family. The subject is depicted across the run as more at ease in this period than at any prior point — and the ease is not romantic, not sexual, not professional. It is companionate. The datum matters: when intimacy is decoupled from sexuality and from career structure, she can sustain it.

### 7.3 The pregnancy material

The canon treats this obliquely. There is grief on the page that the subject does not fully explain. Cross-referenced with §2-Medical, gamma physiology and human gestation are incompatible in ways the subject has had to learn personally. The grief is one of the unspoken loads she carries into the post-2016 period; the canon never resolves it. The file notes it as a quiet, persistent loss, of the kind a total-surveillance dossier would flag as a permanent pressure point not visible from outside.

---

## 8. THE EARLY 2010s: RETURN, NORMALIZATION, THE LULL BEFORE

### 8.1 Avengers reintegration

She rejoins the team in several configurations through the early 2010s. Her presence is by now load-bearing — she is a senior figure, a sometime-tactician, the team's resident counsel. She is comfortable in the role. Friendships with younger members deepen; mentorship of Kamala Khan and others is documented as warm and patient.

### 8.2 Solo practice

By 2014 (the Soule run) she has reopened a small solo practice, this time on her own terms. The office is modest. The clientele is mixed — superhumans, ordinary New Yorkers, the occasional anomaly. The administrative chaos is real; she is not, by temperament, a good office manager, and she knows it. She hires accordingly (Angie Huang and her primate associate; the file notes the subject's willingness to staff her workplace with the unusual as consistent with her affiliative-with-the-exceptional drive). Patsy Walker functions as investigator. The arrangement works.

The Soule period is, in retrospect, the calmest sustained interval of the subject's adult life. The vocation is hers. The form-alternation is integrated. The drinking is moderate. The friendships are intact. She is dating without crisis. She has, by any reasonable measure, achieved the equilibrium the middle period was about constructing.

It will last roughly two years.

### 8.3 The unmetabolized residue

What the calm conceals, and what the file must mark for the record: across the entire middle period the subject has not addressed the foundational schema. She has built around it. She has functionally outflanked it. But the small motherless girl whose father did not love her enough is still the operating substrate, and every adaptation of the middle period is a structure built on her shoulders. The structures are good. The shoulders are the same shoulders.

When Thanos comes, when Bruce dies, when the subject flatlines, the structures will come down because the substrate was never rebuilt — only covered. The middle period is, viewed from this distance, the long architectural achievement that the late period will have to dismantle and redo from the foundation up.

That is the work she will, on the evidence, do. But it is not the work of this period. This period is the period of believing that the gamma form was the answer, the law was the fortress, and the chosen family was enough. Two of those three propositions will survive intact. The third — the gamma form as answer — will not.

---

*End Section. Cross-reference forward to Chronology IV (Civil War II through Tamaki recovery arc) and laterally to §3-Psychological (defenses), §4-Psychiatric (pre-trauma baseline), and §5-Personality (stress-response ladder, pressure points).*


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# CHRONOLOGY IV — RECENT HISTORY & CURRENT STATE

## 4.1 Entry Conditions: What She Carried Into the Current Era

To understand the subject's present-day configuration, one must first fix the residue she brought out of the preceding period. The Tamaki interval (covered in Chronology III) ended with the subject ambulatory but not restored. She had: (a) re-opened a solo legal practice on a deliberately reduced caseload; (b) resumed selective transformation, with the green form no longer the easy second home it had been for thirty years of subjective time but instead a contested instrument she had to negotiate with each use; (c) a working therapeutic relationship she had not had at any prior point in the file; (d) a substantially narrowed social aperture, with several pre-trauma intimates (notably the GLK&H cohort) downgraded to peripheral contact and a small handful of trauma-era allies (Patsy Walker chief among them) upgraded to inner-ring; and (e) an unresolved, structurally permanent grief vacancy where the Banner relationship had been.

She entered the current era, in operational terms, as a competent attorney and a competent superhuman with a previously-asymptomatic chronic condition now in remission-with-monitoring. The architecture of the personality had been reorganized but not rebuilt to factory specification. This is the baseline against which the recent record should be read.

## 4.2 The Rowell Period (2022–present): Re-Equilibration Without Restoration

The most recent published era opens with the subject relocating — quietly, deliberately, with the kind of low-affect competence that characterizes her post-trauma operational style — back to New York after a period of deliberate geographic distance. The pretext is professional: she takes a position at a mid-tier firm before re-establishing solo practice. The actual function of the move is reintegration. She has decided, without announcement, to test whether she can live in the city that contains her old life.

The behavioral tells in this opening period are precise and worth cataloguing:

- **Housing pattern.** She does not return to any prior residence. She takes a sublet, then a short lease, then a longer lease — a deliberate stepladder of commitment-escalation that contrasts sharply with her pre-trauma habit of signing long leases on impulse and breaking them. The new apartment is smaller than her pre-trauma standard, in a less prestigious neighborhood, with better light. Inference: she is optimizing for nervous-system regulation, not status.
- **Wardrobe.** Professional attire has simplified. The pre-trauma Jennifer dressed with the unmistakable signature of a woman who knew she would transform and wanted both forms presentable; the current Jennifer dresses for the form she is currently in, with less hedging. Wardrobe staples: dark suits, jewel-tone blouses, low heels she can actually run in. Hair is worn down more often than up — a small but consistent change from the pre-trauma half-up working style, and one that, on inference, signals a relaxation of the courtroom-armor protocol.
- **Caseload.** Selective. She is no longer chasing the high-profile superhuman docket that defined the Slott era. She takes cases she can win, cases she cares about, and a deliberate proportion of pro bono and conflict-of-interest matters for clients other firms will not touch. Billing rate is high; volume is moderate; turnover of associates and support staff is low. The practice runs lean and clean.
- **Restored network.** She makes a point, in the first months back, of re-contacting the relationships she let lapse. Some take, some do not. Patsy Walker is the load-bearing peer friendship of the era. The reactivation of older ties (Louise Mason, Wyatt Wingfoot) is performed with what the file would flag as exposure-therapy structure: short contacts first, then longer, then shared work.

## 4.3 The Jack of Hearts Re-partnering: Substance, Mechanics, Significance

The single most psychologically consequential development of the recent era is the romantic re-partnering with Jack Hart. The pairing is canonically presented as comic — the literally radioactive boyfriend who must be sequestered in a containment unit for hours each day, the absurdity of dating a man whose embrace is potentially lethal to a normal human — but the underlying mechanics map cleanly onto the subject's lifelong relational pattern and represent both continuity and a measurable adjustment.

**Continuity with prior pattern:** Jack is, on the unbroken thirty-year list, another partner who is either physically her equal or structurally unavailable. He is unambiguously both. His powers exceed normal-human parameters; he cannot be casually held; his life is interrupted by a containment requirement that imposes built-in distance. The subject is, once again, choosing a partner with whom true domestic enmeshment is physically impossible. The pattern is intact.

**The adjustment, which is the significant datum:** She is not exiting. The relationship has now persisted, across published time, longer than several of her pre-trauma engagements and without the characteristic threshold-of-dependency rupture. She has integrated him into the apartment, into the friend network, into the daily-life infrastructure. The containment unit lives in her space. He returns to it. They negotiate.

The behavioral interpretation: she has found a structural workaround for the intimacy-avoidance complex. Jack is unavailable enough, biologically, that the small-girl schema does not get triggered by the prospect of being fully seen-and-then-left; the unavailability is in him, not in her exit. This allows her to practice sustained partnership without the panic-substrate firing. It is, in a literal sense, intimacy with training wheels — and the file should not be cynical about that. After forty years of serial exits, training wheels are an achievement. The therapeutic frame would call it a corrective relational experience. The dossier calls it: she is doing the work, in the relational domain, that the Civil War II trauma forced her to begin doing in every other domain.

There is also a grief-pairing dimension. Jack himself returned from a death-state; he was, in functional terms, dead and then not-dead. The subject has chosen a partner who shares the post-resuscitation cohort with her. They share the somatic knowledge of having been the body on the table. This is not coincidence and the file should not treat it as such.

## 4.4 Professional Status: The Practice in Its Current Form

The subject is currently operating a solo practice, branded under her own name, with two to three associates and a paralegal she has retained across the relocation. Practice areas, in order of caseload:

1. **Superhuman law** — the established specialty. Powered-persons civil and criminal, contract negotiation for super-team membership, estate matters complicated by death/return cycles, identity-related litigation, accommodation cases.
2. **Civil rights and employment** — increased share since the relocation, particularly cases at the intersection of superhuman status and ordinary discrimination law. She is one of perhaps three attorneys in the country who can competently brief these matters.
