Against the father: hyper-independence, geographic distance (LA origin, East Coast practice for most of adult life), professional autonomy, refusal of paternal advice or aid even when it would be useful, public deployment of opinions she knows he disapproves of. The behavior reads as "I do not need him" but the energetic cost of maintaining it discloses the opposite. A truly indifferent daughter would call occasionally; she does not call at all, which is more work, not less.

#### 6.2.3 Displacement

Anger originally addressed to the father is displaced onto institutional male authorities (judges who patronize her, opposing counsel who underestimate her, male teammates who try to manage her). The displaced anger is more freely expressed than the source anger could ever be; she will publicly demolish a senior partner who condescends to her while remaining unable to articulate a single sentence of grievance to her father directly.

#### 6.2.4 Rationalization

Specific to her relational exits. Each ended relationship is post-hoc explained in terms the listener cannot dispute: incompatibility of schedules, his career, my career, the timing, the geography. The pattern across enough partners that the explanations become statistically suspect; the real variable is proximity to threshold intimacy, and the rationalizations function to prevent her from having to examine that.

#### 6.2.5 Identification with the Aggressor (Selective)

In a narrow domain: courtroom behavior. She absorbed and weaponized the cold, exacting, withering register her father used on her, redirecting it at opposing counsel and hostile witnesses. The cross-examination voice is recognizably his voice. She did not just survive him; she took the weapon home with her and learned to use it for prosocial ends. This is one of the more sophisticated transformations in the file.

#### 6.2.6 Undoing

Smaller, less remarked: the tendency, after a sharp remark or a flash of anger, to immediately deliver a joke or warmth that cancels the prior beat. Observable in her dialogue rhythm across writers — bite, then balm. The undoing is fast enough to be nearly invisible but consistent enough to be structural.

---

### 6.3 MATURE DEFENSES (High-Level)

#### 6.3.1 Sublimation

The strongest defense in her repertoire and the one most responsible for her continued function. Aggression channels into legal advocacy and superheroics; exhibitionism channels into the She-Hulk performance and the meta-fictional address; the wish to be seen channels into the courtroom and the public-facing hero role. Each of these is a culturally valuable activity that perfectly metabolizes a drive that, in a less integrated subject, would be socially destructive.

The volume of prosocial work she has produced — superhuman law as a sub-discipline she effectively built, decades of Avengers/FF service, mentorship of younger heroes, the bar association work — is the externalized record of sublimation operating at industrial scale.

#### 6.3.2 Humor

Not affect-avoidance humor (that would be classed lower); genuine humor in the Vaillantian sense — the capacity to acknowledge a painful truth and simultaneously hold it at a survivable angle. The fourth-wall breaking in the Byrne run is the canonical example: she is fully aware she is a fictional construct being looked at by an audience, and rather than dissociate or rage, she makes friends with the audience and renegotiates the terms. This is mature defense as art form.

*Operational features:*
- Self-directed first, others-directed second. The mockery starts at home, which neutralizes its capacity to wound others.
- Specific over general. Her humor is concrete, situational, observational; she does not deal in cynical generalities.
- Calibrated. She does not joke in the wrong rooms. The Tamaki run shows long stretches where she is simply not funny, because the situation does not admit of it, and she knows.

#### 6.3.3 Suppression (vs. Repression)

The mature cousin of repression. She can put a feeling down for now, with awareness that it is being put down and intention to return to it. The capacity is visible in her courtroom function — she can be in active grief and still try a case competently — and is part of why she rebuilt after the Tamaki collapse rather than disintegrating. She did not pretend the trauma was not there; she scheduled it.

#### 6.3.4 Altruism

Distinct from sublimation. The mentorship pattern — taking younger heroes seriously, advocating for junior associates, the pro bono work she does for superhumans who cannot pay — is altruism in the technical sense: gratifying her own needs (to be the adult she did not have, to provide the mirroring she did not receive) through service to others, with the gratification fully available to consciousness and not denied.

#### 6.3.5 Anticipation

Less remarked but present. Her response to the Tamaki collapse, once stabilized, included deliberate construction of preventive structures — therapy schedule, exercise schedule, social check-ins, the rebuilt practice with sustainable hours. She learned from the breakdown and built scaffolding against the next one. The current Rowell-era equilibrium is anticipatory work made habit.

---

### 6.4 POSITIVE COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

These are not defenses against affect but constructive structures she has built to compensate for the original deficits. They are what makes her a functioning adult rather than merely a defended one.

**The Vocation.** Law as identity, epistemology, community, and daily structure. The practice gives her a place to be competent on contact, a peer group of similarly trained minds, a daily ritual of intellectual challenge, and a moral frame for action. It is the single most stabilizing structure in her life.

**Chosen Family.** Louise Mason, Patsy Walker, the GLK&H colleagues, the Avengers and FF rosters that have functioned as substitute kin. The friend-keeping is durable across decades and is the actual relational achievement of her life — what she could not do romantically she did in friendship. The friendships are real, reciprocal, and have survived her worst periods.

**The Heroic Identity.** Not the performance but the substantive prosocial commitment. Being someone whose body and skills are at the disposal of strangers in danger. This compensates for the early experience of being a small person to whom bad things happened by making her the large person to whom others can come.

**Mentorship.** Providing to younger figures what was not provided to her. Each mentee is a small repair of the original deficit, conducted with full awareness.

**Therapy (post-2016).** The acquisition of an explicit, on-page therapeutic relationship is the most important addition to her compensatory architecture in twenty years. It provides what no defense can: a place to actually FEEL the affect rather than route around it.

**Physical Practice.** The training, the workouts, the maintained body. Both forms require upkeep; the upkeep itself is regulatory.

---

### 6.5 NEGATIVE COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

These are the costs. They are real, persistent, and operationally relevant.

**Sexualization-as-Control.** Preempting being-looked-at by authoring the looking. Functional short-term, expensive long-term, because it requires her to keep performing a self that is partly armor. The Starfox arc is what happens when the armor is mistaken (by another) for an invitation, and the violation lands on territory she had been using defensively, with no fallback structure underneath.

**Serial Romantic Exits.** Each exit is locally rational and globally pathological. The aggregate pattern is the avoidance of the conditions under which the maternal-loss/paternal-rejection complex would have to be metabolized inside a sustained intimate bond.

**Episodic Alcohol Use (mid-2000s).** Affect regulation by chemical means, social-disinhibition vector. Not biochemical dependency (gamma metabolism), but a behavioral pattern of using intoxication to grant herself permission for desire and to mute self-monitoring. Reduced significantly post-Tamaki.

**The Long Avoidance of the Human Form.** For thirty years she preferred the form that did not require her to feel like the person she actually was. This is the most expensive compensation she has run, because the price was an unintegrated self that, when finally forced into the room by trauma, was unmetabolized adolescent material in an adult woman's life.

**Over-functioning Under Stress.** Her stress response is to do more work, faster, with more visible competence. Locally adaptive (she gets the case won, the crisis managed); long-term, it teaches the people around her that she does not need help, and they stop offering it, which compounds isolation precisely when isolation is most dangerous.

**Geographic / Social Avoidance of the Father.** The energetic maintenance of distance from a man she has not seen in years is a continuous low-grade tax on the system. The unresolved wound continues to organize behavior in ways she would prefer to deny.

---

### 6.6 SYNTHESIS

The defensive architecture is **unusually layered**: she has functional structures at every level from primitive (splitting) to mature (sublimation, humor, anticipation). This range is what produced both her remarkable resilience and her vulnerability to a specific kind of collapse — the kind where the mid-tier defenses (intellectualization, reaction formation) cannot reach the injury and the primitive ones (splitting, somatization) are forcibly disrupted at the same time. Civil War II hit her in exactly that combination, which is why the collapse was as deep as it was.

What distinguishes her from less integrated subjects in the file is **the documented capacity to add new defenses to the repertoire in adulthood**. The therapy work, the anticipation behaviors, the slow integration of the human form into a continuous self — these are post-trauma acquisitions, not pre-trauma equipment. She is, at the time of latest reporting, running a defensive system that is more sophisticated than the one she had at the beginning of the file, having paid the tuition to upgrade it.

This is the operational finding: she is not a defended subject who has avoided injury. She is an injured subject who has built, rebuilt, and is still building. The work is in progress and the trajectory is upward.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE: WALTERS, J.S.

## Preamble — Methodological Note

What follows is a decade-by-decade psychological reconstruction of the subject, organized along three orthogonal axes — **affect regulation**, **cognitive style**, and **self-concept** — with secondary attention to defenses, attachment behavior, and somatic-psychological integration where these illuminate the primary axes. The reconstruction draws on observable behavioral data (canonical record, 1980–present), inferred internal events (where behavior is overdetermined and unambiguous), and the cross-referencing of stated affect against demonstrated affect. The frameworks used are conventional: Bowlby/Main attachment categories, Vaillant's defense hierarchy, Linehan's biosocial model for affect dysregulation, Beck's schema theory for self-concept, Herman's three-stage trauma model for the post-2016 material, and Bromberg's "standing in the spaces" formulation for the bi-form somatic problem. None of these are imposed; each is invoked where the behavioral record forces it.

The subject's developmental anomaly — that her body changed in her mid-twenties in a way that altered the affordances of her self-presentation — means standard developmental staging must be read through a bifurcated lens. Each decade reviewed has, in effect, two psychological organisms to track: the pre-existing Jennifer-schema (intact, continuous, largely unrevised by the gamma event) and the gamma-form Jennifer-schema (constructed, elaborated, and at various points dominant, recessive, repudiated, or reintegrated). The interaction between these two schemas is the through-line of the entire file.

---

## Childhood and Late Adolescence (pre-1980, reconstructed)

The childhood material is sparse in the canonical record but every reference is consistent and the pattern is unmistakable.

**Affect regulation in this period was externalized to a single absent object and a single rejecting one.** The mother died in a vehicular accident in which the child was a passenger. The father — Sheriff Walters, a man whose professional identity (law enforcement) collapses the distinction between authority and approval — communicated, in the period after the accident, that the surviving daughter was implicated. Whether this was ever stated in those words or only transmitted in micro-affect is irrelevant to the developmental outcome. A child of approximately latency age who survives the event that takes her primary attachment object, and whose remaining attachment object is grieving and accusatory, has no available regulation strategy except foreclosure. Affect is not modulated; it is shut down at the source. The behavioral residue is visible decades later in the adult subject's pattern of **going from zero to crisis without intermediate registration** — she will operate at apparent baseline and then, on a sufficient stimulus, transform. The transformation is, among other things, the somatic literalization of a regulation strategy that skips the middle frequencies.

**Cognitive style consolidated early and consolidated hard.** The bookish, stammering, socially marginal child described in flashback panels (and referenced in the subject's own adult voice-over across multiple runs) made the standard intelligent-shy-girl bargain: if affect cannot be trusted, *language* — particularly structured, rule-bound, adversarial language — can be. The decision to enter law was not, on the evidence, a vocational discovery in late adolescence; it was a temperamental destiny that the subject narrated to herself probably from middle school onward. By the time she sits for the LSAT she is already cognitively a lawyer: she thinks in cases, in counterfactuals, in burden-of-proof. This style is set before the transformation and persists unchanged across every subsequent decade. It is the most stable thing about her.

**Self-concept in childhood was organized around two cores: smallness and culpability.** "Small" is not only physical but social — unseen, overlookable, the kind of child teachers like and peers ignore. "Culpable" is the residue of the accident: a low-grade, pre-verbal sense that her existence is in some way unearned, that she was the one who should not have walked out of the wreck. This is not articulated guilt; it is a substrate. Later, as an adult, she will be unusually drawn to defense work — to the structural position of the person standing beside the accused. The schema fit is not coincidental.

The cousin Bruce, encountered in summer visits, is the single non-pathogenic figure in the developmental field. He is intelligent, gentle, attentive, and — crucially — also marginal in his own family system. He is a mirror who reflects back something other than smallness or culpability. The intensity of her later grief for him is unintelligible without this datum.

---

## 1980–1989: The Acquisition Decade

**Affect regulation in the first post-transformation years is dichotomized along the form axis and is, on the surface, dramatically improved.** In the human form she remains brittle, easily overwhelmed, prone to the foreclosure pattern of childhood; in the gamma form she experiences something she has never had before, which is **affective spaciousness** — the felt sense that her body is large enough to contain her feelings. Early issues (Savage She-Hulk, 1980–82) treat the transformation as involuntary and stress-triggered, but the behavioral record undermines the framing: she does not flee the form, does not seek to suppress it pharmacologically, does not consult Banner for a cure. She investigates her enemies in it, sleeps adjacent to it, comes to expect it. The "involuntary" framing is largely the author's gesture toward Banner-parallel; the subject's actual behavior is that of a person who has discovered a regulation strategy and is testing its bounds.

By mid-decade (Avengers, 1982 onward; FF, 1984–85), she achieves and elects permanent transformation. The election is the decade's pivotal psychological event. It is the first time she chooses her own body, and the choice is for the version that regulates. The Vaillant defense most active here is **sublimation**: aggression that had no permitted outlet in the small-bookish-girl schema is now channeled into superheroics and adversarial law, both socially sanctioned, both prosocial, both reliably efficacious. This is high-functioning psychological work and should be recognized as such — many subjects in her position (acquired enhanced capacity, trauma history) regress to grandiosity or to vigilantism; she does neither.

**Cognitive style in this decade refines but does not change.** She is now an attorney in practice (initially LA, then increasingly East Coast as she follows the team affiliations); she develops the courtroom voice that will persist for forty years — fast, witty, structurally rigorous, fond of analogical reasoning, comfortable with the rhetorical inversion. What is new is the development of a **tactical cognition** to complement the legal one: combat under team conditions requires real-time multi-agent modeling, and she takes to it readily. The Avengers/FF tenures function as graduate school for this capacity. Cognition is, throughout the decade, ego-syntonic; she likes thinking and she likes that she is good at it.

**Self-concept in this decade undergoes the most rapid restructuring it will ever experience, but the restructuring is partial and the architecture matters.** She constructs, over roughly five years, a confident, sexually present, socially fluent self organized around the gamma form. This new self is not false — the warmth, the wit, the generosity, the courage are all real — but it is *built on top of* the childhood schema rather than integrated with it. The small-culpable-unseen schema is not revised; it is **occluded**. The gamma form provides such a sufficient daily experience of being-seen that the underlying schema is rarely activated. When it is activated — usually by father-contact or by isolated moments in the human form — it produces affect disproportionate to the stimulus, and she has no good account of why. She has not, in this decade, done the work of revising the substrate; she has built a beautiful structure over it and hopes the foundations will hold.

Attachment behavior in the relational domain (Zapper, Ridge, brief Wyatt Wingfoot entanglements) shows the pattern that will persist: rapid initial intimacy, high warmth, engagement at the level of activity and shared world, and then exit at the threshold where dependency would be tested. She is not yet aware that this is a pattern; she experiences each exit as situational.

---

## 1989–1994: The Sensational Inflection

The Byrne run (Sensational She-Hulk, 1989–94) is psychologically the most diagnostic period of the first half of her career, because the meta-fictional device — direct address, fourth-wall manipulation, awareness of the page — is **the externalization of a defense she has been running internally for years**. To know oneself as watched, and to preempt the watching by becoming the narrator of it, is a sophisticated self-protective maneuver with a precise developmental origin: the child who cannot trust the gaze of the parent learns, if she is clever, to *manage* the gaze rather than receive it.

**Affect regulation in this period acquires a new register: ironic distance.** Humor — Vaillantian mature defense — is now load-bearing. She can name her situation, mock the framing, deflate the sexualization by performing it knowingly. This is genuine coping resource and it works. What it costs is that affect must be **routed through wit before it can be experienced**; raw feeling without the irony-filter becomes increasingly hard to access, and the few panels in which Byrne lets her be tired or quiet or hurt have the quality of breakthrough. The brittleness in the human form, no longer a daily problem because she lives in the gamma form, has become a brittleness around unmediated feeling generally.

**Cognitive style develops a self-observational layer.** She is now thinking about how she is being read, by readers and by the in-world watchers; this is a meta-cognition that, in healthy doses, supports self-awareness, and in less healthy doses, produces the **courtroom-in-the-head** rumination that will later become problematic. She has not crossed into rumination yet; the self-observation in this period is mostly playful.

**Self-concept stabilizes around the gamma-form pole and the integration project is shelved.** This is the period in which it is most accurate to say that the human form has become "the costume" and the gamma form has become "her." This formulation will be quoted back to her in later decades — sometimes by herself, sometimes by writers letting her interrogate it — and it will not entirely hold up. But for these five years it functions, and she is, on balance, happier than she has been or will be for some time.

---

## Mid-1990s to early 2000s: The Quiet Interval

This is a period of relative narrative inactivity for the subject, which the file reads as a plateau rather than a regression. The behavioral patterns established in the first decade hold: she practices law, she takes assignments with teams, she sustains friendships (Louise Mason is the durable relationship of this period and the next; Patsy Walker enters the long-term roster). There is no major restructuring. The principal psychological work of the period is, paradoxically, the *non-event* — the absence of crisis that would have forced revision. The substrate schema remains occluded; the gamma-form architecture continues to do daily regulation; the relational pattern continues to terminate engagements before the dependency threshold.

What can be inferred but not directly evidenced: the unrevised substrate is not inert. Across a sustained plateau it accretes — a slow build-up of unmetabolized material around the maternal-loss/paternal-rejection complex and around the un-grieved versions of the prior partners she exited. The 2004 detonation does not come from nowhere.

---

## 2004–2009: The Slott Decade — Architecture Under Stress

The Slott run is the period in which the structure built over the childhood substrate is first systematically pressure-tested. The pressure-tests come in four forms and the subject's responses to each are diagnostic.

**First pressure-test: the courtroom-form mandate.** She is required to appear in court in the human form because juries do not credit the gamma form as trustworthy. The reaction is severe and revealing: she experiences this as *humiliation*, specifically as a forced regression to the small-unseen-culpable schema. The schema, occluded for two decades, is reactivated by exactly the situation it was originally formed in — being made small in a setting where her authority depends on being seen. **Affect regulation in the human form is now demonstrably worse than it was in the 1980s**, because she has had two decades of practice not using it. The atrophy is real. She experiences the courtroom as ego-dystonic in a way that no other professional setting has ever been; the very vocation that was her epistemological home becomes the site of her most acute self-experience problem. The dissonance is not resolved; it is endured.

**Second pressure-test: the relational manifold.** Jameson (marriage and annulment), Wingfoot (revisited), Hercules, Juggernaut. Each of these is a partner who is, in some legible way, her physical equal — mitigating the vulnerability differential that ordinary partners pose. The pattern is **attachment-in-the-affordance-of-non-fragility**: she can be in the gamma form, can engage without modulation, can fight and fuck and joke without fear of breaking the other. What she cannot do, with any of them, is sustain past the threshold where her partner would see the human-form schema. The Jameson marriage is the most instructive — it is briefer than it should be, ends on grounds that on inspection are pretextual, and leaves her with a residue of confusion rather than grief. She does not yet have a vocabulary for the pattern.

**Third pressure-test: the Starfox affair.** A documented violation of consent via the pheromonal/chemical modulation associated with that partner's powers. The subject's response is characteristic and important: she **prosecutes**. She metabolizes the personal injury through the professional frame; she names the violation in juridical terms; she pursues remedy. This is the file's clearest example of intellectualization functioning *adaptively* — not as evasion of feeling but as a container for feeling that would otherwise be ungovernable. The cost is also legible: the affective processing is incomplete. She has filed the case; she has not fully felt the injury. The residue is visible in her sexual behavior in the following years, which acquires a hypervigilant quality not present before.

**Fourth pressure-test: the power-stripping by the Fantastic Four.** She is briefly forcibly returned to the human form. This is, in psychological terms, an experimentally controlled reactivation of the original substrate, and the subject does not handle it well. The behavior — anger, refusal, urgency to reverse — is read in-narrative as resistance to a punishment; it is more accurately read as a panic response to forcible deprivation of her regulation strategy. A subject who has outsourced affect regulation to a body and then has that body taken away experiences, predictably, decompensation.

**Affect regulation across this decade, then, looks like this:** in the gamma form, still excellent baseline, but increasingly subject to acute spikes when the human-form schema is forcibly activated. In the human form, severely impaired and getting worse. **A bridging strategy emerges: alcohol.** The drinking of this period has been read as party-girl performance, and the performance is real, but the function is regulation. Intoxication is being used to (a) lower the threshold at which she can access desire in the gamma form without the new hypervigilance, and (b) blur the dissonance between gamma-confidence and the now-reactivated substrate. The behavior pattern is, as the medical file notes, not addiction biology; it is **affect-regulatory use**, which is its own clinical entity and is the typology of substance use most predictive of future relapse under trauma load. (This prediction is borne out in 2016.)

**Cognitive style in this decade becomes the most elaborated it will ever be.** Superhuman law is a niche she essentially creates, and the cognition required is novel: she is fusing common-law analogical reasoning with the metaphysics of superhuman capacity, working out doctrine in real time. This is genuine intellectual achievement and the file should mark it as such. Where the cognition becomes problematic is in its colonization of internal life — the courtroom-in-the-head, now mature, runs nearly continuously. She argues for and against her own choices, briefs her own behavior, holds herself to evidentiary standards that no internal life can meet. **Rumination is now a daily feature.**

**Self-concept by the end of the decade is more fragile than it has been since the early 1980s**, but in a complicated way: the gamma-form self is more elaborated and more publicly successful than ever (full partnership, public profile, romantic notoriety), and simultaneously the substrate is more activated than it has been in twenty years. The structure has not fallen, but it is now visibly creaking, and the subject has begun — in private moments the writers occasionally permit — to wonder about it. The Civil War alignment (registration, prosecution of Captain America) is, in this context, not principally a political position but a *retreat into the highest-order legal frame she has access to* under affective destabilization. When the substrate is loud, the law is the room she goes to.

---

## 2007: World War Hulk — Pre-trauma to the Coming Trauma

The Bruce-as-enemy episode of 2007 deserves its own paragraph because of what it sets up. The cousin who is the single non-pathogenic figure in her developmental field arrives in rage, attacks the city, and is fought by her — and defeats her. Two things happen psychologically. First, the **ego-ideal collapses**: the gentle, brilliant, kind cousin is now the monster. The lifelong identification with him as the integrated gamma case must be revised; if Bruce can lose to it, so can she. Second, the cousin who saw her clearly is no longer reliably available as a mirroring object — even when restored in subsequent issues, the relationship is shadowed. The grief that will arrive in 2016 is partly the grief of this earlier loss, deferred.

---

## 2014–2016: Soule Interval — A Brief Equilibrium

The Soule run is a period of relative re-equilibration. She leaves the large firm, opens her own practice, works smaller cases, dates less destructively. **Affect regulation improves** modestly because the structural stressors of the Slott decade — the courtroom-form mandate, the high-pressure firm — are off. **Cognitive style** simplifies somewhat; she is doing more direct work and less doctrine-fusing. **Self-concept** is in a calmer place, with the substrate quieter than it has been in years. The drinking attenuates. This period reads, in retrospect, as the calm before — and it is important to register that she had built herself a sustainable mid-life equilibrium that the 2016 event then destroyed.

---

## 2016–2018: The Tamaki Period — Trauma and Reconstruction

The Civil War II event is the most psychologically significant moment in the subject's adult life and the file's clinical analysis is best organized through Herman's three-stage model: **safety, remembrance and mourning, reconnection**.

The acute event: critical injury, cardiac arrest, resuscitation, and — proximate in time and causally entangled — the death of Bruce at allied hands. The combination is etiologically maximal. She has experienced her own near-death and the death of the single fully-mirroring object in her life, in the same window, and the killing was perpetrated by someone within her in-group. There is no clean attribution of rage available; there is no closure ritual available; the body in which she would normally process is itself implicated, because it is the *gamma* body, and the gamma body is now what killed her cousin's body.

**Affect regulation in this period is globally and catastrophically impaired.** The gamma form, for thirty years her regulation strategy, is now affectively contaminated: transformation is experienced as intrusive and dystonic, and when it occurs it produces the gray, rage-driven, Banner-Hulk-coded variant that frightens her. This is not a metabolic change in the gamma physiology; this is a *psychological* change in what the transformation now means. The form she chose, that was her agency, has become the form she fears. **The bifurcation she managed for thirty years by integrating around the gamma pole has been forcibly inverted**; the human form is now the safer one, and the human form was never the one she developed regulation skill in. She has, in effect, neither a working regulation strategy nor a body she trusts.

Behaviorally: isolation in the apartment, micromanagement of routine to avoid affect, avoidance of Avengers contacts, avoidance of practice, panic episodes in safe contexts, sleep disturbance, hypervigilance, intrusive recollections. Full PTSD criteria, as the psychiatric module documents.

**Cognitive style is dramatically narrowed.** The courtroom-in-the-head, formerly elaborated, becomes a single relentless interrogatory: did I cause this, could I have prevented it, what does it mean that I am alive. Rumination has become symptom. The analogical fluency is intact in flashes but cannot be sustained; she cannot brief her own life because there is no precedent to analogize to.

**Self-concept undergoes the first real revision since the 1980s.** The gamma-form self is no longer reliably available as the organizing pole; the human-form substrate is loud, but the substrate is also no longer adequate to who she has become as an adult — she is not the small-bookish-girl, she is forty years a lawyer and a hero with the small-bookish-girl underneath. Neither pole holds. **For the first time in her adult life she has to construct a self that is neither**: a self that can hold both the gamma capacity and the gamma fear, both the adult competence and the substrate vulnerability, both the survival and the survivor's guilt. This is the developmental work she outsourced to her body for thirty years, now mandatory.

The work proceeds, on-page, through **explicit therapy**. The file should emphasize this: she goes to a clinician, she does the talking, she shows up across episodes. Exposure work — re-entering the practice in small steps, re-establishing one friendship at a time, allowing limited transformation under controlled conditions — is the visible curriculum. Linehan's biosocial framing applies: she is learning, for the first time, *skills* for affect regulation that she previously got for free from the form. Distress tolerance, opposite action, the practice of staying in a feeling rather than transforming out of it.

By the end of the Tamaki run she is not recovered in any restorative sense; she is **reconstituted**. The substrate schema is, for the first time, partly revised: the small-culpable-unseen child has been seen by a competent clinician and by the witnesses of her own friendship network, and the substrate has updated to that degree. The gamma form is partly reintegrated: she can occupy it, with care, in defined contexts. The bifurcation persists but is held differently — she now stands, in Bromberg's phrase, *in the spaces* between the forms rather than colonizing one pole.

---

## 2022–present: The Rowell Equilibrium

The Rowell run depicts a mid-30s subject who has done the trauma work and is now learning to live with its residue. This is the most clinically realistic depiction in the run because it does not restore the 1989 confidence.

**Affect regulation in this period operates on a new model.** She has skills now where before she had a body. The skills are less effortless than the body was, but they are more durable and they survive transformation between forms. The gamma form is reintegrated as a *tool* rather than a *home*; she uses it, lives in it for periods, but does not exclusively identify with it. The human form, for the first time in her adult life, is also a place she can live — not without discomfort, but without the dysphoric urgency of the Slott period.

**Cognitive style has recovered fluency.** The courtroom rumination, while not absent, is now self-monitored; she catches it. The professional cognition is back online; the practice is functional. The analogical reasoning returns. What is new is a willingness to *not know* — to leave questions open, to tolerate ambiguity in her own internal life that the lawyer of 2006 could not have tolerated. This is real growth.

**Self-concept has integrated to the degree it can.** The


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# UATU DOSSIER — WALTERS, JENNIFER SUSAN
## Section 7: Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

> *Caveat operandi:* This section applies terrestrial diagnostic frameworks (DSM-5-TR and ICD-11 analogs) to a subject whose neuroendocrine substrate has been irrevocably altered by gamma transduction. Several criteria sets are stretched by the subject's biology — most notably substance-use thresholds, somatic anxiety symptoms (her transformed cardiovascular and endocrine baselines are non-standard), and the entire question of "dissociative" presentation in a person who literally inhabits two bodies. The framework is used here as the best available common language, not as ground truth. Where gamma physiology complicates a criterion, this is flagged.

---

### 7.1 Longitudinal Diagnostic Course — A Periodization

The subject's psychiatric history divides cleanly into four eras, each with a distinct diagnostic signature. The file organizes the assessment around this periodization rather than presenting a single static formulation, because the most important psychiatric fact about this subject is that **her diagnostic picture is not stable across her life and the changes are themselves diagnostic**.

#### Era I — Pre-Index (childhood through approximately age 25)

**Working impression:** Subclinical persistent depressive features; social anxiety, situational rather than generalized; no Axis I disorder meeting threshold.

The childhood record (maternal death at approximately age 6–7; paternal blame in the immediate aftermath; subsequent decade in a household where affection was conditional on competence and silence) would, in a clinical intake, generate a high index of suspicion for childhood-onset dysthymia and adjustment disorder with depressed mood. The behavioral signature in adolescence — bookishness, social marginality, the stammer reported in some early biographical accounts, the avoidance of mirror and photograph, the absence of dating in high school — is consistent with depressive cognition about the self (low self-worth, anticipated rejection, anhedonic withdrawal from peer activity) layered with situational social anxiety.

What rules out a formal childhood depressive disorder at this remove is the **preservation of academic function and the trajectory toward law school and bar admission**. She did not collapse; she compensated. The compensation took the form that has defined her entire adult life: she became excellent at the one thing in the house that earned response from her father (academic achievement, articulated argument), and she let everything else atrophy. This is *premorbid personality formation under depressogenic conditions*, not depressive disorder. The distinction matters because it tells us what her baseline coping looked like before any of the later events: she copes by working, by reading, by arguing, by becoming the smartest person in the room. When those compensations fail (as they do in the Tamaki run), there is no underlayer of leisure-based or relational coping to fall back on — she has to build it from scratch in her late thirties.

#### Era II — Post-Transformation Adjustment (approximately the first two years post-incident)

**Working impression:** Adjustment disorder with mixed features (anxious, behaviorally disinhibited), in remission within 18–24 months; gamma-state hypomanic-flavored shift in self-schema accessibility, not a true hypomanic episode.

The early Savage She-Hulk record is, paradoxically, the period of her life with the *fewest* psychiatric symptoms in the human form and the most behavioral acting-out in the transformed form. Involuntary transformations triggered by anger or fear meet a literal Criterion B intrusion criterion for a stressor-response disorder, but the affective valence is wrong for a trauma diagnosis: she is not distressed by the transformations, she is *thrilled* by them. The pattern looks less like PTSD and more like an adjustment disorder in which the "adjustment" is happening in the direction of pleasure rather than distress.

The mood elevation in the transformed state during this era — increased goal-directed activity, decreased need for sleep, hypersexuality, grandiosity, pressured speech, reckless decision-making (the Trask pursuit) — would, in any other patient, prompt a hypomanic-versus-manic differential. It is not. The mood elevation is **state-dependent on physical form and on situational context**, not endogenous, not cyclic, not present in the human form, and not present in the transformed form when the situation does not call for it. She is not bipolar. She is a person whose self-schema is bifurcated and who has just discovered that one of the schemata feels much better to inhabit.

#### Era III — Mid-career equilibrium with intermittent decompensations (approximately the late 1980s through 2014)

**Working impression:** No threshold disorder for most of this period. Two discrete decompensation episodes meet partial criteria: (a) the mid-2000s episode of alcohol misuse and sexual acting-out, best characterized as *alcohol use disorder, mild to moderate, with the caveat that gamma metabolism distorts standard tolerance/withdrawal criteria*; and (b) the post-Starfox episode, which presents as *acute stress reaction with features of sexual trauma response*, resolved relatively rapidly through her characteristic legal-procedural metabolism of the injury.

The mid-2000s drinking is the diagnostically interesting one because of the biology. Standard alcohol use disorder relies on a tolerance/withdrawal/loss-of-control triad that assumes baseline human hepatic metabolism. Subject's gamma physiology almost certainly precludes true physiological dependence — she will not have withdrawal seizures, she likely cannot achieve sustained blood alcohol elevation without extraordinary doses, and her body will not develop the cellular adaptations that ground the physiological criteria. What she **does** have, behaviorally, is every one of the *psychological and social* criteria: drinking more and longer than intended, persistent desire to cut down, time spent in pursuit, important activities given up, continued use despite social/interpersonal problems, use in situations where it is physically hazardous, and craving. By DSM-5 criteria *applied behaviorally*, she meets threshold. By ICD-11 criteria, which weigh the behavioral pattern more centrally, she more clearly meets threshold. The clinical formulation is that **she used alcohol instrumentally as a permission structure for desire and disinhibition that she could not access sober in her human form and was ashamed of accessing sober in her gamma form**. This is functional/affect-regulatory use, not appetitive use. It remitted when the underlying dynamic was addressed (in part through the Slott-era arc of being stripped of her powers and forced to confront the dependency).

The Starfox episode warrants its own diagnostic note. Subject experienced retroactive recognition that her sexual choices had been influenced by another's pheromonal/empathic manipulation. The acute response — destabilization of her sense of sexual agency, intrusive re-evaluation of past encounters, channeled rage — would meet criteria for *acute stress disorder* in the first month if the symptoms had persisted. They did not, because she did what she always does: she filed. The legal action was not just instrumental justice-seeking; it was *the metabolic pathway by which she converted an injury to her sexual agency into an exercise of her professional agency*. Diagnostically this is adaptive defense use; the file flags it because the same mechanism, deployed against a less tractable injury (Bruce's death), would later fail.

#### Era IV — Post-Civil War II (the Tamaki run forward)

**Working impression:** Posttraumatic Stress Disorder, full criteria, severe, chronic, with delayed expression of some symptoms; comorbid Prolonged Grief Disorder (DSM-5-TR; ICD-11 6B42); comorbid Panic Disorder, with situationally predisposed attacks; no comorbid major depressive episode despite significant depressive symptomatology (the symptoms are better accounted for by the PTSD and grief diagnoses); secondary alcohol misuse not present in this era (an important negative finding — she did **not** return to the mid-2000s coping pattern, which is itself prognostically significant).

This is the diagnostic core of the file and the section requires expansion.

---

### 7.2 PTSD: Criterion-by-Criterion Substantiation

**Criterion A (Exposure to actual or threatened death, serious injury, or sexual violence):** Multiply satisfied. Direct exposure: critically wounded in the Thanos engagement, with documented cardiac arrest and resuscitation. Witnessing in proximity: aware in the same temporal window of Bruce's death at allied hands. Learning of violent death of close family member: same event. The Criterion A stressor is doubly indexed, both somatic and relational, which is prognostically worse than either alone.

**Criterion B (Intrusion symptoms):** All five sub-criteria documented at some point in the post-event record.
- B1 (intrusive memories): observed in the Tamaki run as unbidden recall of the Thanos engagement and of Bruce, triggered by ambient cues (medical settings, the color gray, the sound of arrows, archery imagery).
- B2 (nightmares): on-page reference; sleep disturbance is the most consistent vegetative symptom.
- B3 (dissociative reactions / flashbacks): this is where the subject's biology generates a unique symptom presentation. **The transformations themselves become flashback vehicles.** When she Hulks out in this era, she experiences the transformation as ego-dystonic, as something happening *to* her, with derealization and time distortion phenomenologically identical to a flashback — and the gamma form that emerges is no longer the green She-Hulk of her chosen self-image but a gray, rage-driven figure resembling Bruce's earliest gamma presentation. The transformation is doing the work of a flashback at the level of embodied re-experiencing: she is *becoming the moment of loss* somatically. This is a presentation textbook PTSD cannot quite categorize, and it is the most clinically distinctive feature of her post-trauma course.
- B4 (psychological distress at cues): pronounced. Avengers settings, hospital settings, contact with Hawkeye, mention of Bruce.
- B5 (physiological reactivity to cues): documented; the panic-attack literature applies.

**Criterion C (Avoidance):** Both sub-criteria.
- C1 (avoidance of internal reminders): she does not speak of Bruce for an extended period; she stops the transformation entirely for a period.
- C2 (avoidance of external reminders): geographic withdrawal to her apartment, declination of Avengers contact, suspended legal practice, refusal of media appearances.

**Criterion D (Negative alterations in cognition and mood):**
- D1: dissociative amnesia for portions of the Thanos engagement.
- D2: persistent exaggerated negative beliefs ("I am dangerous"; "I cannot be trusted with the form"; "everyone I love dies").
- D3: distorted cognitions about cause/consequence, particularly survivor-guilt cognitions about Bruce.
- D4: persistent negative emotional state (fear, anger, shame predominating; the shame is the most under-discussed and probably the most clinically significant).
- D5: markedly diminished interest in activities — the work, the friendships, the sex life.
- D6: detachment/estrangement — explicit on-page.
- D7: persistent inability to experience positive emotions — partial; she retains intermittent humor, which is prognostically excellent.

**Criterion E (Alterations in arousal and reactivity):**
- E1: irritable behavior and angry outbursts — the rage episodes in the Tamaki run.
- E2: reckless or self-destructive behavior — borderline; the willingness to engage adversaries without backup in this era reads as passive self-endangerment.
- E3: hypervigilance — environmental scanning, startle to door sounds.
- E4: exaggerated startle response — documented.
- E5: concentration problems — affects work product; she catches her own errors and self-flags.
- E6: sleep disturbance — chronic.

**Criterion F (Duration > 1 month):** Yes, by orders of magnitude.

**Criterion G (Functional impairment):** Severe across occupational, social, and intimate domains.

**Criterion H (Not attributable to substance or medical condition):** This is where the gamma biology complicates things. One could argue that her symptoms are a manifestation of altered gamma neuroendocrinology rather than psychological trauma. The file rejects this: the symptoms are stimulus-locked to trauma cues, respond to psychological intervention (she gets visibly better with therapy on-page), and have phenomenological structure (the embodied re-experiencing through transformation) that maps to the psychological architecture of the trauma rather than to any known gamma syndrome.

**Specifier:** "With delayed expression" partially applies — some symptoms (the shame cluster, the chronic avoidance of the green form's positive associations) consolidate over months rather than emerging acutely. **"With dissociative symptoms (depersonalization/derealization)"** clearly applies, in the very specific form described under B3 above.

---

### 7.3 Prolonged Grief Disorder

The Bruce loss meets criteria for what DSM-5-TR codes as Prolonged Grief Disorder and ICD-11 codes as 6B42, distinct from PTSD though comorbid. The diagnostic markers:

- Persistent yearning and preoccupation with the deceased extending well past the 12-month threshold (in the published record, the grief remains live years after the event).
- Identity disruption (she experienced his death as a loss of part of self — appropriately, since he was her gamma-mirror and the only family member who saw her without contempt).
- Marked sense of disbelief; difficulty with reintegration into relationships and activities; emotional numbness specific to the loss; intense loneliness; feeling that life is meaningless **in the specific register of having lost the only person who understood the central biological fact of her life**.

The grief is complicated by three factors that worsen prognosis: (a) the death was at allied hands, generating a fracturing of her institutional trust that she has not fully repaired; (b) survivor guilt (she flatlined and was resuscitated; he did not get the resuscitation); (c) the loss closed a developmental door — the future relationship with Bruce that she had implicitly assumed would be available is not.

She has metabolized this slowly and incompletely. The Rowell-era equilibrium is real but the grief is integrated rather than resolved. This is the correct outcome for losses of this magnitude; the file does not flag it as a treatment failure.

---

### 7.4 Panic Disorder, Secondary

Discrete panic episodes documented post-CWII, including in objectively safe contexts (her own apartment, low-stimulus environments). Criteria met: recurrent unexpected attacks (some are cue-triggered and properly belong to PTSD; a subset are uncued and properly support a panic diagnosis); persistent concern about additional attacks; behavioral changes related to attacks (avoidance of locations where attacks have occurred). The panic diagnosis is partially absorbable into the PTSD diagnosis but is broken out because (a) some attacks are uncued, (b) the anticipatory anxiety functions independently, and (c) the panic phenomenology in her case has a distinctive somatic signature: she experiences initial panic in her **human form** as a precursor to involuntary transformation, which compounds the panic with anticipatory dread of losing control. This is a feedback loop unique to her biology and clinically important: standard panic psychoeducation ("the symptoms are not dangerous") is technically false for her, because her panic *can* trigger a 700-pound transformation.

---

### 7.5 What She Is NOT — Rigorous Differential

The most common diagnostic errors a non-specialist would make with this subject, and why each is wrong.

**Not Dissociative Identity Disorder.** This is the single most important differential and the one a naive observer reaches for first because of the two-body presentation. It is wrong on every criterion.
- *No alter.* Dissociative Identity Disorder requires two or more distinct personality states with their own patterns of perceiving, relating, and thinking about self and environment. She has one self across both forms. The mood shifts, the disinhibition shifts, the embodied confidence shifts — but the *cognitive structure, value system, autobiographical narrative, vocabulary, humor, political commitments, professional knowledge, and relational stances* are continuous.
- *No amnestic barrier.* DID requires recurrent gaps in recall inconsistent with ordinary forgetting. She has full memory across forms. (The Civil War II era amnesia is trauma-related and form-independent.)
- *No internal experience of separateness.* She does not experience She-Hulk as another person. She experiences She-Hulk as *herself, more so*.
- *The bifurcation is at the level of self-schema, not identity.* She holds two organized self-representations — "small, unseen me" and "large, seen me" — and switches between them in a manner that is structurally identical to ordinary state-dependent self-concept variation, just amplified by a literal somatic correlate.
- *Diagnostic contrast with Banner.* Her cousin's gamma response *does* present with dissociative architecture (the Hulk is an alter, with separate memory, separate language, separate relational stance). She does not. Same biology, opposite psychological outcome. The comparison clarifies the diagnosis: gamma transformation does not cause dissociation; trauma-shaped premorbid personality determines whether dissociation will be the response.

**Not Bipolar I, Bipolar II, or Cyclothymia.** No endogenous mood cycling. Mood shifts are state- and situation-dependent, not periodic. No discrete manic or hypomanic episodes of the required duration unlinked to transformation or situational stressor. The transformed-state elevation is not autonomous — it remits when the situation does. No depressive episodes meeting major depressive episode criteria in the absence of identifiable stressor. The "She-Hulk is happier" phenomenon is *self-schema accessibility variance*, not a mood disorder.

**Not Narcissistic Personality Disorder.** Surface presentation (large physical presence, confidence, sexual self-display, public role) misleads. NPD requires grandiose self-importance, fantasies of unlimited success/power/etc., belief in being special and unique, requirement for excessive admiration, sense of entitlement, interpersonal exploitativeness, lack of empathy, envy, arrogance. She demonstrates none of these characterologically. She empathizes broadly (this is the prosocial spine of her legal practice). She takes losses seriously and grieves proportionately. She is capable of shame — extensively documented, and a near-perfect rule-out for NPD, where shame is the affect that cannot be tolerated and must be projected outward. Her confidence is *competence-based and form-based*, not fantasy-based. Her sexuality is exhibitionistic but the cognitive frame around it is awareness of being looked at, not entitlement to being adored. The exhibitionism is compensatory and self-aware. NPD is ruled out conclusively.

**Not Histrionic Personality Disorder.** Surface resemblance in some Sensational-era behavior (theatricality, fourth-wall awareness, sexualized self-presentation, attention-seeking) is real but does not extend to the cognitive substrate. HPD presents with impressionistic, vague, easily-influenced cognition; her cognition is rigorously organized, analytical, and sustained over years of complex case work. HPD presents with shallow, rapidly-shifting affect; her affect is deep and durable (forty years of grief over her mother; sustained grief over Bruce). HPD presents with consideration of relationships as more intimate than they are; she has a calibrated and accurate read on her relationships, sometimes uncomfortably so.

**Not Borderline Personality Disorder.** The serial intense relationships pattern raises the question. Ruled out on every other criterion: stable rather than oscillating identity, no recurrent suicidal behavior or self-harm, no chronic emptiness, no inappropriate intense anger as a characterological baseline (the post-CWII rage is trauma-bound, not characterological), no stress-related paranoid ideation, no frantic efforts to avoid abandonment (she is the one who exits). The relational pattern is *avoidant*, not borderline; she ends relationships at the threshold of dependency rather than escalating to crisis to prevent abandonment. The two patterns can look superficially similar in the cycle of intense engagement and rupture but the motivational structure is opposite.

**Not Avoidant Personality Disorder, though avoidant *traits* are present.** APD requires pervasive social inhibition across domains. She has high social function in professional and superhuman-community settings; the avoidance is specifically activated in the intimacy domain and in human-form vulnerability contexts. Trait-level, not disorder-level.

**Not Obsessive-Compulsive Personality Disorder.** Perfectionist work product is real but is not pervasive; she can leave a brief unfinished to go to a bar, she can take vacations, she can tolerate imperfection in others, she is not rigid about morality beyond ordinary professional ethics, she is not miserly, she is not a hoarder. Trait-level work perfectionism, not disorder.

**Not Substance Use Disorder, current.** The mid-2000s episode was time-limited and remitted. No evidence of return.

**Not Adjustment Disorder, current.** Post-CWII presentation exceeds adjustment-disorder threshold by every measure of severity and duration; the correct diagnoses are the trauma and grief diagnoses, not adjustment.

**Not a Psychotic Disorder.** Despite living in a world where her ordinary experience would constitute psychosis in any other context (she becomes a different-sized green person; she breaks the fourth wall and addresses an audience that ordinary people cannot perceive), reality-testing within her ontological frame is intact. The fourth-wall awareness, treated diagnostically, is interesting: in our frame it is a delusion; in her canonical frame it is veridical perception of a real feature of her universe. The file treats it as veridical and notes only that her *relationship* to that perception (using it for humor, control of self-presentation, occasional manipulation of her own narrative) is itself a defense structure, not a symptom.

**Not Somatic Symptom Disorder.** Her somatic experiences are real biological events.

**Not Factitious Disorder, not Malingering.** Self-evident.

---

### 7.6 Etiological Formulation

The etiology runs in three layers, each necessary, none sufficient alone.

**Developmental layer:** Early maternal loss with paternal blame produced a child organized around (a) the conviction that visibility is dangerous (her visibility in the car preceded her mother's death; her father's gaze became the gaze of accusation), (b) the compensatory strategy of mastery-through-articulation, and (c) an attachment template in which closeness is conditional and revocable. This is the substrate.

**Biological layer:** The gamma incident provided a somatic vehicle for the unmet developmental needs. The transformed body is large (the small girl, supersized), seen (the unseen girl, unmissable), strong (the helpless girl, invulnerable), and desirable (the unloved girl, wanted). The transformation did not create new psychological structures; it provided a *physical answer to existing psychological questions*. This is why she embraced it and her cousin did not — his psychological questions had different answers.

**Traumatic layer:** Civil War II inflicted a wound calibrated to defeat her existing coping. It threatened her body (which had been her solution), killed the person who had been her witness


## Behavioral Atlas

# UATU DOSSIER — WALTERS, JENNIFER SUSAN
## SECTION: BEHAVIORAL ATLAS

A surveillance-grade catalog of observable conduct across forty-plus years of recorded life. Items are organized by state. Each entry pairs the *tell* (what an observer logs) with the *substrate* (what it indexes). Cross-references are to the patterns established in §3–§5 of the master file.

---

### I. BASELINE / CALM STATE

Calm, for the subject, is operationally defined as: caseload manageable, no live trauma anniversary, no contact with the father within seventy-two hours, full sleep cycle, transformed form available on demand and recently used at least once in the prior 48 hours. Under these conditions the following patterns are reliable.

**Postural and somatic baseline (human form).** Sits forward in chair, elbows out, occupying more lateral space than her shoulder breadth requires — a learned compensation for years of being the smallest person at the table. Walks with a slightly long stride for her hip-width; foot strike is heel-first and audible on hard floors. When standing in conversation she squares her shoulders to the speaker rather than angling, a courtroom habit. Hands rarely fall to her sides at rest; they find a pen, a coffee cup, a phone, a hair tuck, a hem-smooth, a lapel-adjust. Idle hand activity is high. She is almost never still.

**Postural and somatic baseline (transformed form).** Stride shortens, weight settles back into the hips, she takes up exactly the space she occupies and no more — a reversal of the human-form compensation, because the body now answers the room. She leans, she lounges, she perches on desks and counters. She crosses her legs at the knee where space allows it and at the ankle where it doesn't, a deliberate softening of a silhouette that reads as threatening when uncomposed. Hand activity drops markedly. The need to fidget evaporates when the body itself feels sufficient.

**Eye behavior.** Long direct gaze, four to six seconds before a break, then return. Breaks down and to the left when she is calculating, up and to the right when she is constructing language. Blink rate is slightly suppressed in conversation — a cross-examiner's training overlaid on a temperamental willingness to be looked at. She tracks hands, not faces, when assessing whether a stranger is dangerous.

**Speech in calm.** Mid-fast cadence, full sentences, parenthetical asides she signals with a slight tonal drop and recovers from cleanly. Latinate vocabulary in professional contexts, Anglo-Saxon vocabulary in social ones, and she will code-switch within a single conversation depending on whom she's addressing. Laugh is loud, head-back, unembarrassed — and noticeably louder in transformed form than in human form, where it sometimes ducks behind a hand. The childhood stammer is gone from the surface but reappears as a one-beat hesitation before consonant-initial words when she is tired or has just spoken with her father.

**Daily rituals.** Coffee black, second cup with milk. Reads three to four legal feeds and one general-news source before opening email; will not check email before this sequence. Runs in the early morning when in routine — six to eight miles, paced conservatively in human form because she can, not because she must. Cooks rarely; orders consistently from a small rotation of three or four places per neighborhood and tips in cash. Reads fiction at night, paper not screen — a deliberate sleep-hygiene practice she adopted after the Tamaki-era insomnia.

**Wardrobe logic.** Tailored, structured, jewel-toned in professional settings; she dresses for shoulders and waist rather than for legs. Avoids prints that fragment under photography (she is photographed often). Keeps a duplicate of every key outfit in transformed-form size, packed and ready — a logistical tell with a psychological signature: she will not be caught unable to be either self.

**Phone behavior.** Picks up on the second ring for known contacts, lets unknown numbers go to voicemail and reviews transcripts in batches. Texts in full sentences with terminal punctuation. Does not use voice notes; finds them imprecise. Email signature in human-form practice is shorter than in transformed-form practice — a small inconsistency she has never noticed and would deny if shown.

**Money behavior.** Tracks billable hours obsessively; tracks personal spending poorly. Generous tipper, generous gifter, slow to invoice friends. Keeps emergency cash in three places: wallet, apartment, office. Carries a small physical notebook and a fountain pen; the notebook is not for notes, it is for the act of taking them, which calms her.

---

### II. MILD STRESS

Trigger conditions: opposing counsel of unusual competence, a complex motion under deadline, an Avengers call-up that interrupts trial prep, an unfamiliar social setting in human form, a new romantic interest in week two.

**Wit sharpens.** Latency to a joke drops from roughly two seconds to under one. Jokes acquire bite; targets become specific rather than situational. Self-deprecation rises — the calibrated kind, designed to lower the room's threat level by volunteering a flaw. This is functional and almost always lands.

**Work output increases.** She will out-prep, out-brief, out-research. The mild-stress version of the subject is the version her firm rate-cards on: hours go up, error rate goes down, and she becomes mildly intolerant of underperformance around her, signaled by a clipped *"mm-hm"* and a faster return to her own work.

**Caffeine intake rises.** A third cup appears. She will not eat lunch unless someone places food in front of her.

**Touch-points multiply.** Hair tucked behind the right ear, then the left, then the right again. Earring fidget (right ear, lower lobe; she favors small studs in part because hoops catch on this gesture). Ring on right hand turned with left thumb. None of these reach the threshold of visible distress; they are baseline-plus.

**Transformation cadence.** She will transform once during the workday for no operational reason — a coffee run, a walk around the block — and return. This is self-medication via embodiment and she knows it, post-Tamaki; pre-Tamaki she did it without insight.

---

### III. MODERATE STRESS

Trigger conditions: trial loss in progress, multi-front case collapse, a relationship reaching the four-to-six-month threshold where dependency would crystallize, a call from her father, media attention focused on the human-form self.

**Drinking appears.** Pattern is social-disinhibition: wine with dinner becomes wine instead of dinner; she gravitates to bars where she is known, where the bartender pours without asking, where the music is loud enough to occupy the part of her brain that is otherwise rehearsing arguments. Two-drink threshold is where the wit becomes flirtatious; four-drink threshold is where she leaves with someone or leaves alone with deliberate decisiveness. Gamma metabolism prevents the next-morning consequence, which is part of the problem: there is no somatic feedback to brake the behavior.

**Sexual acting-out.** Not promiscuous in the disorganized sense; sex under moderate stress is *chosen*, controlled, and frequently with partners she has slept with before — a known-quantity behavior, not a stranger-seeking one. The transformed form is almost always the form she chooses to be seen in for these encounters. This is preemption: she manages being-looked-at by selecting the body that has already won the look.

**Geographic micro-moves.** Re-arranges furniture, changes a commute route, picks up shifts at a different courthouse, takes a case out of state. The pattern is *displace the body, settle the mind*. Full apartment moves cluster around the worst of these periods.

**Relational exit signals.** She becomes harder to schedule. Texts get shorter. Plans get cancelled with credible but proliferating professional reasons. She will not initiate the breakup conversation; she will arrange conditions under which the partner does. This is the most consistent single behavior across forty years of her romantic record and the most reliable predictor she has crossed the moderate-stress threshold over an attachment.

**Father-contact aftermath.** Specific to paternal trigger: she drinks alone rather than socially that night, does not transform for 24–48 hours, and is sharply impatient with anyone who attempts care. The hand-fidget migrates to the left forearm, a self-soothe she does not perform in any other context.

---

### IV. HIGH STRESS / OVERLOAD

Trigger conditions: major case with public stakes, civil-emergency call-up, betrayal by a colleague or ally, professional standing under threat (bar complaint, sanctions, malpractice exposure).

**Retreat into the procedural frame.** Speech becomes more formal, sentence structure more parallel, vocabulary more Latinate. She will brief her own life: "the operative question is," "on the present facts," "assuming arguendo." Observers who don't know her read this as competence under pressure; observers who do read it as a flare.

**Over-functioning.** Sleep drops to four hours, work expands to fill the rest. She will take on additional matters in this state — not from grandiosity but because idle time is the threat. Delegates poorly under high stress; rewrites associates' work; apologizes for it later in calm.

**Humor becomes mordant.** The bite that emerges under mild stress turns dark. Death jokes, body jokes, gamma jokes — at her own expense, usually, and usually to disarm before someone else can deploy the same material against her. The fourth-wall instinct (the meta-awareness of being watched) intensifies in high stress; she becomes audibly aware of the rhetorical posture she is occupying and will name it. *"This is the part where I'm supposed to —"* is a tell.

**Eating becomes performative.** She eats in front of people but does not actually consume, pushes food, drinks more water than she registers. Alone, she does not eat.

**Form-switching frequency drops.** Counter-intuitively. Under high stress she picks a form and holds it for the duration of the crisis — usually transformed for operational stakes, human for purely legal ones — because the act of switching itself becomes effortful. The form is now a tool, not a refuge.

**Compulsive list-making.** The fountain pen and the small notebook come out. Lists of tasks, of arguments, of names of people to call. She does not consult the lists. The making is the regulation.

---

### V. ACUTE THREAT / COMBAT

Trigger conditions: physical danger to self or to a protectee, active superhuman engagement, hostage scenario, ambush.

**Pre-engagement.** Half-second pause. Eyes go to exits, then to civilians, then to threat — in that order, every time. Mouth often forms a word she does not say (an oath, a name, a procedural objection); she is briefing the situation to herself before she enters it.

**Transformation tell.** Pre-Tamaki: smooth, near-instantaneous, accompanied by a roll of the shoulders and a small exhale, almost relieved. Post-Tamaki: a visible flinch precedes it, a half-second of resistance she has had to learn to push through, and the exhale becomes a deliberate inhale-hold-release — a regulation technique acquired in therapy and now reflexive. The flinch has decreased in frequency since the Rowell-era stabilization but has not disappeared and probably never will.

**Combat style.** Strikes are economical, leverage-aware, lawyer-brained: she will use the opponent's mass against them rather than overpowering them outright when she has the option. Prefers throws, holds, structural displacements (walls, vehicles, terrain) to direct strikes. Does not punch faces unless the engagement has already escalated past de-escalation; her first instinct is *contain*, not *destroy*. This is unusual among her power-cohort and reads as the lawyer overlaying the gamma — she has internalized proportionality as a reflex.

**Verbal layer during combat.** She talks. To opponents (negotiation, taunt, Miranda-flavored warnings), to bystanders (instruction, reassurance), to herself (running commentary, a courtroom-in-the-head externalized under load). Silence in combat is the worst sign she gives — it indicates she has assessed the situation as past-verbal, which means she is about to do something she will be unhappy about later.

**Threat-assessment quirks.** Underestimates magical threats (she is a common-law thinker, and magic resists doctrinal organization). Overestimates threats associated with crowd dynamics and media presence — not the threat to her body but the threat to the after-narrative. She fights differently when she knows she is being filmed: cleaner, slower, more legible, with greater civilian-protection theater.

**Post-engagement.** Returns to human form before debriefing whenever feasible — a deliberate practice to demonstrate (to self and to observers) that the transformed self is a tool and not a refuge. Hands shake for roughly ninety seconds; she puts them in pockets or wraps them around a cup. Will not discuss the engagement substantively for two to four hours; will discuss logistics immediately.

---

### VI. INTIMACY

Trigger conditions: courtship, sexual encounter, the periods of attempted partnership, close friendship deepening past acquaintance.

**Opening behavior.** Fast, warm, witty, generous with attention. High eye contact, real laughter, real curiosity. She is, by every account in the record, exceptional company in the first two months of any relationship. This is not performance; it is genuine engagement that has not yet activated the avoidance schema.

**The four-month inflection.** Around weeks twelve to sixteen of any sustained romantic engagement, the following appear: a sudden professional crunch that consumes weekends, a renewed interest in heroic obligations, a re-emphasis on her own apartment as primary residence regardless of where time is actually spent, and a subtle but measurable increase in transformed-form preference around the partner — making the body harder to read as the small, unguarded self. The pattern is so consistent across partners (Wingfoot, Jameson, the Slott-era rotation, Jack of Hearts) that a sufficiently informed observer can calendar it.

**Bedroom behavior.** Confident, communicative, frequently in transformed form by partner request or her own choice. Will not be photographed. Will not stay over on a first encounter; will host but resist staying. The deliberate non-overnight is the cleanest tell of the avoidance pattern, because it sequesters intimacy to bounded time-blocks under her control.

**Friendship behavior.** Different architecture entirely. Friend-keeper across decades — long-haul commitments to Louise Mason, Patsy Walker, the GLK&H circle. Remembers birthdays, shows up for funerals, takes calls at 3 AM. The friendships are sustained precisely because the dependency stakes are lower; she can be loyally available because she is not being asked to be merged.

**Disclosure pattern.** Will discuss her father in deflective comedy with new partners, in flat factual terms with established friends, and almost never in genuine affect with anyone except (historically) Bruce. Will discuss her mother almost never with anyone, in any register. The Bruce-bond was load-bearing for this reason and the gap has not been filled.

**Sex after grief.** A specific pattern: in the weeks following any significant loss she becomes briefly hyper-sexual, then abruptly celibate. The sex is regulatory; the celibacy is the system overcorrecting once the regulation is recognized.

---

### VII. GRIEF

Trigger conditions: bereavement (Bruce; lesser figures), case loss with human cost, anniversary dates (mother's death, Bruce's death, Civil War II), client death.

**First 48 hours.** Functional. Logistical. She handles arrangements, calls, paperwork, will draft eulogies and obituaries unprompted. Affect is flat to mildly elevated; she is sometimes inappropriately witty in this window, which she will later regret and over-apologize for.

**Days three through ten.** The arrangements end and the affect arrives. She isolates — apartment, lights low, phone on do-not-disturb except for a short whitelist. Does not transform. Eats poorly. Sleeps in clothes. Rewatches familiar films, rereads familiar books; she does not consume new material in grief, only known quantities. This is the most reliably documented pattern across the entire record and it is unchanged from her twenties to her late-published era.

**Weeks two through six.** Re-entry, with significant friction. She will return to work before she is ready and over-perform; she will accept social invitations and leave them early; she will pick a fight with someone safe (a friend, an associate, an Avenger she trusts to forgive her). The fight is the affect finding an exit.

**The Bruce-grief is its own category.** Different rules: she has had to seek explicit therapy for it; she will not joke about it; she will not discuss it with anyone except her therapist and, occasionally, in extremis, with another gamma-mutate. Anniversaries are observed privately — she takes the day off, transforms once, walks somewhere green, returns. The walk is a ritual and has been since the first anniversary.

**Maternal-loss anniversary.** She does not consciously mark it. She is reliably in a moderate-to-high-stress behavioral pattern in the week around the date — drinking, sexual acting-out, geographic micro-moves — and has been every year of the published record. She would deny the linkage if asked. The pattern is too consistent for chance.

**Survivor guilt presentation.** Subtle. Shows up as over-functioning for the deceased's surviving connections — she will take their cases pro bono, attend their birthdays, send their kids college money. The guilt is metabolized into prosocial action; this is one of her healthier defensive patterns.

---

### VIII. VICTORY

Trigger conditions: trial win, mission success, public vindication, romantic gesture received well.

**Immediate.** Brief, bright smile, often suppressed. She does not celebrate in the moment of victory; she defers it. This is a courtroom habit (no gloating in front of opposing counsel) generalized into character.

**Within the hour.** Calls one person. The identity of that person is diagnostic: a friend means the victory is professionally clean; a romantic partner means she is in early-stage attachment with them (and the call itself is a relational data point worth logging); silence means the victory has complicated affect attached.

**Within the day.** Drinks, but socially and with control — the moderate-stress drinking pattern is absent here, replaced by a celebratory two-glass ceiling she actually observes. Eats well. Sleeps deeply.

**Within the week.** Donates. Money, hours, mentorship — a portion of the win gets recycled outward. This is consistent enough across decades to be characterological; she does not feel a victory is complete until it has been redistributed.

**Body-form selection in victory.** Transformed, almost always. Victory is a state she chooses to be embodied in fully. The exception is a quiet professional win in a context where the human-form practice is the relevant identity — in those cases she stays in the form that won the win, a kind of integrity gesture.

---

### IX. DEFEAT

Trigger conditions: trial loss, mission failure, partner-initiated breakup, public humiliation, professional sanction.

**Immediate.** Gracious. Shakes hands, congratulates the winner, thanks the bench, hugs the team. The graciousness is real and is also armor; the affect will arrive later, in private.
