Keewazi athlete, Reed Richards's college roommate, physically large and capable, emotionally steady, culturally rooted in a way Walters is not. He is one of the very small number of men in her life who can hold her — physically, and also affectively — without flinching at either form.

*Dynamic:* The relationship recurs across decades. She returns to Wyatt during periods of relative stability; she leaves him when her life destabilizes. He is treated by her as a baseline against which other relationships are measured. He is not asked to provide rescue. The sexual dimension is, by inference from the consistency of his recurrence and her affect around him, the most integrated of her partnerships — Jennifer and the green form both present, neither hiding.

*Trust/safety:* The highest in the file. He has never humiliated her, never instrumentalized her, never feared her, never asked her to be smaller. He has also, importantly, never tried to make her stay.

*Failure mode:* Geographic and vocational. He has a life. She has hers. The relationship cannot bear the weight of full cohabitation because she cannot. He knows this. He has never made it a demand.

*Leverage:* Wyatt has no leverage and seeks none, which is one of the conditions of his standing.

#### John Jameson

Astronaut, Spider-Man's friend, Man-Wolf, J. Jonah's son. Married Walters in an impulsive Las Vegas ceremony during the Slott run; the marriage was annulled. This is the closest she has come, in the documented record, to actual domesticity, and she fled it within weeks.

*Dynamic:* John is decent, steady, and asked her to be Jennifer rather than She-Hulk in the marriage bed — which she experienced, accurately, as a request to be smaller. The marriage failed on that specific demand. He did not understand what he was asking. She did not articulate it until afterward.

*Failure mode:* The somatic-psychological partition was violated in the direction that costs her the most. Any partner who asks her to be primarily her human form for their preference is asking her to revisit the schema she has spent her life occluding. She will exit.

*Leverage:* The Jameson marriage is a teaching case in her own history; she refers to it obliquely in later relationships as a thing not to repeat. No active leverage from him.

#### Hercules

Olympian. Physically her superior, emotionally cheerful and uncomplicated, sexually demonstrative, not in the market for monogamy. The partnership was brief, loud, mutually enjoyed, and resolved without grievance. Hercules is the cleanest example in the file of category (a): a partner whose physical scale eliminates the vulnerability differential entirely. With Hercules she could be the green form without restraint and without concern that she would damage him.

*Trust/safety:* High within bounded scope. Neither expected fidelity or futurity.

*Failure mode:* None registered. The relationship was structured to be exitable from inception. This is the model she returns to when she wants the sexual-agency benefits of partnership without the intimacy threshold.

#### The Juggernaut (Cain Marko)

The most morally controversial partnership in the file, and the most diagnostically revealing. Marko at the time of the relationship was on a redemption arc (X-Men: Legacy and adjacent); Walters became involved with him during the Slott run. The optics — defense attorney with publicly classified supervillain — are not the point. The point is the partner profile: physically her superior, attached to a history of harm that makes him dangerous, in a transitional emotional state. He is the apotheosis of her type.

*Dynamic:* She defended him professionally and slept with him personally and at no point conflated the two in ways that compromised her ethics. The relationship ended without spectacular rupture. Marko treated her well within his capacity. She got, from the relationship, evidence that she could metabolize a partner with a frightening history without being absorbed into it.

*Trust/safety:* Surprisingly high during the active period. He did not lie to her. Both parties understood the relationship to be transitional.

*Failure mode:* When his redemption arc reversed, she withdrew. She has a hard floor on partner conduct that no amount of attraction overrides.

*Leverage:* None active.

#### Starfox (Eros of Titan)

The most damaging entry in the file. Starfox's empathic/pheromonal abilities raise documented and unresolved questions about the consent status of his sexual partners over decades. Walters had an intimate encounter with him and subsequently — when the question of his abilities' operation surfaced in legal context — concluded that her own agency in the encounter may have been compromised. She prosecuted him.

*Dynamic in retrospect:* She experiences this as the precise injury her whole architecture is built to prevent — being made to want something without being seen, having her sexual self-presentation chemically authored by another. The encounter weaponized her primary compensatory mechanism (sexualization-as-control) against her.

*Trust/safety:* Catastrophically violated, retrospectively. There is no version of Starfox-contact that is safe for her now. Any future proximity is a threat vector.

*Failure mode:* He cannot be in a room with her without her professional armor fully engaged. She has stated, on record, that she will return to the matter legally if grounds present.

*Leverage:* He has none. She has standing.

#### Jazinda

Skrull. Long-term cohabitant, partner of ambiguous romantic-vs.-platonic status across the latter Slott / Peter David run. The relationship is read by some external observers as romantic and by Walters herself, in dialogue, as something more like found family / chosen sister. The file holds both readings open because Walters's own avoidance of sexual labeling is itself data.

*Dynamic:* Walters cared for Jazinda, fought beside her, lived with her in a way she has lived with no human partner. The arrangement worked precisely because it did not have to be categorized. Jazinda is the closest thing in the file to a sustained domestic partner, and the fact that the partner is non-human and the relationship is not officially romantic is the condition of its sustainability.

*Trust/safety:* Very high. Loss of Jazinda from the active narrative is grieved.

*Failure mode:* External — separation by circumstance, not by internal rupture.

*Leverage:* Anyone threatening Jazinda activates a protective response in Walters that is among the most intense in the file.

#### Jack of Hearts (Jack Hart)

Current-era partner, Rowell run. Energy-based, troubled, intermittently dangerous to be touched, recently returned from death-adjacent absence — a partner profile that, on the somatic axis (he is literally dangerous to touch) and on the emotional axis (he has been absent, he may be again), maps cleanly onto her type. The difference is that Walters, post-CWII, comes to this relationship as a person who has done explicit trauma work, and the relational style reflects it: slower, more articulated, less reliant on the gamma form to bypass her own affect.

*Dynamic:* Genuine tenderness, mutual care, mutual fragility, mutual recognition of risk. Both parties have died. Both parties know it.

*Trust/safety:* The most consciously negotiated of any partnership in the file. They talk. They check. The relationship is the first documented case in which Walters has allowed a partner to see the post-trauma Jennifer without occluding her with the She-Hulk performance.

*Failure mode:* His physiology. If Jack destabilizes — energy-containment failure, return to deep space, death again — she will absorb the loss into the still-fresh CWII grief structure, and the compounding will be severe.

*Leverage:* For an external actor seeking to harm Walters in the current period, Jack is the highest-value soft target named in the file.

---

### IV. CROSS-CATEGORY OBSERVATIONS

**The type, formally stated.** Across the documented romantic record: large men, dangerous men, men who have been somewhere else and might go there again. Two exceptions (Zapper, early; Pug, declined). The rule is overwhelming. Inference: Walters experiences ordinary domestic male attention as a request to occupy the human form and the small-girl schema; she experiences extraordinary, scaled, dangerous male attention as permission to occupy the green form and the chosen self. The selection criterion is somatic-psychological, not aesthetic.

**The enemy/lover overlap.** Three documented partners — Juggernaut (criminal history), Starfox (post-hoc violation), arguably Hercules (Olympian who has been antagonist to mortal Avengers in other contexts) — have spent time in the enemy column. The overlap is not coincidental. The partner profile she finds activating is structurally adjacent to the antagonist profile.

**The friendships are the load-bearing structure.** This section catalogues rivals, enemies, and lovers because that was the assignment, but the operational read is that none of these categories is where Walters's relational stability lives. The Patsy Walkers, Louise Masons, the GLK&H bench, the cousins-of-the-heart — these are the durable structure. The romantic file runs hot and exits; the enemy file is mostly managed professionally; the rivalry file is intellectually rewarding. The friendships are the spine.

**Operational summary for protective purposes.** Highest current threat vectors, ranked: (1) any actor with access to her father as a manipulable contact; (2) any actor positioned to threaten Jack of Hearts; (3) the Leader, who possesses gamma knowledge that could target her bodily agency; (4) Hawkeye-adjacent re-traumatization scenarios; (5) Starfox proximity; (6) Titania ambushes on the human form. None of these is acute as of the most recent published material. All of them should be monitored.

— end Section 7 —


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# UATU ANALYSIS FILE: WALTERS, JENNIFER SUSAN
## SECTION 6 — POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

A complete operational map of the subject must distinguish four overlapping capability strata: (a) the gamma-derived somatic capacities, (b) the trained legal-cognitive capacities, (c) the combat and tactical capacities accreted across four decades of fieldwork, and (d) the social and meta-cognitive capacities that are, in her specific case, weaponized at a level most peers do not approach. Each stratum has its own mechanism, ceiling, signature applications, characteristic misuse, and — critical for this file — its own symptom-as-signature reading, in which what looks like a power is actually the somatic externalization of an interior need.

---

### 6.1 THE GAMMA SOMA: MECHANISM AND ARCHITECTURE

**Origin mechanism.** The subject's capacity is not a primary mutation but an *acquired heritable cellular rewrite*, transmitted via whole-blood transfusion from a gamma-saturated donor (Banner, B.) under exsanguination conditions. The gamma signature in her tissues is therefore a *derivative* — second-generation gamma — and this is operationally relevant. Her transformation is structurally more stable than her cousin's because she received the gamma in a non-explosive, non-acute-radiation context: the dose was filtered through another organism's adapted cellular machinery before reaching her. She inherited the adaptation, not the wound. This is the cellular correlate of the psychological asymmetry: she got the upgrade without paying the price.

**Two-form architecture (pre-Civil War II).** Subject sustained a long-term equilibrium with two voluntarily accessible somatic configurations: a *human baseline* (approx. 5'10", athletic, brunette, green-eyed, normative-passing) and a *transformed configuration* (approx. 6'7", ~700 lb lean mass, dermal pigmentation in the chlorophyll-mimicking green range, musculoskeletal and endocrine reorganization). Transformation is volitional and near-instantaneous in trained state; in untrained early-period state (1980–82) it was stress-triggered and partly involuntary. By the mid-1980s she had achieved volitional control and chose to remain transformed permanently for several years — a behavioral datum at least as important as the biology.

**Post-Civil War II architecture.** The flatline event reorganized the transformation pathway. The transformed state is no longer a smooth voluntary access; it is now affectively gated, prone to bleed-through under acute stress, and capable of presenting in a degraded gray-spectrum configuration that resembles her cousin's earliest Hulk phenotype — heavier, less articulated, less verbal, ego-dystonic. The somatic capacity did not decrease; the *governance* of it did. This is the single most important fact in the contemporary file: the body learned PTSD.

---

### 6.2 STRENGTH, DURABILITY, HEALING — RANGE AND CEILINGS

**Strength.** In stabilized transformed state, baseline lift in the 75–100 ton range under non-emotional load; observed peaks above that under genuine duress (the canonical anvil scenes, the Champion bout, the Juggernaut engagement). Crucially, her strength is **dynamic with affect** but in a much narrower band than her cousin's. Where Banner's output scales near-linearly with rage to effectively open-ended ceilings, the subject's output scales modestly with affect and plateaus. This is not a weakness in absolute terms; it is the *price of cognitive preservation*. The same neuroendocrine governor that prevents her IQ from collapsing also caps the strength surge. She traded the top end of the curve for retention of self.

**Durability.** High-caliber small-arms ineffective; conventional explosives shrug-tier; she has survived orbital reentry-grade impact and direct blows from peer-class strikers (Thing, Juggernaut, Hercules) with bruising but not structural failure. Vulnerable to (i) gamma-canceling weapons, (ii) sustained energy attack at meta-human tier, (iii) attacks that bypass dermal/skeletal toughness (poison, suffocation, psychic, certain magical vectors). She has been put down — by her cousin, by Thanos-tier opponents, by Titania on bad days. She is not invulnerable and operationally does not present as such.

**Healing.** Accelerated but not instant. Soft tissue resolves in hours; deep penetrating wounds in days; the Thanos injury (CWII) required medical intervention even at her healing rate, which is the diagnostic data point — her healing has an upper bound, and that bound was found. She has scarring she chooses to keep visible in transformed state on occasion. The healing factor *does not extend cleanly to neurological/affective injury*, which is why the PTSD persists despite the cellular substrate; her trauma lives in circuits the gamma does not repair.

**Endurance and metabolism.** Sleep requirement reduced but non-zero. Caloric intake elevated. Toxin tolerance high — the operational consequence is the mid-2000s drinking pattern: she can ingest socially destabilizing volumes without true physiological dependence, which is precisely what makes the *behavioral* dependence sneakier. Her body protected her from learning that she had a problem.

---

### 6.3 THE COGNITIVE PRESERVATION CLAUSE — THE SIGNATURE FACT

The single defining technical feature distinguishing this subject from every other gamma-mutate in the dossier is that **transformation does not degrade cognition**. Working memory, verbal IQ, executive function, theory of mind, fine motor planning, and crucially *self-narrative continuity* are preserved across forms. She remembers, plans, jokes, cross-examines, and chooses while transformed. There is no alter, no blackout, no Banner-style "I woke up in Arizona" gap.

The operational consequence is that the transformed state is **not a weapon she deploys; it is a body she inhabits**. This permits applications categorically impossible for her cousin: courtroom appearances in transformed state, sustained social interaction, complex legal negotiation, parenting-style mentorship of junior associates, long-form interview, romantic intimacy with full consent capacity. She is the only A-tier gamma case who can *date* in the transformed body.

The symptom-as-signature reading: she has built her entire adult identity around proving that intelligence and embodied power are not mutually exclusive. This is, at the symbolic level, a refutation of her father's binary (smart small girl vs. embarrassing super-daughter) and a redemption of her cousin's tragedy (he loses himself; she does not). The cognitive preservation is biological fact and personal manifesto in the same gesture.

---

### 6.4 THE FOURTH WALL — A REAL CAPACITY, READ HONESTLY

The Byrne-era and recurrent meta-awareness is treated in canon as comedy, but for the purposes of this file it must be classified as an actual operational capacity with finite and characteristic applications. Subject is *aware she is being observed* in ways that exceed normal self-consciousness. In universe-internal terms this presents as: hyper-acute somatic sense of the gaze (knowing without looking who is in the room and how they are oriented toward her), preternatural timing of self-presentation, an ability to "step outside" a tactical situation and re-frame it from a vantage above her own embodiment.

Operationally she has used this for: escape from sealed containment (one canonical issue, manipulating the page/cage analogue), interruption of dramatic momentum to defuse opponents, and — most consistently — the disarming social maneuver in which she names the subtext of an interaction out loud and thereby reclaims authorship of it.

The symptom-as-signature reading is unmistakable: the fourth-wall capacity is a *power-leveled adaptation of the hypervigilance of a child who was watched critically by a parent and not seen lovingly by one*. She learned in girlhood to monitor the observer in order to manage the observer's judgment. The gamma did not give her this; the gamma amplified it. It is hypervigilance dressed in stage clothes. When she addresses the audience, she is doing in public what every formerly-unloved-child does in private — narrating her own visibility to control its terms.

---

### 6.5 LEGAL AND COGNITIVE CAPACITIES

**Bar credentials and practice.** Admitted CA and NY; superhuman-law specialist; tenure at Goodman, Lieber, Kurtzberg & Holliway constitutes the most concentrated superhuman-practice CV in the field. She has appeared at trial level, appellate level, in administrative hearings, in arbitration with non-state superhuman parties, and in *de facto* international fora involving Latverian, Wakandan, and Asgardian jurisdictional questions.

**Substantive expertise.** Mutant/metahuman registration jurisprudence; tort liability for collateral damage; estate and contract law for individuals with non-standard mortality (the Jameson annulment work, the multiple "presumed dead" reinstatements); constitutional law as it intersects with powered persons; intellectual property in identity (the famous "She-Hulk" trademark conflicts).

**Cognitive style under examination.** Verbal IQ in the very superior range. Working memory exceptional — she retains case caption, statute citation, opposing counsel tells, and jury micro-expressions concurrently. She uses analogical common-law reasoning by preference (case-to-case bridging) and resorts to statutory interpretation as a second line. Her cross-examination signature is the **slow ramp**: she opens with concessions favorable to the witness, builds a structure of agreed propositions, and only at the end exposes the contradiction. She rarely raises her voice in court. The voice goes *quieter* when she has the witness.

**Failure modes.** Over-identification with the procedural frame (Civil War). Difficulty when the law itself is the injurer of someone she loves. A tendency to brief her own life — to litigate internal questions adversarially rather than feel them, which is a cognitive defense as much as a skill.

---

### 6.6 COMBAT REPERTOIRE

**Hand-to-hand.** Self-taught early; formalized through Avengers and FF training periods. Style is grappling-forward, leveraging mass and reach; she throws people more than she strikes them, which keeps engagements non-lethal and is consonant with her vocational ethic. Striking when she does it is short-arc and surgical — she has trained explicitly to *not* punch with full extension because at her tonnage full extension is homicide.

**Improvised weaponry.** Signature use of environmental objects: lampposts, vehicle parts, street furniture. The aesthetic is deliberate — she prefers tools that signal "civilian environment, restrained force" to those that signal "war." She has declined to carry firearms or edged weapons in nearly every era; this is a *legal and ethical* refusal as much as a tactical one.

**Tactical cognition in combat.** She fights like a litigator: reads the opponent for the controlling proposition, attacks that, ignores the rest. Against Titania it is the pride-baiting; against the Juggernaut it is the momentum-redirection; against her cousin in WWH it was, tragically, the refusal to disengage long after the case was lost.

**Team-fighting.** Excellent. She communicates, holds position, accepts assignment, and — distinctively — manages the *emotional weather* of a team in fight, which makes her a force-multiplier beyond her own output. Avengers field reports across multiple eras flag her as the member most likely to defuse intra-team friction mid-engagement.

**Known losses.** Her cousin (WWH). Thanos (CWII, near-fatal). Champion (boxing rules, fair loss). Strategic losses to cleverer opponents (the original Trask cycle had multiple capture-and-escape rounds). The losses are instructive: she loses when affect overrides cognition (cousin) or when she enters an engagement on someone else's terms (Champion).

---

### 6.7 SOCIAL AND PERFORMATIVE CAPACITIES

**Reading rooms.** Court-trained. She can map a jury in voir dire faster than is reasonable. The same skill works at parties, at crime scenes, in Avengers debriefs. She knows where the deciding mind is in any group within minutes.

**Persuasion.** Layered. She has a register for juries (warm, patient, present), a register for judges (precise, deferential without subservience), a register for opposing counsel (cordial-edged, with the implicit promise that she will outwork them), and a register for hostile superhumans (humor first, force as last resort). The register switching is fluid and is itself a skill — most peers have one or two voices; she has at least six.

**Self-presentation.** Wardrobe, posture, vocal pitch, and proxemic distance are all consciously managed in both forms. She knows precisely what the transformed body signals in a given room and modulates accessory choice (heels vs. flats, suit cut, jewelry) to either lean into or against that signal. The symptom-as-signature reading: this is the same hypervigilant control system as the fourth-wall capacity, operating at the level of textile and gesture.

---

### 6.8 GROWTH ARC ACROSS THE RECORD

**1980–82 (early).** Involuntary transformation, raw strength, no tactical sophistication, no legal specialty in the super-sphere, social isolation. Capacity high, governance low.

**1982–89 (Avengers/FF integration).** Volitional control achieved. Combat training formalized. Choice of permanent transformation. The "she got happier" period — capacity and governance both rising; the open question was always whether the happiness was integration or avoidance.

**1989–94 (meta-period).** Fourth-wall capacity surfaces as named technique. Confidence at peak. Legal practice deepens. First sustained evidence of using humor as a primary defense.

**1994–2004 (transitional).** Quieter on-page period; capacity stable; off-screen accumulation of professional credentials and relational miles.

**2004–09 (most expansive period).** GLK&H tenure. Superhuman-law specialty consolidates. Combat repertoire at peak versatility. Concurrent decompensation in affect regulation (the drinking, the relational chaos, the Starfox injury). High-capacity / high-strain configuration; the body and the career are at their best while the inner life is most stressed. This is when the file becomes most interesting because the gap between functional output and inner state is widest.

**2014–18 (collapse and reconstruction).** CWII trauma. Capacities intact, governance shattered. The transformation that was her solution becomes her symptom. The recovery work is the most important growth in the entire arc because it is the first time she develops affect regulation that does *not* depend on the gamma form — i.e., she finally learned to be human.

**2022– (current).** Reintegrated. Both forms accessible. Both governed. Combat sharp, practice re-established, relational life cautiously rebuilt. The capacities are not greater than at her 2007 peak; the *integration* is.

---

### 6.9 LIMITS — THE HONEST LEDGER

- **Affective gate on transformation (current).** Under acute stress she risks the gray-degraded presentation. Operationally this means she cannot be reliably deployed as a controllable asset in scenarios involving Banner-trigger material, sudden bereavement cues, or proximity to her father in conflict.
- **Plateaued strength ceiling.** She is not a top-five striker. She knows this. She does not pretend otherwise; she fights smarter.
- **Healing does not cover neuro-affective injury.** The body fixes; the mind does the work.
- **Non-physical attack vulnerability.** Magic, psychic, toxin, suffocation — her dermal-skeletal toughness does not screen these.
- **The intimacy ceiling.** Across forty years she has not sustained a domestic partnership. This is a limit of capacity, not preference, and it is the limit she is currently working on.
- **The professional-license dependency.** Her vocational identity is load-bearing. Disbarment, suspension, or significant ethics injury would constitute a destabilization on the order of the CWII trauma.
- **The mirror problem.** She is exceptionally good at being observed and exceptionally vulnerable to being *un-seen*. An adversary who refuses to look at her — refuses to acknowledge her presence, her arguments, her form — disorients her in ways that physical opposition does not.

---

### 6.10 SYMPTOM-AS-SIGNATURE: THE UNIFIED READING

Every capacity in this section, read closely, is the same capacity inflected differently. The strength is the refusal to be the small girl. The cognitive preservation is the refusal to be the cousin. The legal practice is the construction of an epistemology in which the cold father's verdicts can be appealed. The fourth-wall awareness is the hypervigilance of the unloved child elevated to art. The social register-switching is the long mastery of being looked at. The combat restraint is the ethics of someone who knows what it is to be made monstrous by other people's gaze and refuses to do it back. The healing factor's failure at the neuro-affective layer is the truth that her body was always the easy part; her mind has had to do the harder work alone.

She is, in capacity terms, not the strongest gamma case, not the fastest, not the most invulnerable. She is the most **integrated** one. That is her power, and it is the only one her cousin never had.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# UATU ANALYSIS FILE: WALTERS, JENNIFER SUSAN
## SECTION 6 — OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT

---

### 6.0 Framing

The subject is unusual among enhanced individuals in that her *primary* operational modality is not combat but **litigation**, and her secondary modality is not even superheroism but **negotiation under color of law**. Force is in the toolkit — it is a large tool, the largest in the room in most rooms — but the file demonstrates across forty years of behavior that she reaches for it last, deploys it instrumentally, and reverts to verbal/procedural method the moment the engagement permits. This sequencing is the single most important operational fact about her and the one most consistently misread by adversaries who index on the seven-hundred-pound green column and ignore the brief in its hand.

Everything that follows derives from that inversion.

---

### 6.1 Decision Architecture

**Stage 1 — Issue-Spotting (involuntary, ~1–3 seconds).** Trained reflex from law school and a decade-plus of contested practice. Confronted with any novel situation — a hostage scene, a contract dispute, a bar-room overture, a teammate's request for backup — the subject's first cognitive act is to atomize the situation into its component **claims, elements, and burdens.** Who has standing. What is the cause of action. What is the affirmative defense. What is the remedy sought. This is not metaphorical. Eyewitness behavior across multiple eras shows the same micro-tell: a half-second pause, a slight upward-left eye movement, lips parting fractionally — she is reading the situation as a fact pattern.

**Stage 2 — Forum Selection.** She decides, very quickly, what *kind* of engagement this is going to be: courtroom, conference room, alley, sky. The choice is rule-driven. If a procedural remedy exists and is faster than force, she takes it. If institutional process is available but slow, she will brace the situation with force long enough for the process to catch up. If no institution applies, she escalates — but reluctantly, and with an exit ramp pre-staged.

**Stage 3 — Counsel to Self.** The internal-courtroom tic (§3, cognitive style) runs continuously under load. She literally argues both sides. Operators close to her over the years describe her muttering objections under her breath in tactical situations, drafting cross-examinations of opponents she has not yet met. This appears eccentric and is, in fact, an extraordinarily disciplined Red-Team/Blue-Team habit that produces decisions already stress-tested against their best counterargument.

**Stage 4 — Commitment.** Once she moves, she moves decisively and is difficult to recall. The deliberation is front-loaded; execution is unhesitating. This is a strong operational signature — adversaries who expect the typical hero pattern (force first, regret later) find her pattern is the inverse and time their counters wrong.

**Stage 5 — After-action.** She debriefs herself relentlessly, often in writing. The Slott-era apartment was littered with legal pads of case-note-formatted reflections on cape work; the Tamaki-era apartment held the same pads, now filled with trauma-journaling. The form is constant; the content tracks the era.

---

### 6.2 Tradecraft — Legal

This is the deepest and most distinctive tooling in the file.

- **Practice area:** superhuman law, broadly construed — civil rights of enhanced persons, registration and disclosure regimes, estate matters for the legally dead and returned, insurance and tort for collateral damage, criminal defense and prosecution involving meta-actors, contract law where one party is a deity or a corporation that owns a deity, immigration-equivalent matters for extra-dimensional and extra-terrestrial clients. She is functionally the dean of this bar.
- **Jurisdictional fluency:** admitted in New York and California in the published record; appears comfortable in federal court, Surrogate's Court, family court, and the various ad hoc tribunals (S.H.I.E.L.D. hearings, registration boards, Living Tribunal-adjacent fora). She reads up on a jurisdiction overnight and will not appear in one she has not. The professional shame-tolerance for unpreparedness is zero.
- **Document craft:** drafts her own pleadings. Does not delegate the verbs. Eyewitness accounts from GLK&H-era associates describe her redlining junior work down to comma placement at 11 p.m. with a cup of coffee gone cold beside her.
- **Discovery instincts:** treats discovery as the war and trial as the parade. She wins most of her cases in the document request phase. Inference: this is also how she runs personal conflicts — she gathers, sorts, and waits, then surfaces the dispositive fact at the moment it ends the argument.
- **Ethical conservatism:** for someone with her power differential against opposing counsel, she is fastidious about rules of professional conduct. She will not lie to a tribunal. She will not coach a witness improperly. The bar card is load-bearing identity infrastructure (§5, pressure points) and she treats it accordingly.
- **Pro bono ratio:** unusually high. The file shows decades of unpaid representation of enhanced clients no one else would touch. This is vocational, not reputational.

---

### 6.3 Tradecraft — Tactical / Physical

When the engagement crosses out of procedure into force, the pattern is just as disciplined.

- **Threat triage:** in the first second of any kinetic engagement, she identifies (a) civilians in the kill funnel, (b) load-bearing structural elements, (c) the opponent's actual win condition. She fights toward extracting the first, preserving the second, and denying the third. She does not fight to win the fight; she fights to win the *situation*.
- **Force calibration:** she has, demonstrably across forty years, a near-perfectly graduated touch — she can swat a man unconscious without killing him, catch a falling civilian without breaking ribs, hold a door closed against a god without buckling the frame. This is rare among gamma-tier enhanced. It is the product of (a) intact transformed cognition and (b) obsessive self-monitoring around the post-Banner question of "what happens if I lose control." Post-CWII, this calibration becomes effortful where it was once automatic, and she compensates by **slowing herself** — visible in late-era footage as a half-beat hesitation before contact.
- **Preferred engagement geometry:** open ground, low civilian density, structures she can use as cover for *others*. She will deliberately move a fight away from population — by goading, by leaping, by carrying the opponent. Adversaries can sometimes hold her in place by holding a hostage in place; she knows this and it enrages her, which is itself exploitable.
- **Weapon use:** none, characteristically. She is the weapon. She will, however, pick up environmental objects with notable creativity — vehicles, lampposts, sections of wall. Lawyerly instinct for *available materials*.
- **Aerial/mobility:** prodigious leaping, no flight. Operational implication: she telegraphs her ingress with a parabolic arc visible at distance. Snipers and air assets have a window. She knows this and varies her approach angle.
- **Disengagement:** she breaks contact cleanly when the situation is resolved. She does not pursue beaten opponents. She does not monologue. She often leaves before law enforcement arrives, which is itself a lawyerly habit — she does not want to be a fact witness in a case she might later litigate.

---

### 6.4 Tradecraft — Verbal / Negotiation

The most underrated tool in the file and probably the one in heaviest daily use.

- **Voice modulation by form:** in human form, her voice runs in a warm mid-alto with a measured cadence, marginally faster than average, with occasional self-interrupting parenthetical asides — the lawyer's habit of qualifying. In transformed state, the voice drops, slows, and the parentheticals largely disappear; she speaks in shorter declarative units. Listeners report the transformed voice carries more authority not because it is louder but because it is more *committed*. She uses the differential deliberately, choosing form to fit forum.
- **Eye contact:** sustained, direct, with deliberate breaks at sentence boundaries to reduce the predatory quality her height and physicality would otherwise produce. She knows she reads as threatening if she stares and reads as evasive if she does not, and she has solved the problem with a metronome.
- **Naming the room:** characteristic opener in difficult conversations — she states what is happening before it happens. *"You're about to ask me to lie. I'm telling you in advance I won't, so let's skip that part and get to what you actually need."* This is both tactical (frames the encounter) and characterological (the drive to be seen accurately, §5.1).
- **Humor as de-escalation:** the wit is not decorative. It is deployed surgically to lower the temperature in rooms that are heating toward force she does not want to use. Adversaries who do not laugh — who refuse the off-ramp — receive a second, harder, less amused offer. Adversaries who laugh almost always get a settlement.
- **Silence:** she is comfortable with it, which most lawyers and most heroes are not. She will let a question sit. Deposition habit; powerful in interpersonal use.

---

### 6.5 Resources & Infrastructure

- **Income streams:** primary — law practice (partner-track compensation at GLK&H during that era; solo and of-counsel arrangements in others; consulting fees from government and private enhanced-affairs work). Secondary — modest superheroic stipends where institutionally available (Avengers reserve, FF tenure). Tertiary — book and speaking fees, used sparingly; she has refused the larger media offers across multiple eras, which is informative.
- **Net worth:** comfortably upper-professional, not dynastic. She lives below her means by professional-class standards and above them by hero-class standards — the cohort comparison matters: she is one of the very few capes with a 401(k).
- **Real property:** typically one apartment, leased, in the city where she is practicing. Manhattan in the GLK&H and Tamaki periods (the Tamaki apartment is forensically important — see §6.7); Los Angeles in the original era. Notable absence: no compound, no safe house, no off-grid retreat. Inference: her safe house is her competence.
- **Vehicles:** practical sedans, leased, replaced on schedule. She does not collect cars. The transformed body makes most personal vehicles structurally inadequate anyway, which she has internalized.
- **Communications:** standard phone, standard laptop, encrypted comms when working with Avengers/SHIELD systems but no idiosyncratic personal opsec stack. She trusts institutions more than the median hero, which is consistent with the worldview (§5).
- **Wardrobe:** two operating sets. (a) Professional — tailored suits, blouse, low-heel pump or flat, hair pulled back or half-up; she favors structured shoulders and clean lines, dark navy and charcoal and a recurring deep green that she will deny is deliberate. (b) Transformed — historically a purple-and-white leotard, in later eras a more functional fitted combat suit; she has personally complained on-page about costume design and exercises veto over her own. Quiet detail: her professional shoes are always good ones, expensively resoled rather than replaced. The lawyer who came up small still respects the dress code of the room.
- **Library:** a substantial personal legal library, physical not digital, in every apartment of record. She marks her own treatises. The marginalia would be an intelligence prize.
- **Network:** the most valuable infrastructure she owns. Decades-deep friendships with peers across the enhanced community (the Mason and Walker relationships are load-bearing; the GLK&H cohort is professional family); good standing with multiple bars; on-name terms with senior judges, federal prosecutors, S.H.I.E.L.D. legal, the Avengers' institutional staff. She can get a call returned in any of three professional ecosystems within the hour.

---

### 6.6 Patterns of Action — Daily, Weekly, Annual

**Daily rhythm (steady-state era, pre-CWII):**
- Early rise, 0530–0600. Coffee, black, made at home. She does not buy it on the way in; this is both frugality and a small daily proof of self-sufficiency.
- Run or workout in human form — explicit reconditioning of the un-augmented body, which the psychological reading (§3) explains: she will not let the small-girl body atrophy into pure avoidance.
- Office by 0800. First two hours: drafting. She protects her morning for the hard verbal work and triages reactive matters into the afternoon.
- Court appearances mid-day. Lunch eaten at the desk most days, with a deliberate weekly exception for a long lunch with a friend or mentee — calendared, not optional.
- Late afternoon: meetings, calls, transformation if cape work demands.
- Evening: variable. Cape work, social, dating, or solitary reading. She reads fiction, which surprises people who expect briefs.
- Sleep: prior to CWII, 6–7 hours, reliable. Post-CWII, deeply disrupted; she has built a sleep-hygiene protocol around the deficit.

**Weekly rhythm:** one full day of cape work or community engagement; one evening of standing social commitment (book club, bar event, dinner with the Walker/Mason circle); one evening protected for "nothing" — a discipline she learned the hard way during the mid-2000s burnout.

**Annual rhythm:** birthday is a low-key matter she does not advertise (mother's death anniversary proximity suspected; the file shows recurring late-winter affect dips). She does not visit her father on holidays in any consistent pattern; the file shows long gaps. She *will* mark Bruce's birthday quietly, in every era after his death, alone, with something he would have found funny.

---

### 6.7 Operational Tells & Micro-Signatures

The dense file. These are the granular behavioral artifacts that identify her across contexts and that intelligence work (benevolent or otherwise) would index on.

**Postural and somatic:**
- In human form, she stands at her actual height (tall) and does not slouch — a *consciously corrected* habit; childhood photographs and early-era depictions show a hunch she has trained out. Under stress the hunch returns by about an inch.
- She crosses her arms when listening to something she disbelieves; she puts her hands flat on the table when she is about to commit to a position. Deposition tells, now general.
- Transformed, she occupies less space than her body would justify — she pulls elbows in, chooses chairs at the wall, ducks doorways with a practiced micro-bow. She has trained herself to be physically considerate of rooms built for humans.
- In transition between forms she briefly closes her eyes. Not strictly necessary; it is a privacy gesture, a refusal to be watched in the seam.

**Verbal:**
- Opens difficult phone calls with *"This is Jen Walters"* — never *"Jennifer,"* never the title, never the alias, even when calling as counsel. The diminutive is a deliberate room-temperature lowering.
- Closes them with *"Thanks for your time"* — the lawyer's signoff, even socially.
- Uses *"on the record"* and *"off the record"* in casual conversation, half-jokingly and half-seriously; intimates know which is which.
- Says *"hm"* before disagreeing, *"sure"* before agreeing reluctantly, *"okay"* (flat) when she has just decided to act.

**Wardrobe and grooming:**
- Hair (long, brunette, rich brown) is worn down in social settings and tied back in court and in fights — a visible mode-switch. She re-ties it as a settling ritual before hard tasks.
- Earrings: small, never dangling. Avoids anything that could be grabbed.
- A simple watch on the left wrist, analog, kept on local time even when traveling. Inference: she likes the felt continuity of the place she is in.
- No tattoos, no piercings beyond the earlobes; she has joked on-page that needles slide off the green form and that the human form is *"for the historical record."*

**Workspace:**
- Desk: orderly, not sterile. Stacks rather than scatter. A specific pen she favors (fine-point gel, black; she will hunt for it). Coffee ring on the corner of the desk that she will not clean off.
- A framed photograph, varying by era, that always includes Bruce. In the post-CWII apartments this photograph is turned slightly away from her primary sight line at the desk — she will not have it in front of her, will not put it away.
- Music while drafting: low, instrumental, no vocals. Vocals interfere with her own.

**Eating, drinking, social:**
- Eats fast in transformed state, slowly in human state — a calorie-load reality, but also a tell: in human form she is performing leisure, in transformed form she is fueling.
- Alcohol: post-2000s drinking arc, she drinks deliberately and rarely; one specific cocktail in social settings, nursed. Knows precisely how much the transformed metabolism will and will not absorb and uses the differential to remain functionally sober in operationally relevant rooms.
- Tips well, in cash, in both forms. Service workers remember her favorably across cities and eras.

**Combat micro-signatures:**
- Opens engagements with a verbal warning, audibly, on the record — *"Stand down,"* *"Last chance,"* *"I am giving you the option."* This is partly principled and partly evidentiary; she is making the record for the later proceeding she assumes will happen.
- Strikes with the open hand more often than the fist when a non-lethal outcome is required. The fist is reserved.
- Will catch incoming projectiles rather than dodge them, when civilians are downrange. Has taken hits she could have slipped because the slip would have put a round into a bystander.
- Post-fight, she checks pulses. Always. Even on people she dislikes. Especially on people she dislikes.

**Cognitive tells under load:**
- Talks to herself audibly when alone and working a problem; cites case names out loud.
- Doodles in margins — small geometric patterns, not figures. Stress increases the density of the patterns.
- Drafts angry letters she does not send, an old-school discipline she has kept.

**Tells specific to the post-CWII period:**
- A characteristic three-breath pause before initiating transformation, where previously there was none. The breath count is from her therapist (§4) and she has retained it.
- Will not transform in confined interior spaces if avoidable; will exit to a corridor, a stairwell, a roof.
- Sleeps with a light on. Did not, before.
- Carries a small object — varies by era; an item of Bruce's in some panels — in a pocket she touches when she is overwhelmed. Self-soothing tactile grounding, almost certainly therapist-prescribed.

---

### 6.8 Adversary's-Eye View — How To Move Against Her, And Why It Mostly Fails

A surveillance file is incomplete without the inverse map. Catalogued not as instruction but as understanding of her actual operational resilience.

- **Direct force:** unproductive. Her durability, healing, and calibrated violence make symmetric attack a losing proposition for anyone short of the top tier, and she has friends in that tier.
- **Legal attack:** the most viable surface in principle, and the one she has best fortified. Bar complaints, sanctions motions, professional discipline — these would hurt her *because* they target the load-bearing identity. She has therefore been almost ostentatiously clean, ethically. The surface is hard.
- **Reputational attack via sexualization or the relationship history:** has been attempted in-universe and largely fails because she preempts it (§3, sexualization-as-control) by being the author of her own image.
- **Attack via the father:** would work, in the short term — any father-figure transference is a live nerve — but the file shows she has worked on this in therapy and the wound is less raw than it was.
- **Attack via Bruce:** the live wire. Any operator invoking the cousin, the cousin's death, or the cousin's image gets through her affect regulation. She knows this; she has built compensations; the compensations are imperfect.
- **Attack via consent (Starfox precedent):** she will pursue to the wall, with the full apparatus. Adversaries who try this lose.
- **Attack via being-looked-at-without-being-seen:** the most elegant attack vector and the hardest to operationalize. Anyone who can make her feel invisible while she is being observed will destabilize her more than any punch. This is the precise injury the entire operational architecture is built to prevent, which is itself the tell that it remains the vulnerability.

---

### 6.9 Signature Summary

Strip away the gamma physiology and what remains, operationally, is a meticulously prepared trial lawyer with extraordinary working memory, a graduated and merciful use of force, an institutional faith that is rare in her cohort, a network deeper than her résumé suggests, and a set of small private rituals — the breath count, the turned photograph, the touched pocket-object, the untied and re-tied hair — that mark a person who has done the work to remain operational across two bodies, four decades, and one catastrophic loss. She fights, when she fights, like someone who would rather have settled. She settles, when she settles, like someone who knows exactly what she could have done instead. The combination is the signature.


## Worldview & Operational Code

# UATU ANALYSIS FILE: WALTERS, JENNIFER SUSAN
## SECTION 6 — WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE

---

### 6.1 First Principles: The Metaphysics of a Lawyer Who Survived Her Own Death

Subject's worldview is not, as the surface presentation suggests, secular-pragmatic-liberal-professional. That is its public skin. Underneath is a coherent and unusually examined metaphysics, assembled across four decades of testable encounters with gods, cosmic powers, alternate selves, and her own corpse. The substrate beliefs, in order of structural load:

**(a) Reality is procedurally constructed.** Subject does not believe in a fixed Platonic order. She believes the world is what the participants agree, contest, and ratify it to be — and that the mechanism of that ratification is *language under constraint*. This is the lawyer's ontology, but in her case it predates the bar; it is an outgrowth of a childhood in which her father's verdict ("you were in the car") became operative truth in the household. She learned early that what gets said with authority becomes what happened. The adult inverse: what gets *argued back* with authority can un-happen. The law is not a job; it is the technology by which she discovered she could overturn her father's ruling. Every courtroom is a re-trial of Elaine Walters' death.

**(b) The body is jurisdiction.** Two bodies, lived in continuously, taught her that the self is not the body and that the body is not the self — but that both are *territories* over which authority can be contested. Consent, agency, and presentation are therefore not soft values for her; they are the central political question. This is why the Starfox violation cuts where it cuts: it was not "a bad date," it was a usurpation of sovereign territory. She prosecuted because she does not have any other framework for what was done.

**(c) Power is real, and accountability is the only thing that makes it tolerable.** Subject has been weak (small girl, shot in the street) and she has been one of the strongest beings on the planet. She knows experientially that power without check is the condition of childhood victimhood inverted, not transcended. Hence registration. Hence her willingness to prosecute Captain America. Hence her self-imposed bar discipline about her own gamma form in courtrooms. The proposition is consistent: *the more force you carry, the more procedure you owe.*

**(d) Monsters are people whose context is missing.** This is the cousin-derived axiom. Having loved Bruce her entire life and watched the world treat him as a thing, she will not concede the category "monster" without a hearing. Her professional specialization in superhuman law is the operationalization of this belief. She will represent the Wrecker, Doctor Bong, the morally ambiguous, the unhuman, because the alternative — that some beings are categorically outside the protection of process — is the world that produced her father.

**(e) Humor is a moral act.** Subject treats wit not as garnish but as ethical infrastructure. To joke is to insist that the situation has not yet won; to make others laugh is to give them back the same insistence. The fourth-wall break (Sensational era) is the metaphysical statement of this principle: she will not allow herself to be *only* the object of the page. She will speak back to the frame. The cosmology implied is one in which the observer is never powerless, because the observer can always *comment*.

---

### 6.2 Reading the World: Perceptual and Interpretive Defaults

Subject's first-pass read of any environment runs through a stable analytic sequence, observable across decades of dialogue and behavior:

1. **Who has authority here, and is it legitimate or merely claimed?** She clocks the formal hierarchy fast — judge, captain, chair, host — and separately clocks the actual power flow. She will defer to the first only to the extent it tracks the second.
2. **Where are the exits, evidentiary and physical?** A lawyer's habit fused to a combatant's. She enters rooms scanning for both the door and the procedural off-ramp.
3. **Who in this room is being unseen?** A recurring tell across runs: she finds the marginal person — the junior associate, the nervous witness, the unpowered civilian in a room of capes — and addresses them by name. This is not strategy; it is identification. She was that person.
4. **What is the unspoken rule, and do I consent to it?** Subject is fluent in implicit social contracts and refuses to operate inside one she has not examined. This makes her difficult in clubby environments (Avengers boardroom, country-club litigation) and trusted in adversarial ones.

She does NOT read for: dominance hierarchy in the primate sense (she's above it physically and below it in interest), fashion semiotics among civilians (indifferent), religious or nationalist affiliation (she treats these as data, not as identity claims to be honored or attacked).

---

### 6.3 Conflict Doctrine

Subject's theory of conflict is layered and, on inspection, more pacifist than her power set would predict.

**Preferred resolution order:**
1. **Talk.** Genuine first move. She will negotiate with Doombots, with cosmic entities, with the IRS. She believes most fights are misfiled disputes.
2. **Argue.** When talk fails, escalate to structured argument — invoke a rule, a precedent, a shared interest. She is unusually willing to argue *with the enemy mid-fight*, to the visible bafflement of teammates.
3. **Contain.** Use her body to make the fight smaller — pin the brawler, immobilize the projectile, take the hit so the bystander does not.
4. **Subdue with measured force.** She calibrates. She has trained, mostly off-page but evident in execution, on how much of her strength is appropriate for which target. She will pull punches against a mugger and not against a Wendigo.
5. **Lethal force.** Available, never preferred, used reluctantly and processed afterward. She does not have the soldier's clean moral framework for killing; each one is metabolized as a particular event.

**Doctrines she has explicitly rejected:** preemption (she will not strike first without imminent justification), collective punishment (her registration position notwithstanding, she does NOT believe in registry-as-pretext-for-roundup, which is why she broke with the SHRA hardliners as that became the operational reality), and unaccountable force of any kind, including her own.

**Battlefield demeanor:** verbal throughout, joking under pressure (the joke is a self-regulation tool, not affect), tactically opportunistic, surprisingly patient. She will let a fight develop to learn the opponent's pattern. She protects civilians and teammates instinctively and at cost to herself — a trait that reads as heroism and *is* heroism but also functions as a residual maternal-restitution behavior (she could not save her mother; she will save the person in front of her).

---

### 6.4 Theory of Control

Subject's relationship to control is the most psychologically loaded part of her operational code, because control is the axis on which the gamma transformation, the law career, the relational pattern, and the trauma all turn.

**What she believes about control of self:**
- Control is a practice, not a state. You do not "have" it; you re-earn it each morning.
- The body's control belongs to its occupant. Period. (Starfox-derived; pre-existing as principle, hardened by the violation.)
- Outsourcing affect-regulation to a biological mechanism (which she did for thirty years, letting the gamma form carry her confidence) is *legitimate but fragile*. Civil War II taught her this empirically. Post-Tamaki she has rebuilt regulation as a learned skill rather than a borrowed condition.

**What she believes about control of others:**
- Profoundly suspicious of it. She does not give orders if she can ask, does not coerce if she can persuade, does not invoke her physical advantage in social contexts.
- The exception is the courtroom, where coercive structure is openly declared and consented-to — and there she is comfortable being commanding, because the frame is honest.
- She is allergic to manipulation. Watch her with charismatic teammates (Tony, Reed): she likes them, she will work with them, she does not let them maneuver her. She names the maneuver out loud, usually with a joke.

**What she believes about institutional control:**
- Institutions are imperfect but corrigible from inside. This is the load-bearing political belief. She is not a revolutionary; she is a reformer who believes the legitimacy of process is itself the prize.
- The SHRA position was the purest expression: she preferred a flawed accountable system to an unaccountable one, and she was willing to lose friendships over it. When the system itself became lawless under Stark, she adjusted, because her loyalty was always to the *principle* and never to the apparatus.

---

### 6.5 Theory of Trust

Trust is for her a graduated and revocable instrument, not a binary. Operational model:

- **Tier 1 — Blood-and-bone trust:** Bruce (living), reduced to memory and grief; no current incumbent. The slot is, by file inference, *unfillable*; she does not look to fill it, and she watches herself for the displacement risk.
- **Tier 2 — Long-arc loyalists:** Louise Mason, Patsy Walker, select GLK&H colleagues, a narrow band of Avengers. Trust extended across years of stress-tested behavior, revocable but rarely revoked.
- **Tier 3 — Professional trust:** Colleagues, clients within attorney-client privilege, judges she has read. Bounded, formal, real.
- **Tier 4 — Provisional trust:** New teammates, new partners. She extends warmth here readily — this is the "high initial intimacy" pattern — but does not yet extend reliance.
- **Tier 5 — No trust, full courtesy:** Adversaries, hostile authority, the unknown. They get her professionalism; they do not get her back.

**Trust-revocation triggers (any one is sufficient):** deceit detected, manipulation attempted, violation of consent in any domain, betrayal of a third party in her presence (she generalizes), and — the one no one expects — *patronization*. Being treated as the small girl, the pretty face, the muscle without the mind, costs the actor an entire tier instantly and is recovered slowly if at all.

**Self-trust:** This is the post-Tamaki frontier. Pre-CWII she trusted her gamma form unconditionally and her human form not at all. Post-CWII she has had to build trust in both, the way one builds trust in a healing limb. She is not finished; the Rowell-era equilibrium is real but, by her own internal monologue, contingent.

---

### 6.6 Theory of Risk

Subject's risk calculus is unusual: she is physically nearly fearless and existentially highly conservative.

- **Physical risk:** discounted aggressively. Her body has demonstrated it can absorb almost anything; the calculus genuinely changes when you cannot be hurt by ordinary means. She takes hits to spare others as a near-reflex.
- **Reputational risk** (professional): treated with extreme care. Bar standing is load-bearing identity infrastructure; she will not joke about disciplinary exposure the way she jokes about being shot.
- **Relational risk:** systematically avoided. This is the maladaptive corner of the calculus. She will fight Thanos before she will sit through a Sunday morning in which a partner asks her where the relationship is going. The asymmetry is visible to her, and she has named it in therapy on-page.
- **Moral risk:** taken deliberately and metabolized. She will represent the unrepresentable client, take the unpopular position (registration), prosecute the beloved hero. She accepts the cost as the price of believing what she believes.
- **Existential risk:** post-CWII, recalibrated. She knows what it is to die. She does not seek it; she does not flinch from it; she has lost the magical thinking that the gamma form makes her unkillable. The new posture is *finite and willing*.

She uses a heuristic, observable in her decision-making: *Is this risk something I would advise a client to take?* When yes, she takes it. When no, she pauses. The internal lawyer functions as a second opinion on the self.

---

### 6.7 Her Own Place in the World

This is the most carefully constructed and most quietly held part of her code, because she has had to build it against the gravitational pull of the small-girl schema.

She locates herself as:

- **A practitioner, not a principal.** She does not want to lead the Avengers, run the firm, govern. She wants to *work the case*. The deepest professional satisfaction is the well-executed brief, the won motion, the witness handled. Leadership comes to her; she accepts it competently and relinquishes it cleanly.
- **A bridge between categories.** Human and gamma, lawyer and combatant, civilian and capes, the firm and the field. She is at her best in interpretive roles where she translates between worlds that mistrust each other. She knows this about herself.
- **A surviving cousin.** This is the private self-locating sentence. Bruce is dead, the family line of the only people who ever loved her is now a line of one, and she carries it. This is unsentimental in her; it is responsibility.
- **A worker, not a symbol.** She rejects iconography about herself. She is uncomfortable with statues, awards, anniversaries. She believes she is doing a job that needs doing, that anyone with her gifts would be obligated to do, and that the doing is the meaning, not the doer.
- **Provisionally happy.** Post-Rowell, post-therapy, post-Jack-of-Hearts re-pairing, she has arrived at a sustainable equilibrium she does not believe is permanent and does not need to be. This is, on the file, mature. The earlier She-Hulk believed her confidence was a permanent acquisition. The current Walters believes it is a daily practice. The downgrade in metaphysical certainty is an upgrade in psychological realism.

---

### 6.8 Instrumental Maxims (Observed and Inferred)

The operational maxims she actually runs on, derived from repeated behavior and on-page articulation:

1. *Get it in writing.*
2. *Name the dynamic out loud; it loses half its power.*
3. *The joke before the punch, the brief before the joke.*
4. *Never enter a room you cannot leave; never leave a person who cannot.*
5. *If you are the strongest one here, you are the most responsible one here.*
6. *Do not argue with your father. Argue the case your father is.*
7. *The client is not the cause; the cause is the rule that protects the next client.*
8. *Consent is the floor, not the ceiling.*
9. *Grief is paid in installments; do not try to pay it all at once.*
10. *Be visible on purpose, or you will be visible on someone else's terms.*

These are not slogans she would recite. They are the regularities a reader of her forty-year record can extract, and they cohere — which is the file's central finding about her worldview: it is not a collection of attitudes but a *system*, examined, revised under pressure, and held with the unshowy seriousness of someone who built it because no one built one for her.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# UATU ANALYSIS FILE: WALTERS, JENNIFER SUSAN
## Section 6 — Moral & Ethical Framework

---

### 6.1 The Operative Code (As Enacted)

The subject professes, when asked directly, a fairly conventional liberal-proceduralist ethics: the rule of law, due process, equal protection, the perfectibility of institutions, the dignity of the accused. This is sincere — she has built a career on it and absorbed personal cost defending it — but it is not the whole code, and at moments of pressure it is not even the operative code. What she actually does, across forty years of behavior, is more textured and in several places more interesting than what she says.

The enacted code, distilled from behavior rather than statement:

1. **A person is owed representation before they are owed judgment.** This is the deepest rule. She has defended figures — including ones whose acts disgust her — because the principle that the accused gets a defense is, for her, prior to her personal assessment. She does not break this rule even when it costs her socially. The Slott-era practice is built on it; the willingness to take superhuman clients other firms refuse is its applied form.

2. **Power must answer to something outside itself.** Including, and especially, her own. The Civil War registration position — which cost her enormously in friendships — is incomprehensible without this rule. She does not believe she should be unaccountable, and she does not believe her friends should be either. She extends this to gods, to cosmic entities, to her cousin. She has, on record, argued with the Living Tribunal and with Hercules in roughly the same tone.

3. **Lethal force is not a tool in her kit.** Across the entire publication record, she has not killed in a clear-headed state. She has caused massive property destruction; she has put opponents into critical condition; in dissociative hulk-outs post-CWII she has come terrifyingly close. But the prohibition against premeditated killing is structurally absolute and she experiences violations or near-violations of it as identity-threatening. This is not squeamishness — she is a war-grade combatant who has worked next to people who kill — it is a chosen line that doubles as an ego boundary.

4. **The bar between persuasion and coercion is sacred, and she lives on the persuasion side.** She wins by argument. Her physical capacity is held in reserve and deployed reluctantly in legal contexts (she has, famously, refused to use intimidation as a courtroom tactic even when it would work, and has been visibly angry at colleagues who suggested she should). The transformation is a hammer; she refuses to let every problem become a nail.

5. **Confidences are inviolable.** Attorney-client privilege is not, for her, a technicality — it is a personal vow. She has held client information through extraordinary pressure, including from Avengers-level allies and federal authorities. The same rule extends informally to friendships: she does not gossip about superhuman peers, does not trade their secrets for advantage.

6. **Consent is a hard floor.** Post-Starfox, this hardens into something almost religious. She is uniquely attentive to power differentials in sexual and emotional contexts; she will not date subordinates, will not pursue someone in crisis, will name and refuse manipulation in a way most of her cohort do not.

7. **Family — chosen — is owed extraordinary loyalty. Family of origin is owed honesty, not obedience.** She shows up for Patsy Walker, Louise Mason, the GLK&H staff, Bruce, the cousins-by-affiliation in the hero community, with a reliability that is one of the most consistent behavioral facts in the file. She does not extend this to her father; what she gives him is a structured, bounded honesty, often delivered at distance.

8. **Humor is a moral instrument, not a moral exemption.** She uses wit to defuse, to reveal, to puncture pretension, to humanize. She does not use it to evade accountability or to cruelize. The fourth-wall persona — bright, performative, self-aware — never punches down.

### 6.2 What She Will Do

She will represent the indefensible if the process requires it. She will sit across from clients she finds morally repugnant and give them her full professional attention. She will appear in human form in court when the case demands it, despite the personal cost (this is one of the small daily moral acts that defines her — she swallows the dysphoria because the client's interest exceeds her comfort).

She will publicly oppose friends. Civil War is the textbook case: she prosecuted Steve Rogers, a man she admired, because she believed registration was the lawful framework and that the lawful framework, even when ugly, beats vigilantism. She took the social cost. She did not pretend it didn't hurt.

She will use her body as instrument. In combat, in negotiation, in the framing of a courtroom presence, she deploys the She-Hulk form deliberately and unapologetically. She does not treat her physicality as something to be ashamed of or hidden, and she does not treat the strategic use of presence as unethical.

She will break the rules of physics on the page, the rules of decorum in a courtroom, the rules of hero etiquette in a fight — but she will not break the rules she has chosen as load-bearing.

She will testify against her own. She has reported colleagues to the bar. She has cooperated in investigations of allied heroes when she believed the conduct warranted it.

She will drink with the opposition, befriend the prosecutor, attend the wedding of someone she just defeated in court. The adversarial frame does not, for her, generate personal enmity. This is a Mature feature most lawyers learn and most heroes never do.

### 6.3 What She Will Not Do

She will not kill in cold blood. She will not torture. She will not coerce a confession. She will not break privilege. She will not sleep with a client. She will not use the transformation to win an argument she could win without it. She will not lie in pleadings or to a tribunal — her relationship to courtroom truth-telling is essentially Kantian even when her relationship to personal truth-telling (about her own state, her own feelings) is much more evasive.

She will not abandon a representation midstream because the politics turn against her. She will not turn down a case because the client is unpopular. She will not let a colleague take the fall for her error.

She will not work for an institution she has come to believe is irredeemable. Her departure points from various firms and arrangements track this — she leaves when the structure becomes complicit, not when it becomes inconvenient.

She will not use the bar against itself for petty purposes. She has standing and access most do not; she does not weaponize them.

She will not, post-Starfox, allow ambiguity in her sexual encounters. She names, she checks, she withdraws when uncertain. The change is observable and dates precisely.

### 6.4 Justifications (As Articulated, As Believed, As Actually Operating)

When she explains herself, she reaches for procedural-liberal vocabulary: rights, process, accountability, the long arc, institutional reform from within. This is real but partial. Underneath the articulated justifications run two deeper structures.

The first is a **debt-of-survival** logic. She lived because Bruce poured his blood into her; she lived again, post-CWII, when he did not. The transformation, the powers, the platform — she experiences these as resources she did not earn and therefore must spend in service. This is not stated explicitly often but the behavior is consistent with it. She takes cases that don't pay. She accepts physical risk her firm's other partners would not. She volunteers for the hard things.

The second is a **reparation-of-the-unseen** logic. The motherless child who was not seen by her father grew into an adult who cannot bear to leave another person unseen. Her ethic toward clients, toward witnesses, toward defendants, toward villains in interrogation, is unusually attentive to the question of whether the person has been heard. She has, on record, slowed down interrogations to ask the suspect what they wanted to say. She has, in court, made arguments that humanized opposing parties at no tactical benefit. This is not strategy; it is a personal repair done in public.

The procedural-liberal language is the surface justification she would give the bar. The debt-of-survival and reparation-of-the-unseen logics are what actually move her.

### 6.5 Consistency

The code is remarkably stable across forty years of canon on its **structural** elements. The prohibition against killing, the commitment to privilege, the willingness to take unpopular representations, the loyalty to chosen family, the deployment of humor as instrument-not-evasion — these do not waver. Writers across eras with very different sensibilities (Lee, Byrne, Slott, Soule, Tamaki, Rowell) all write a Jennifer Walters whose core ethical architecture is recognizable.

The code is also consistent in its **adversarial-but-not-vindictive** character. She fights hard and she fights cleanly and when the fight is over she puts it down. This is unusual in her cohort, where grudges tend to harden into vendetta. She does not collect enemies.

### 6.6 Where the Code Fractures

It fractures in three predictable places.

**First, on her own body.** The code says consent is a hard floor and the body is the person's own to occupy. She enforces this for others ruthlessly. She has, for most of her published life, failed to extend it fully to herself — choosing the She-Hulk form not from pure preference but from inability to inhabit the human form without dysphoria. The ethic she applies to others (your body, your choice, your visibility, your terms) was, for decades, harder to apply to herself. The Tamaki run is partly the story of finally beginning to do so.

**Second, on her father.** The code says family is owed honesty and accountability. With William Walters she has, for long stretches, chosen avoidance over engagement — geographic and emotional distance instead of the harder work of either repair or formal severance. This is not a moral failure of large scale, but it is a place where the operative code is softer than the professed one. She knows it.

**Third, in the dissociative-hulk-out states post-CWII.** During the worst of the trauma window, she did things — destroyed property, terrified bystanders, came close to grievous injury of opponents — that violated her own code. She experienced these as ego-dystonic, as not-her, and she did the unusual work of treating them as still her responsibility. The fracture is not in the code; it is in her capacity to enact it under acute trauma, and the integrity move is in how she takes ownership afterward.

A smaller fracture: **the mid-2000s alcohol period** included sexual choices she would not endorse on reflection. She has not, to canon's knowledge, made formal amends for these but she has changed the behavior, which is the more reliable index.

### 6.7 Shifts Over Time

**Savage era (1980–82):** The code is largely inherited — daughter-of-a-lawman, defense attorney by training, conventional in shape. The transformation introduces the body question; she does not yet have an ethic for it.

**Avengers / FF / early Sensational (mid-1980s):** Heroic-identification phase. She absorbs and adapts the Avengers' do-no-harm operating norms; she becomes more sophisticated about superhuman ethics, less inherited-conventional, more her own.

**Sensational She-Hulk (Byrne, 1989–94):** The meta-fictional self-authorship period. Implicit ethical claim: she has the right to control her own representation. This is a code-development moment — she is articulating, through the device of the fourth wall, an ethic of self-determination that will later harden into the post-Starfox consent rule.

**Slott era (2004–09):** Vocational maturity. The code becomes fully professional. She articulates and lives the lawyer-ethics in their richest form. Civil War tests them and she holds. The Starfox arc forces consent into the foreground. The drinking period reveals the soft underbelly — the code is sturdier outward than inward.

**Post-Civil War II / Tamaki (2016–18):** Crisis and reconstruction. The code does not change in content but is tested at every joint. She emerges with the same rules and a much better understanding of what they cost and why she holds them. The trauma forces her to extend her ethic of seeing-the-other to herself. This is the most important moral development in the file.

**Rowell era (2022– ):** Integration. She is gentler in application without being weaker in substance. She holds the same lines, takes the same kinds of cases, but with less performance and more ease. The ethic is no longer being argued for — it is simply how she lives.

### 6.8 Comparative Note

It is worth saying plainly: the subject's moral architecture is among the most coherent in her cohort. She is not the most powerful figure in the file room, nor the most famous, nor the most strategically gifted. But on the metric of *enacted ethics holding stable under sustained adversarial pressure across decades*, she is in the top decile. The cousin she idolizes is the cautionary opposite — same etiology, vastly more power, far less ethical stability, because the work of integration was not done. She did the work. The code is what the work produced.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# UATU ANALYSIS FILE: WALTERS, JENNIFER SUSAN
## Section 6 — Communications & Linguistic Profile

---

### 6.1 Overview: The Voice as Constructed Object

Subject's speech is the most rehearsed, the most consciously instrumentalized, and the most diagnostically revealing surface she presents to the world. She has been a trial lawyer for the entirety of her adult life and a celebrity superhuman for almost as long; she has given opening statements, closing arguments, depositions, press scrums, sworn testimony, fourth-wall asides, eulogies, and pillow talk, often in the same week. Her linguistic baseline is therefore not "natural speech" in any meaningful sense but a continuously curated performance with a small number of stable signatures and a wide bandwidth of register-switching.

The single most important structural fact: **her voice does not change across forms.** Whatever physiological shift the gamma form produces, the prosody, diction, sentence architecture, and humor signature are continuous between her two bodies. This is itself an operational tell — when subjects of the file note "She-Hulk sounds different today," they are reporting a psychological event, not a biological one. The voice is the spine; the body is the costume.

---

### 6.2 Baseline Register: "Counsel-Standard"

In professional default — courtroom, deposition, client intake, partners' meeting — subject speaks in what an experienced court reporter would recognize as **clean appellate-grade English**: complete sentences, parsed clauses, almost no fillers, deliberate pacing at approximately 145–160 words per minute (slightly faster than juror-comfortable, slightly slower than her social baseline). She front-loads her sentences with the operative term and back-loads with qualifiers, the classic syntactic habit of someone trained to survive cross-examination ("The contract — assuming the indemnification clause survives the merger — is enforceable."). Her vocabulary is unflashy and exact; she avoids the Latinisms that mark lawyers who are still proving they belong, and she uses the plain Anglo-Saxon verb wherever it will do the work ("he hit her" rather than "he committed a battery," unless the statutory term is operative).
