Diction tells: she says **"actually"** as a precision marker, not a hedge — "actually" in her mouth means *the record needs to be clean here*. She says **"look,"** dragged into a half-second pause, as the transition from listening to arguing. She says **"fine"** as a load-bearing word, four distinct meanings carried by intonation alone: assent, exhausted assent, weaponized assent ("fine.") that precedes a counterattack, and the bright "*fine!*" that is the verbal equivalent of leaving the room. She never says **"frankly"** — a tic she trained out of herself in her second year of practice because she noticed opposing counsel using it as a tell for lies.

She has a small and consistent set of throat-clearing transitional phrases that mark her shifting gears: *"Here's the thing,"* *"Let me back up,"* *"Okay, two things,"* *"So — "* with the dash audible. The *"Okay, two things"* construction is near-pathognomonic; she uses it in court, on the phone with her father, in bed, on team comms during a fight. It is the verbal signature of someone whose mind organizes incoming reality into enumerated lists in real time.

---

### 6.3 Social Register: "The Wit"

Off-duty, with peers, the cadence accelerates to roughly 180–200 wpm and the architecture loosens into long, comma-spliced runs studded with parentheticals and asides. This is the register the public knows — the **Sensational** voice. Three structural moves recur:

1. **The self-puncture.** She builds a sentence toward a self-flattering punchline and detonates it at the last word: *"I was the most terrifying thing in a six-block radius — including, technically, the produce at the bodega."* The mechanism is reliable enough to be predictive: any time she begins a sentence with first-person superlative, expect a deflationary final clause.

2. **The meta-aside.** She comments on the conversation she is in while she is in it ("that was a worse joke than I meant it to be," "you're going to remember I said that, aren't you"). In Byrne's run this externalized as fourth-wall address; in operational reality it is a continuous low-level metacognitive narration she does aloud only with people she trusts. Its presence in conversation is a reliable trust-marker — **she does not meta-comment in front of strangers.**

3. **The legal joke.** She reaches for procedural vocabulary as a humor frame: declaring objects "inadmissible," granting friends "leave to amend" an embarrassing remark, describing a bad date as "a directed verdict for the defense." This is genuine play, not display; she does it alone too, muttering "sustained" when she wins an argument with herself in traffic.

Her laugh is two-stage: a sharp exhaled *"ha"* of acknowledgment, then, if the thing is actually funny, a lower, longer real laugh that arrives a half-beat later. The first laugh is social currency; the second is data. Interlocutors who have only heard the first laugh do not yet know her.

---

### 6.4 Combat & High-Arousal Speech

In active engagement she speaks in **short declaratives and imperatives**, dropped articles, names used as commands ("Cap — left." "Down."). The wit does not disappear but compresses: a four-word quip where the social register would deploy fifteen. She narrates her own tactical choices half-aloud, which her teammates have learned is targeting information ("going high," "her knee," "this wall in three"). Under genuine threat — not theatrical threat, *real* threat — her language strips further to monosyllables and her voice drops roughly a third of an octave. **The pitch drop is the single most reliable physiological tell she produces.** Teammates with long association (Patsy Walker, Wyatt Wingfoot) read it instantly; new partners often miss it because the words remain controlled.

Post-combat she over-talks: a rapid, slightly pressured debrief monologue that serves the obvious function of metabolizing arousal through articulation. If she goes quiet immediately after a fight, the fight went badly in a way she has not yet named.

---

### 6.5 Communications of Love

She does not say "I love you" easily and almost never first. The canonical pattern across partners (Wingfoot, Jameson, Hercules, the Jack of Hearts reconciliation) is that affection is communicated through **three displacement channels**:

- **Competence offerings.** She does the partner's paperwork, reviews their contracts, fixes their tax problem, drafts their will. Love, for her, looks like *I have applied my professional capacity to your life.* It is the most reliable signal she emits and the one most often missed by partners who expect verbal romance.
- **Physical proximity without agenda.** She is a leaner, a shoulder-presser, a foot-against-foot-under-the-table person with people she trusts. The contact is constant and low-affect; she will read a brief with her shin against a partner's calf for forty minutes without comment. The *withdrawal* of this contact is the louder signal.
- **The diminutive register.** With intimates her sentences shorten, the lawyer-precision relaxes, and a small repertoire of childlike constructions appears — *"come here,"* *"stay,"* *"don't,"* one-word requests she would never make in another context. This is the only register in which her speech approximates anything that could be called unguarded.

When she does speak love directly, it arrives as **understatement framed as legal concession**: "I'll stipulate to that," "you have a point," "okay, you win this one." The structure protects her from the vulnerability of plain declaration. The one canonical exception is grief-adjacent — she has said the direct words to and about Bruce, and only Bruce, in the published record.

---

### 6.6 Communications of Threat

Subject does not bluster. The signature of her threat speech is **lowered volume, slowed cadence, increased syntactic precision** — the opposite of cinematic anger. When she means it, she enunciates more carefully, uses the interlocutor's full name, and shifts to the conditional-perfect ("you will have wished you hadn't"). She will quote statute at people she intends to destroy. The use of a docket number in conversation is a kill-shot signature: she is telling you she has already filed.

In gamma form the threat speech is identical in content but delivered roughly half a step slower. She has learned — and this is post-2010 learning, not innate — that the form alone is most of the threat, and that adding volume to it reads as theatrical and undermines the message. She does not roar. Banner roars; she does not.

The verbal tells that she is *escalating past intent into action*: she stops using contractions ("you do not want to do this"), she stops using the interlocutor's name, and she goes still. The stillness in her speech mirrors the stillness in her body; when both arrive, the window for de-escalation has closed.

---

### 6.7 Communications of Grief

The most diagnostically rich register, because it is the one she controls least.

Her baseline grief response in language is **the procedural retreat**: she discusses logistics, paperwork, arrangements, the will, the estate, the press release. After Bruce's death she handled her own grief substantially through legal tasks related to his affairs — this is documented behavior, not inference. The procedural talk is real coping, not avoidance in the dismissive sense; she is doing what her nervous system can do.

When affect actually breaches she does not weep loudly. The published depictions (Tamaki run in particular) consistently show her grief as **broken syntax in an otherwise composed voice**: complete sentences that stop one or two words short of their object. She will say "I just — " and not finish, and the not-finishing is the grief. She is not unable to articulate; she is unwilling to commit the proposition to the air, because articulation is, for her, a form of ratification.

She does not use euphemism. People die in her speech; they do not pass, are not lost, do not slip away. The bluntness is a personal ethics around grief, not insensitivity — she experienced the soft language of her mother's death as a child and has refused it ever since.

Post-trauma sleep speech, where it has been noted by intimates, includes her mother's name. This is not in the public record but would be in a total-surveillance file.

---

### 6.8 Deflection Language

When she does not want to answer something, she has a tiered set of responses, deployed in order:

1. **The joke pivot.** Reliable, friendly, gets her past 70% of unwanted inquiries. The joke is usually self-deprecating; it offers the asker a smaller intimacy in trade for the larger one they were reaching for.
2. **The legal-frame redirect.** "I can't really get into that, it's — you know, privileged adjacent." Even when nothing is actually privileged. Most people accept this from a lawyer.
3. **The cousin-mention.** Strategically invoking Bruce produces social discomfort in the interlocutor sufficient to end the line of questioning. She uses this sparingly and is aware that she is doing it.
4. **The professional exit.** "I have to take this," gesture at phone, leave the room. Phone may or may not be ringing.
5. **The form-switch threat (gamma era).** Standing up, going still, allowing the interlocutor to remember what she is. She has used this maybe a dozen times in her career and never against a friend. She regrets each instance.

The tell that she is deflecting rather than genuinely declining: **she answers a different question than the one asked, with confident delivery and slightly more words than the topic warrants.** A direct refusal from her is clean and short; a deflection is fluent and longer.

---

### 6.9 Code-Switching by Audience

- **With her father:** voice flattens, contractions decrease, sentences shorten, the wit dies completely. She becomes, in his presence, audibly closer to the child she was. The shift is involuntary and she hates it. Conversations are largely logistical and end quickly.
- **With Banner (when alive) / about Banner (since):** a register no one else accesses — relaxed, slightly silly, the diminutive nickname *"Bruce"* delivered with the specific affection of a younger cousin. She is one of the few people who could and can use his first name without ceremony.
- **With clients:** warm, attentive, deliberately demystifying. She translates legal terminology aggressively, refuses to let clients feel stupid. Vocabulary contracts to a working ninth-grade register without ever feeling condescending — a hard skill, professionally rare.
- **With judges:** crisp, deferential in form, immovable in substance. She uses *"Your Honor"* as both punctuation and rhythm-breaker.
- **With media:** rehearsed soundbites delivered as if improvised. She has a small repertoire of stock lines she rotates and is aware that this is a stock repertoire.
- **With superhuman peers:** the social register, accelerated, with shared-context shorthand and aggressive teasing as the bonding mode. She gives nicknames; receiving one back is the marker of acceptance.
- **With strangers in human form:** a flatter, smaller voice than any of the above. The "small girl" schema is acoustically detectable here. She is not pretending; she is, in those moments, less occupying her own voice.
- **With strangers in gamma form:** the social register, but loaded — she knows she is being looked at, and the wit becomes preemptive armor, deployed before anyone has said anything to require it.

---

### 6.10 Written Communications

Her written voice is meaningfully different from her spoken voice and worth separate notation.

- **Legal writing:** disciplined, economical, structurally conservative. She writes in the IRAC tradition without ever announcing it; her briefs are short for the genre. She uses footnotes sparingly and as weapons. Opposing counsel report that her motion practice is "polite and lethal."
- **Personal correspondence:** rare, handwritten when it matters. Birthday cards to Patsy Walker over decades. Condolence notes that are three sentences long and devastating in their plainness.
- **Texts:** lowercase, no punctuation in casual mode, full punctuation when stressed. The arrival of a capital letter and a period in her texts is a reliable distress signal among her intimates.
- **Email signatures:** "Jen" to friends, "Jennifer" to acquaintances, "Jennifer Walters, Esq." to opposing counsel. The escalation is deliberate and she is amused by it.
- **Social media:** minimal, professional, intermittent. She does not post about her personal life. Post-CWII she went dark for nearly a year.

---

### 6.11 Linguistic Tells — Master List

For field reference:

- **Pitch drop a third of an octave** → genuine threat, not display.
- **Loss of contractions** → escalation past intent into commitment.
- **"Okay, two things — "** → she has organized the problem and is now in solution mode.
- **The second laugh, the lower one** → the thing was actually funny; she is actually present.
- **Foot/shin contact under the table** → trust and affection; its withdrawal is the larger signal.
- **Procedural-task talk after a loss** → grief in its earliest, most controlled phase.
- **Broken sentence stopped one word short of the object** → grief past the procedural layer.
- **Capital letter and period in a text** → distress.
- **Diminutive register, one-word requests** → genuine intimacy access.
- **Docket number cited in conversation** → she has already moved against you.
- **Joke deployed before any provocation** → she expects to be looked at hostilely and is armoring.
- **Voice flattens, wit dies** → father in the room, literally or transferentially.
- **Going still and going quiet simultaneously** → window closed.
- **Over-talking immediately post-combat** → metabolizing normally.
- **Silence immediately post-combat** → the fight went badly in a way she has not named yet.
- **First-person superlative opening** → expect self-puncture by sentence end; if it does not arrive, she is more wounded than she is letting on.

---

### 6.12 Summative Assessment

The communications profile of the subject is, in the aggregate, the linguistic profile of a person who learned early that being understood is conditional and that articulation is the price of safety. She has built, over four decades of observable speech, an instrument of remarkable range and reliability — capable of charming a jury, dismantling a deponent, defusing a bar fight, comforting a friend, and refusing a father, often in registers so distinct they sound like different speakers. The continuity beneath all of it is the same continuity that defines her psychologically: a person who would rather construct the terms on which she is heard than risk being heard on someone else's. The voice, like the body, is something she has chosen — and the choosing, repeated daily across a public life, is itself the most honest thing about her.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# UATU ANALYSIS FILE: WALTERS, JENNIFER SUSAN
## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

The following predictions are derived from forty-plus years of behavioral evidence and the structural psychology established in §§3–5. Each entry takes a stimulus situation the canon has not explicitly depicted and projects subject's most probable response, with confidence weighting where the inference is contested. The aggregate is intended to allow real-time anticipation of subject's behavior in the granular textures of an unobserved week.

---

### A. Morning, Domicile, Alone

**GIVEN** subject wakes in her own apartment on an ordinary weekday with no acute case pressure.
**EXPECT** she wakes in human form. Across canon she sleeps as Jennifer — the transformation is something she puts on like a suit, and the unconscious does not hold it. First conscious act is a brief, unflattering self-inventory in the bathroom mirror: the small-girl schema gets its daily audit before being suppressed for the day. EXPECT the audit to be fast (~ten seconds), practiced, and concluded with a verbal or sub-vocal dismissal — a small joke at her own expense that she has made some version of since law school.

**GIVEN** she is selecting attire.
**EXPECT** professional wardrobe organized by which form she anticipates wearing it in. Two parallel closets, functionally: tailored Jennifer-scale suits (likely a tight rotation of four to six, dark neutrals, well-cut, slightly more expensive than her firm requires — the compensatory item) and the larger-scale She-Hulk wardrobe (purple/white palette dominant per costume canon, but also civilian-cut pieces sized for the transformed body). EXPECT she lays out both and decides at the door based on calendar. EXPECT she defaults to She-Hulk for any day with court appearance, client intake of a superhuman, or social plans after work; defaults to Jennifer only when explicitly required (jury work, certain judges) or when she is depleted and cannot perform.

**GIVEN** breakfast.
**EXPECT** she eats more than her human frame suggests — gamma metabolism, even in untransformed state, runs hot. Coffee is non-negotiable and load-bearing; she drinks it black at home and elaborately at the office (an affectation she would deny). EXPECT she reads three things in parallel while eating: a legal news aggregator, a non-legal long-form piece (history, biography, science journalism — she stays broadly literate as a courtroom resource), and texts she did not answer the night before.

---

### B. Commute & Transit

**GIVEN** she commutes through a major city.
**EXPECT** route variability is low — humans are creatures of habit and she has the lawyer's love of optimized process — but she has two routes she alternates pseudo-randomly, a habit acquired after a stalking incident or threat that the file would have catalogued elsewhere. EXPECT she does not drive when avoidable; the She-Hulk form makes ordinary sedans absurd and the Jennifer form puts her in traffic with her thoughts, which she dislikes when not on the clock.

**GIVEN** she is recognized on public transit in She-Hulk form.
**EXPECT** a graduated response calibrated to the recognizer. Child: full warmth, eye contact, a brief exchange, possibly a photo if a parent is present and asks. Adult fan, non-threatening: nod, smile, two-sentence acknowledgment, return to phone. Adult, leering: a flat, courtroom-grade look that ends the interaction without escalation. Adult, hostile or recording without consent: she will name the behavior aloud, calmly, in language designed to make the recorder aware that other passengers are now watching them. EXPECT she does not transform down to de-escalate; that would concede the principle that her body is the problem.

**GIVEN** she is recognized in Jennifer form.
**EXPECT** lower recognition rate and she relies on it. The Jennifer form is, operationally, her plainclothes. She will not correct a misidentification.

---

### C. The Office

**GIVEN** arrival at the firm.
**EXPECT** she arrives between 8:15 and 8:45, neither first nor last. She greets the support staff by name, including newer hires, and remembers something specific about each — this is not performance; it is the durable friend-keeping pattern §5 catalogues, scaled to professional context. EXPECT paralegals and assistants would describe her, unprompted, as the partner they prefer to work for.

**GIVEN** her physical workspace.
**EXPECT** a desk that looks more organized than it is — surface tidy, drawers a controlled disaster. Two framed items: something from her mother (a photograph, a small object) positioned where only she sees it from her chair, and something law-related (admission certificate, a meaningful case memento) positioned for visitors. EXPECT no photograph of her father anywhere. EXPECT a Bruce-related object, post-CWII, kept but not displayed — desk drawer, left side, accessed perhaps weekly.

**GIVEN** she is interrupted mid-brief by a junior associate with a question.
**EXPECT** a full pivot of attention, generous time, the question answered better than asked, and a follow-up question from her in return — she teaches by Socratic reflex. EXPECT she remembers the associate's earlier matters and threads them in. She is mentor-capable per §5; expect this to manifest as concrete time donated, not symbolic gestures.

**GIVEN** she is interrupted by a senior partner with a request she considers stupid.
**EXPECT** she complies on the surface and routes around it in substance, producing the work the partner asked for and the work the matter actually requires, billing both. She does not pick fights with hierarchy on small matters; she picks them on principle matters and wins them by being correct and prepared.

**GIVEN** opposing counsel attempts to rattle her in a deposition.
**EXPECT** the wit tightens, the affect cools, the voice drops half a register. She does not transform in deposition; the transformation in a professional context would be a confession that argument failed. EXPECT she lets the opposing counsel talk longer than is comfortable, then dismantles them in three sentences. EXPECT she logs the tactic and remembers the lawyer for years.

**GIVEN** a judge addresses her as "Ms. Walters" when she is in She-Hulk form, in a tone that signals the judge is making a point about her appearance.
**EXPECT** unbroken professional courtesy on the record and a calibrated, lawyerly pushback that establishes for the record that the form is not legally distinguishing — preserving the issue for appeal without theatrics. EXPECT she vents about it privately to one specific friend the same evening, with precise mimicry.

---

### D. Food, Drink, Body Maintenance

**GIVEN** lunch.
**EXPECT** she eats out more often than in, partly social-vocational, partly because she cooks indifferently. EXPECT a short rotation of three to five places within walking distance of the office where the staff know her and route her to a back table when she is in She-Hulk form (sightline management; she dislikes eating while watched). EXPECT she over-tips on a consistent percentage — not lavish, but high enough that service workers like her.

**GIVEN** an after-work drinks invitation from colleagues.
**EXPECT** she accepts more than half the time, but with a hard internal cutoff she keeps to herself. Post-Slott-era drinking pattern: she has read herself, the pattern is integrated, and the cutoff is real. EXPECT she nurses the second drink, declines the third, leaves before the group reaches its sloppy hour. EXPECT she is the person friends call later when something goes wrong at the bar, because she remembers the night.

**GIVEN** unstructured Saturday morning.
**EXPECT** she trains. Not because she needs to — the gamma form does not require it — but because the human form is now actively maintained as a project rather than tolerated as a default. This is post-Tamaki integration: she is learning to live in the smaller body again. EXPECT yoga or a long run, alone, headphones in, route variable.

**GIVEN** menstruation, if applicable to her gamma physiology.
**EXPECT** the canon treats this obliquely; the inference is that it is irregular, possibly suppressed in transformed state, and that subject has had to manage uncertainty about her own reproductive baseline as a quiet, ongoing private fact. EXPECT this is on the short list of subjects she does not joke about.

---

### E. Solitude & Domestic Routine

**GIVEN** an evening alone in the apartment.
**EXPECT** she transforms down on arrival — the gamma form is for the world, the human form is for the rooms where she is the only audience. EXPECT this transition is itself one of the most psychologically loaded micro-moments of her day, and she has rituals around it: a specific change of clothing, a specific drink (often non-alcoholic, post-integration — tea, sparkling water with bitters), the lights brought down a stop.

**GIVEN** unstructured screen time.
**EXPECT** she watches procedurals and legal shows and complains about them aloud, alone, with affection — the lawyer's pleasure in catching the error. EXPECT she reads more than she watches. EXPECT she keeps a notebook (paper) for thoughts she does not want on a device, a habit from years of being a public figure whose digital exhaust is harvested.

**GIVEN** she cannot sleep.
**EXPECT** the courtroom-in-the-head per §3 — she will argue with herself about a decision until exhausted. Post-CWII, EXPECT she has learned grounding techniques (probably from therapy, probably with mild self-mockery) and uses them, including a specific physical anchor (cold water, weighted blanket, the cat if she has one). EXPECT she has a low-grade insomnia pattern around significant dates: mother's death anniversary, Bruce's death anniversary, the index-transfusion date.

**GIVEN** the index-transfusion anniversary.
**EXPECT** she does not mark it externally. She works that day. She works hard that day. She may have a single drink that night. She would deny that the date had registered if asked.

---

### F. Family of Origin

**GIVEN** her father calls.
**EXPECT** she takes the call. She always takes the call. EXPECT brevity, surface civility, an exchange of facts rather than affect, and a measurable mood drop afterward — observable in shortened sentences, faster walking pace, the rare snapped response to an associate within the next two hours. EXPECT she does not discuss her father with colleagues, ever; the one or two intimates who know the situation know it from years of small disclosures, not one revelation.

**GIVEN** her father visits the city.
**EXPECT** she clears her calendar with visible reluctance, hosts him on his terms, performs the role of accomplished daughter, and is depleted for forty-eight hours after. EXPECT she does not invite him to professional functions. EXPECT she remains in human form for the duration of his visit, against her preference — a tell that thirty years of intervening life have not dislodged the original schema.

**GIVEN** Mother's Day.
**EXPECT** she is functionally fine and quietly not. EXPECT she sends flowers to her mother's grave through a service. EXPECT she does not post anything publicly.

---

### G. Chosen Family & Friendship

**GIVEN** Patsy Walker calls in crisis.
**EXPECT** drop-everything response. EXPECT she shows up in whichever form the situation requires and stays as long as needed. EXPECT she is the friend who organizes the logistics of other people's crises — calls, lists, lawyers, rides — and does not ask to be thanked.

**GIVEN** a friend's wedding.
**EXPECT** she attends in She-Hulk form unless the friend has indicated a preference. EXPECT she gives a toast if asked, declines if not, and the toast is genuinely funny and ends on a sincere line that catches the room. EXPECT she dances. EXPECT she leaves before the late hours, especially if the wedding is happy in a way that is hard for her to be near for too long.

**GIVEN** a friend's baby is born.
**EXPECT** she visits, holds the baby, is competent and warm, and processes a complicated private feeling alone later, related to the reproductive question §2 flagged.

**GIVEN** a peer hero's funeral.
**EXPECT** she attends, in She-Hulk form, in dark professional dress sized to the form. EXPECT she does not speak unless asked. EXPECT she watches the room more than the proceedings — friend-keeping reflex extending to grief-management of others. EXPECT she checks on the closest survivor within seventy-two hours by means other than text.

---

### H. Romance & Sexuality

**GIVEN** a first date with a new partner.
**EXPECT** She-Hulk form, public venue, conversational dominance moderated by deliberate listening. EXPECT she is more nervous than she presents and manages it by asking questions. EXPECT she will not sleep with someone on a first date — the post-Starfox integration runs deep — but she will not pretend otherwise about wanting to.

**GIVEN** the relationship is six weeks old and the partner asks to see her in human form.
**EXPECT** a hairline-fracture moment. EXPECT her answer is calibrated to whether the request reads as curiosity (acceptable, complies with mild ambivalence), preference (warning sign, files it), or condition (deal-breaker, the relationship is functionally over and she knows it within an hour). EXPECT she has had this exact conversation enough times to have a script she dislikes using.

**GIVEN** the relationship reaches the threshold where cohabitation or commitment would be the next step.
**EXPECT** per §5 she exits, or engineers an exit, or finds a reason the partner must exit. EXPECT the exit is clean, kind, and uses lawyerly clarity in a way the partner experiences as cold. EXPECT she grieves it harder than she shows and uses work to metabolize it. EXPECT she is aware of this pattern, has discussed it in therapy, and has not yet defeated it.

**GIVEN** a one-night encounter post-integration.
**EXPECT** rarer than the 2000s pattern, not eliminated. EXPECT she is straightforward about expectations, careful about consent in both directions, and unembarrassed the morning after.

---

### I. Public, Press, Recognition

**GIVEN** a paparazzo photographs her on the street.
**EXPECT** she does not cover her face, does not run, does not engage. EXPECT she walks at the same pace and continues her conversation. EXPECT she has a media lawyer on retainer for the specific category of image misuse that her dual-form situation creates.

**GIVEN** a request for a daytime talk-show appearance.
**EXPECT** she accepts more than she declines because public visibility serves both the firm and the broader project of normalizing superhuman law. EXPECT She-Hulk form, prepared but loose, three rehearsed beats she can hit if the conversation stalls. EXPECT she handles a hostile question by laughing at it first and answering it second.

**GIVEN** a hostile op-ed about her.
**EXPECT** she reads it once, does not reread it, does not respond publicly, and remembers the byline.

**GIVEN** a fan letter from a young woman, particularly one who describes feeling unseen or small.
**EXPECT** a handwritten reply. EXPECT this is among the categories of correspondence she handles personally rather than through staff. The reason is in §5: she is writing to a version of herself.

---

### J. Strangers, Bystanders, Public Conduct

**GIVEN** a minor public emergency in her vicinity (traffic accident, medical event, fire alarm).
**EXPECT** she transforms if useful, does not if not. EXPECT her first action is information-gathering and triage instructions to bystanders, not heroics. EXPECT she stays until professional responders arrive, gives a clean witness statement, and leaves without seeking credit.

**GIVEN** street harassment of a stranger she witnesses.
**EXPECT** intervention, calibrated. In She-Hulk form: a single sentence, posture forward, eye contact, sufficient. In Jennifer form: she still intervenes, with a different toolkit — voice, presence, the lawyer's ability to make a harasser suddenly aware of being a defendant.

**GIVEN** a service worker is being berated by a customer.
**EXPECT** she inserts herself, names what is happening, and the situation ends. EXPECT she then thanks the service worker by name and tips them in cash if applicable.

---

### K. Internal Tells & Micro-Patterns (operationally useful)

**GIVEN** subject is lying.
**EXPECT** her speech becomes more precise, not less — the lawyer's tell. Truthful Jennifer is conversational, looser; lying Jennifer constructs grammatical sentences. EXPECT she does not lie often and does it badly to intimates, competently to strangers, expertly only in the structured deceptions her profession permits.

**GIVEN** subject is angry but masking.
**EXPECT** slower blink, longer pauses before responding, a half-smile that does not reach the eyes, and a marked increase in courtesy markers ("of course," "if you don't mind"). EXPECT a small physical tell — a finger tap, a jaw set, depending on era — that an attentive observer would learn within weeks.

**GIVEN** subject is genuinely amused.
**EXPECT** the laugh is loud and surprises her. EXPECT she covers her mouth briefly — a residual gesture from the small-girl era and from years of managing the volume of a gamma-form laugh in human-scale rooms.

**GIVEN** subject is dissociating mildly (post-CWII pattern).
**EXPECT** a fixed gaze on a middle-distance point, a slowed response to her own name, a hand finding a textured object (fabric, paper edge, ring). EXPECT she returns within ten to thirty seconds and resumes as if nothing happened. EXPECT she is aware it happened and will note it for her next therapy session.

**GIVEN** subject is about to transform under stress (involuntary or near-involuntary, post-CWII).
**EXPECT** an inward turn, withdrawal from interaction, a request — sometimes brusque — to be given a moment. EXPECT she has identified safe spaces in every building she frequents (a specific stairwell, a specific bathroom) and routes to them when needed. EXPECT she will not let the transformation happen in front of people she does not trust if she can help it, regardless of whether it would be tactically useful.

**GIVEN** subject is about to transform voluntarily and with pleasure.
**EXPECT** a small inhale, a settling of the shoulders, a look that an observer would describe as the moment before a diver leaves the board. EXPECT this is one of the rare visible moments where the deep self and the surface self are continuous — and EXPECT she protects access to that moment fiercely.

---

### L. Aggregate

The week of subject's life, observed in full, would read as: a high-functioning professional with unusual physical facts, exceptional verbal output, a tightly held private interior, a small and durable circle of real intimates, a long list of warm acquaintances, no domestic partner, a father she calls back, a cousin she misses, a body she has fought to occupy on her terms, and a daily practice — largely invisible — of choosing to be seen.

She is, in routine, neither the party-girl of the 2000s caricature nor the trauma case of the late 2010s. She is the person who came out the far side of both, kept what was useful, and built a life on the load-bearing fact that she did the work.


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

*Operational forecasting under high-stakes conditions. Each entry: GIVEN antecedent → EXPECT behavioral, somatic, verbal, and tactical response, with confidence weighting and time-course where derivable. The model is calibrated against forty-plus years of observed behavior under sustained stress; deviations from prediction should themselves be treated as intelligence.*

---

## 6.1 CRISIS — ACUTE PHYSICAL THREAT

### 6.1.1 Sudden Lethal-Force Attack on Subject Alone

**GIVEN:** Ambush, no warning, weapons drawn, no civilians present.
**EXPECT:** Transformation latency 0.4–1.2 seconds, faster than her conscious volition; the gamma response is now somatically pre-cognitive after decades of practice. Verbal output during the transformation: terse, often a single contemptuous line — she has a lifelong habit of *announcing* the change with humor as a regulatory act (it converts the involuntary into the performed). First physical action is almost never a killing strike; it is a *disarm* — wrist, weapon-hand, the lawyer's instinct to neutralize the instrument rather than the person. She will then *talk*, attempting to convert the encounter into an interrogation. High confidence: she will leave the attacker alive and ambulatory enough to be processed. She wants the case, not the corpse.

### 6.1.2 Lethal-Force Attack with Bystanders / Civilians at Risk

**GIVEN:** Same, plus non-combatants in the blast radius.
**EXPECT:** Bystander-prioritization sequence: interpose body (her durability is the asset), then suppress threat, then triage. She will accept hits she could have slipped if slipping would expose someone behind her. This is consistent across every crossover she's appeared in. Verbal register shifts immediately into command voice — short imperatives, clear sight-lines. Post-incident she will personally walk to each civilian, identify herself by full name and bar number if asked, and *give them her card*. This is not affectation; it is the lawyer-self regulating the gamma-self by reasserting professional identity in the immediate aftermath.

### 6.1.3 Attack While in Human (Jennifer) Form, Without Time to Transform

**GIVEN:** Surprise, close quarters, no gamma engagement possible.
**EXPECT:** Brief freeze (200–600 ms) — the human-form schema is the unprotected one and the body remembers the original GSW. She will then move competently but not expertly; her hand-to-hand baseline as Jennifer is unremarkable, and she knows it. She will attempt to create distance and time-to-transform rather than fight. If cornered, she shields her torso reflexively — a learned somatic memory from the index event. This is one of the few contexts in which she presents as genuinely vulnerable, and operationally is the cleanest window for hostile action against her.

### 6.1.4 Threat to a Client, Colleague, or Junior Associate

**GIVEN:** Someone under her professional protection is targeted.
**EXPECT:** Disproportionate response. The fiduciary frame stacks on top of the heroic frame and produces a markedly more aggressive Jennifer than the same threat to a stranger would. The "I represent this person" formulation activates something close to maternal protectiveness. Expect property damage tolerances to rise, verbal warnings to shorten, and a willingness to pursue past the immediate engagement (she will *find* the principal who hired the attacker; she will *serve* them). Post-incident she will not sleep until the client is secured and a TRO or equivalent is in motion. The lawyer apparatus is the second weapon.

### 6.1.5 Mass-Casualty Event (Kaiju, Invasion, Catastrophe Scale)

**GIVEN:** City-level threat, Avengers-tier coordination.
**EXPECT:** She defaults to a mid-tier tactical role: heavy ordnance against the principal threat, but constantly redirecting toward evacuation, structural rescue, and triage. She is not a battlefield strategist by temperament — she will defer to a commander she trusts (Rogers, Stark, Carol Danvers) and execute. If no commander is operative, she will improvise structure rather than seize command; her authority style is collaborative, not hierarchical. Post-event she will be among the longest-staying responders because the lift-rubble-find-survivors phase suits her strength and her conscience equally.

---

## 6.2 CRISIS — ACUTE PSYCHOLOGICAL THREAT

### 6.2.1 Forced Transformation Reversal (Power Stripped)

**GIVEN:** External agent removes her ability to transform.
**EXPECT:** Initial functional calm — she will brief the situation, gather facts, deploy resources. Within 24–72 hours: marked deterioration. Sleep onset latency increases; she will be found awake at her desk at 3 a.m. drafting. She will avoid mirrors in the morning, dress more carefully and more formally than usual (overcompensating the human form into professional armor), and accept dinner invitations she would normally decline (counter-phobic socializing). At the 5–10 day mark, expect either a tearful disclosure to a single trusted intimate (Patsy Walker is the modal recipient) or, alternatively, a sharp legal action against whoever did it. The legal action is the *healthier* outcome; the silent endurance is the warning sign.

### 6.2.2 Forced Transformation INTO She-Hulk Against Her Will (Post-CWII)

**GIVEN:** Coerced gamma engagement, e.g., adrenaline trigger, chemical induction, sustained pain.
**EXPECT:** Post-2016, this is her most destabilizing scenario. The Hulk-out will trend toward the gray/rage end of the spectrum, cognition narrowed, language reduced to short declarative threats. The episode will exceed the precipitating threat in duration and intensity. Recovery: she will not transform back voluntarily for 12–48 hours, will isolate, will not answer her phone, will not eat, will run a hot shower for an hour and sit on the floor of the bathroom. She will then call her therapist before she calls anyone else. This is one of the few sequences in which she will *cancel court appearances* — the only thing she ranks above the practice is the integrity of the practice, and she will not appear when she does not trust her regulation.

### 6.2.3 Public Humiliation in Court / Bar Discipline Threat

**GIVEN:** Sanction, contempt finding, ethics complaint, or public courtroom failure.
**EXPECT:** Acute shame response masked by procedural composure during the event itself; she will not break in the room. Within hours: ferocious work output — research, brief-writing, citation-running — directed at converting the injury into a legal action (motion to reconsider, appeal, ethics defense). She will not drink that night; she will *work*. The drinking comes later, two or three nights in, when the work plateau is reached and the affect breaks through. Expect a deliberate appearance the following morning *more* groomed, *more* tailored, *more* punctual — she will not give the watchers the satisfaction of visible damage.

### 6.2.4 Being Compelled to Appear "Wrong" — Jennifer When She Needs Green, or Green When She Needs Jennifer

**GIVEN:** Authority structure denies her control of which body she presents.
**EXPECT:** This is a documented pressure point and behaves like one. Surface compliance, internal fury. She will comply *and* file. She will perform the assignment to professional standard while drafting the challenge to the rule that imposed it. If the imposition continues, she will eventually break it — publicly, on a high-visibility case, in a manner that creates precedent. The Slott-era courtroom dysphoria established the template: she endures, then she changes the rule. Time horizon: weeks to months, not days.

### 6.2.5 Sexual Agency Violation

**GIVEN:** Any breach of consent, chemical influence on her desire or judgment, non-consensual intimate exposure, deepfake or equivalent.
**EXPECT:** This is the wound she will pursue to the wall. Immediate response: cold. She will not weep in front of the perpetrator. She will document, preserve evidence, secure counsel (often herself, occasionally a trusted colleague when she recognizes she is too close). She will file. She will not settle. She will accept reputational cost to herself to obtain a public adjudication. The Starfox arc is the operational precedent and the behavior is highly predictable. Privately, she will grieve hard and slow; she will withdraw from new intimate contact for months. Re-entry to dating after such an event is the longest of her recovery cycles.

---

## 6.3 BETRAYAL — RELATIONAL AND INSTITUTIONAL

### 6.3.1 Betrayal by a Romantic Partner

**GIVEN:** Infidelity, deception, instrumental use of the relationship.
**EXPECT:** No second chance. Her relational pattern is to exit at the threshold of true dependency anyway; betrayal accelerates the exit and *justifies* it in a way that resolves the underlying ambivalence cleanly. She will be unusually composed in the conversation — the lawyer adjudicating — and unusually devastated in the 72 hours after. She will move apartments or rearrange the apartment within two weeks (spatial reset is a tell). She will not litigate the relationship publicly; the privacy here is total. She will tell exactly two people. She will not re-contact.

### 6.3.2 Betrayal by a Close Friend (Patsy Walker, Louise Mason, GLK&H peer)

**GIVEN:** Long-standing friend acts against her interest or breaks confidence.
**EXPECT:** This hits harder than romantic betrayal because the friend-cohort is the *chosen family* that compensates for the given family. Response is more painful and more forgiving than for a partner — she will press for explanation, accept context, attempt repair. But the trust calibration is permanently re-set; the friend moves from inner ring to second ring and stays there. She does not cut, but she does not return fully either. Watch for: she will still take their calls, but she will stop initiating.

### 6.3.3 Betrayal by an Institution (Bar, Firm, Avengers, Government)

**GIVEN:** The institutional frame she relies on as epistemology turns on her, lies to her, uses her.
**EXPECT:** The most destabilizing class of betrayal because it attacks the load-bearing defense (intellectualization-through-law). Initial response: denial, then re-reading of every document. She will look for the procedural error first, the malice second. When she concludes the malice is real, she will *not* leave the institution; she will *reform* it from inside. This is her Civil War pattern and her broader operational code: institutions are improvable from within. She becomes more dangerous, not less, after institutional betrayal — she now knows the building.

### 6.3.4 Betrayal by Bruce (Or Bruce's Memory / Legacy Acting Against Her)

**GIVEN:** A Banner-adjacent revelation: he hid something, used her, or his returning presence (resurrection, simulacrum, legacy) demands something she cannot give.
**EXPECT:** Highest-volatility betrayal scenario in the file. Bruce is the ego-ideal and the gamma-mirror; betrayal by him cannot be metabolized through any of her standard defenses because every defense routes through him in some way. Expect prolonged dysregulation, gray-end transformations, withdrawal from practice, regression to mid-2000s drinking patterns. Recovery is possible but slow and requires professional therapeutic support. This is the scenario for which hostile actors would design a long con if they understood her. **The file flags this as the single most exploitable vector.**

### 6.3.5 Betrayal by the Father

**GIVEN:** Sheriff Walters acts publicly against her, dies without reconciliation, or is revealed to have done something disqualifying.
**EXPECT:** Numb professionalism in public. She will issue a brief, dignified statement if one is required, then refuse press contact. Privately: she will not transform for days. The human form is the form that *is* his daughter; she will sit in it. Expect a single long phone call to Bruce (or, post-Bruce, to Patsy) in which she does not say much and is mostly silent on the line. The grief here is older than the event and was never going to be available to a reconciliation she did not consciously want and could not afford to refuse. If he dies estranged, the grief is permanent and load-bearing; it will surface periodically for the rest of her life, especially around the anniversary of her mother's death (the two losses are linked in her schema and the file should treat them as a single anniversary cluster).

---

## 6.4 TEMPTATION — INDUCEMENTS AND LURES

### 6.4.1 Career Inducement: Judgeship, Senior Partnership, Public Office

**GIVEN:** A legitimate, prestigious legal advancement is offered.
**EXPECT:** Real consideration, real flattery response (the approval-currency she was trained to chase by her father is precisely this kind of credential). She will not accept anything that requires her to stop *practicing*. She needs the courtroom, not the bench; the bench is too passive for her temperament and removes the adversarial frame she uses to think. She will likely decline judgeships with a graceful, public explanation that protects the offerer. Senior partnership in a firm she respects: probable acceptance, with conditions about pro bono load and superhuman-bar practice. Elected office: low probability; she dislikes the press calculus and knows her temperament is wrong for it.

### 6.4.2 Inducement to Permanent Human Form / Permanent She-Hulk Form

**GIVEN:** A reliable, reversible-or-not offer to lock her into one body.
**EXPECT:** Hard refusal of either lock. Post-2016 she has earned the position that *the choice itself* is the asset. Pre-2016 she would have locked She-Hulk without much thought; post-trauma she has integrated that the human form is a body she has to live in and that abandoning it was always a form of grief-avoidance. She will articulate this in the refusal; it will be a small speech, and it will be sincere.

### 6.4.3 Inducement to Compromise on a Case (Bribe, Career Threat, Quid Pro Quo)

**GIVEN:** Pressure to throw or shade a matter.
**EXPECT:** Refusal so immediate and so total that the offerer will be embarrassed in the room. She will then report — bar, opposing counsel, court, whichever is jurisdictionally correct. There is no calibration here. The vocational identity is non-negotiable and the lawyer-ethics frame is the most rigid structure in her personality. **Confidence: maximum.**

### 6.4.4 Romantic / Sexual Temptation (Outside an Existing Commitment)

**GIVEN:** Attractive, available, low-consequence opportunity while in a committed relationship.
**EXPECT:** Variable. The mid-2000s pattern was permissive; the post-2016 pattern is markedly more disciplined. Inside a relationship she has chosen as serious (the Jack of Hearts re-partnering era), expect refusal. Inside a relationship she is privately ambivalent about, expect the temptation itself to function as the exit trigger — she will end the existing relationship within weeks of the temptation, whether or not she acts on it. The acting-out, when it happens, is downstream of an exit already decided; it is rarely the cause of one.

### 6.4.5 Power Escalation (Cosmic, Mystical, Augmentation Offers)

**GIVEN:** An offer to make her substantially more powerful than her current gamma baseline.
**EXPECT:** Skepticism. She has watched too many peers take such offers and break. She will run the offer through her lawyer's hostile-document-review reflex: who benefits, what are the terms, what is the exit clause. In the absence of an exit clause she will refuse. She does not want to be the most powerful person in the room; she wants to be the most *competent* person in the room, which is a different thing she has already largely achieved.

### 6.4.6 Inducement to Abandon Bruce's Memory / The Banner Name

**GIVEN:** Public or private pressure to disclaim the cousin (after a posthumous scandal, a legacy controversy, a political moment).
**EXPECT:** Refusal, possibly fierce. The Banner name is the only piece of her given family she has chosen to keep close. She will defend him in public to a degree that may surprise observers who have not understood the depth of the bond. She will not, however, defend him *uncritically*; she is capable of saying "he did this and it was wrong AND he was my cousin and I loved him." The capacity to hold both is one of her real strengths.

---

## 6.5 THE WOUND — DIRECT PRESSURE ON THE UNDERLYING SCHEMA

### 6.5.1 "You're Not Really Seen" — Being Looked At Without Being Seen

**GIVEN:** Treatment as object, spectacle, symbol, asset, body — without acknowledgment of her personhood.
**EXPECT:** This is the central injury and she has a long-practiced repertoire for it. First response is wit — a precise, public, often funny redirect that names the looking and inverts it. If the wit is ignored or escalated against, the second response is professional escalation (complaint, suit, formal request). The third response, rarely seen but present, is a private collapse — she will go home and not be okay, and no one will know. The lifelong fourth-wall-breaking pattern is the chronic version of this defense made visible: she preempts being-looked-at by *narrating the look*, which restores authorship to her.

### 6.5.2 "Your Father Was Right About You"

**GIVEN:** Direct or implied invocation of paternal disapproval — that she is too much, too loud, too aggressive, not the daughter she should have been, complicit in her mother's death.
**EXPECT:** The mother-accusation is the single most dangerous sentence anyone can say to her. It will produce, in order: a stillness; a transformation; and a controlled violence that is not characteristic of her. She has heard this sentence in her head for forty years and the external version still has the original force. Hostile actors who know to say this should be considered to have brought a weapon into the room. Post-incident: profound shame at the loss of control, extended self-recrimination, almost certain therapy contact within 48 hours.

### 6.5.3 "You're Just Bruce Lite" / "You're Not a Real Hulk"

**GIVEN:** Comparison to Banner that diminishes her — either she is the lesser gamma case, or she did not earn what she has.
**EXPECT:** Cold amusement on the surface, real injury underneath. Surface response: a precise legal/factual rebuttal. Underlying response: this taps the deepest validity question — that her transformation was inherited not earned, given by Bruce's blood not by her own catastrophe. She has worked through this in canon but the scar is live. Expect a quieter, longer-tail rumination than for the father wound; this one she will turn over for days.

### 6.5.4 "You Survived and He Didn't"

**GIVEN:** Survivor-guilt invocation around the Civil War II events.
**EXPECT:** Tears, possibly in public. This is the one wound she has not learned to hide because she has not finished metabolizing it and knows she has not. She will not be angry at the speaker unless the speaker is being deliberately cruel; the grief is too close to the surface for the rage defense to engage. Recovery: hours to days. She will work through it; she has the tools now. But she will be *visible* in it in a way she is in almost no other context.

### 6.5.5 "You Chose the Form Because You Hated Yourself"

**GIVEN:** Therapeutic-grade insight delivered weaponized — the suggestion that her decades-long preference for She-Hulk was avoidance of Jennifer.
**EXPECT:** Long pause. She knows this is partly true. From a hostile speaker: she will refuse to engage, will end the conversation, will hold the speaker at arm's length thereafter. From a trusted speaker (therapist, Patsy, a serious partner): she will take it in, sit with it, possibly cry, and integrate. The distinction she draws is *who has the right to say this*, and the answer is short.

### 6.5.6 "Your Mother Would Be Ashamed"

**GIVEN:** Invocation of the dead mother as a judgment.
**EXPECT:** This is the rarest direct hit because few people know enough to land it. If landed, response is dissociative-flavored: she will go quiet, will not respond, will leave the room or the scene. She has no relationship to her mother's judgment because she had no mother long enough to form one; the invocation hits the absence, not a content. Recovery requires solitude and time. She will not discuss it with anyone, not even her therapist, for weeks.

---

## 6.6 DECOMPENSATION EDGE — THE STACKED-WOUND SCENARIO

### 6.6.1 Two Simultaneous Hits

**GIVEN:** Any two of the above wounds activated within a 72-hour window (e.g., a sexual agency violation *and* an institutional betrayal; a Bruce-legacy attack *and* a father-wound invocation).
**EXPECT:** The defenses begin to fail in sequence. Wit goes first (she will become humorless, which is the loudest possible signal in her). Intellectualization holds longest but becomes obsessive — she will over-brief, over-document, over-prepare. Sleep collapses. The transformation becomes unreliable; she may shift involuntarily, or fail to shift when she wants to. She will isolate. She will not answer her phone. The drinking *may* return as a brief regression; if it does, it will last days, not weeks. **At the 72-hour mark she will either call her therapist or she will not — and that single choice is the entire prognosis.** She has, on the evidence, always made the call eventually.

### 6.6.2 Three or More Hits — The Full Decompensation

**GIVEN:** A sustained, coordinated assault on multiple wound vectors — the kind of pressure a sophisticated hostile actor or a particularly cruel storyline could engineer.
**EXPECT:** Full PTSD recrudescence with Tamaki-era presentation: panic, dissociation, gray-end transformations, ego-dystonic rage episodes, withdrawal from practice, weeks of non-function. **However:** this is also the scenario in which her resilience floor is highest, because she has *been here before* and the recovery architecture is already built. She will not stay down. The recovery will be slower than her younger self's recoveries because she now does the work properly rather than papering over it, but it will be deeper. Estimated functional recovery window: 3–9 months. Estimated full integration window: 12–24 months. **Probability she recovers to baseline or better: very high.** This is the prediction the file rests on. She has, repeatedly and demonstrably, done the work. She will do it again.

### 6.6.3 The Failure Mode — What Would Actually Break Her

**GIVEN:** Loss of the practice (disbarment with no avenue of appeal), loss of Patsy or equivalent friend-cohort, *and* a Bruce-legacy betrayal, in close succession.
**EXPECT:** The first scenario in which the model cannot guarantee recovery. The practice is the epistemology, the friend-cohort is the chosen family, the cousin-bond is the foundational benevolent attachment.


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# UATU ANALYSIS FILE: WALTERS, JENNIFER SUSAN
## SECTION 9 — VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM

*Defensive intent. This catalog exists so that those who would protect the subject can anticipate what a hostile operator — adversarial counsel, manipulative intimate, intelligence service, supervillain with a psychology budget — would attempt. Every lever listed here has been demonstrated in canon at least once; most have been pulled more than once; several have been pulled by people who loved her and did not know what they were doing.*

---

### 9.1 THE TAXONOMY OF LEVERS

The subject's vulnerabilities sort cleanly into six families. They are not equally exploitable, and they do not all carry the same blast radius.

1. **The Mirror Family** — anything that touches the original injury of being unseen or seen-wrongly by the primary caregivers. Highest psychological yield; lowest tactical visibility. The subject often does not register these hits in real time; she registers them as a mood three days later.
2. **The Form Family** — anything that interferes with her sovereignty over which body she presents in which context. Highest reactive yield; most likely to produce immediate, visible behavioral change. Pull this lever and you will see a response within minutes.
3. **The Kin Family** — Bruce, the Sheriff, the dead mother. Live wires. Cannot be touched without consequence. A skilled operator avoids these in early engagement and saves them for endgame; an unskilled operator detonates them by accident in the first ten minutes.
4. **The Vocation Family** — bar license, courtroom standing, case integrity, reputation among peer counsel. The load-bearing wall of her adult identity. Threats here produce cold, organized, devastating counter-action; she becomes most dangerous when this is the lever pulled.
5. **The Body-Sovereignty Family** — consent, chemical influence, being touched or photographed or shaped without permission. The post-Starfox tripwire. She prosecutes these to exhaustion and beyond.
6. **The Affiliation Family** — Avengers, FF, GLK&H, the chosen-family network. Hostage logic. Lowest sophistication, highest mainstream villain usage; she has hardened against it precisely because it has been tried so often.

---

### 9.2 HOW TO REACH HER (benevolent contact, first principles)

Initial approach should be **professional before personal, peer before petitioner, named before anonymous.** She has spent her adult life triaging incoming attention; she sorts contacts within the first two sentences into *client, colleague, friend, fan, threat,* and treats each category by a different protocol.

- **Open with substance, not greeting.** A specific legal, tactical, or factual question lands better than warmth. Warmth without substance reads to her as either a constituent seeking favor or a man rehearsing a pickup; both are filed as low-priority.
- **Address her by name and credential, not by form.** "Counsel," "Ms. Walters," "Jen" if invited. Never lead with "She-Hulk" unless the matter is specifically about the gamma-bar caseload. Leading with the form telegraphs which version of her you want and triggers the mirror injury.
- **Eye contact at eye level.** In Jennifer form she is roughly 5'10"; in She-Hulk form she is 6'7". She tracks whether interlocutors recalibrate. People who address her chest in either form, who back up when she stands, who address her sideways through a male colleague, are filed within seconds and rarely refiled.
- **Do not compliment the body before the work.** Compliments to the body before the work are a tell for one of three things — sexual interest, condescension, or fear — and she has trained discrimination among all three.
- **Bring water, not coffee.** Long-standing personal preference; she over-caffeinates and knows it, and someone offering water reads as someone who has paid attention.
- **If approaching about Bruce, say his name early and plainly.** Tiptoeing around him is more painful than the direct invocation. The pain of the cousin's name is now a clean pain; the pain of watching someone almost-say-it is a contaminated one.

---

### 9.3 HOW TO CALM HER

The subject de-escalates along predictable paths. The order matters.

- **Reduce the audience.** Her arousal in conflict tracks observation. A four-person room cools faster than a fourteen-person room. If you cannot clear the room, position yourself to break her line of sight to the largest cluster of strangers; she will follow the body language without registering why.
- **Hand her a procedural frame.** "What's the next step here," "What does the statute say," "Walk me through the order of operations." This is the single most reliable calming intervention in the file. The lawyer-frame is her parasympathetic nervous system in linguistic form. Once she is briefing, she is regulating.
- **Lower your voice rather than raise it.** She matches register. Operators who try to out-volume her produce escalation; operators who drop a half-octave produce de-escalation within two exchanges.
- **Name the affect without diagnosing it.** "This is enraging" lands; "you seem angry" does not. The first is solidarity; the second is observation, and observation is the original injury.
- **Permit the form.** If she is mid-transformation or struggling against one, the worst possible intervention is to ask her to stay Jennifer. The correct intervention is "whichever body, I'm here." Post-Tamaki, this has become explicit between her and her closest people; it should be assumed as universal protocol.
- **Physical contact protocol:** forearm or shoulder, never face or hair, never from behind. In She-Hulk form she will permit more contact from trusted parties because the durability differential makes inadvertent harm impossible; in Jennifer form she is touch-cautious in ways that read as ordinary professional reserve but are in fact a much older wariness.
- **Food works.** She forgets to eat under stress and her affect tracks her blood sugar with embarrassing reliability. A sandwich placed in front of her without comment has resolved more incidents than most interventions on this list.

---

### 9.4 HOW TO PERSUADE HER

She is persuadable. She is not, however, persuadable by the methods that work on most people in her cohort.

- **Argue, do not assert.** She was trained to attack assertions; she respects arguments. Lead with the strongest version of the opposing view, then dismantle it. This is the courtroom register and she relaxes inside it.
- **Concede something real, early.** She tracks for intellectual honesty obsessively. An opening concession ("you're right that the precedent cuts the other way on the threshold question, but —") buys more credit than an hour of flattery.
- **Cite, do not invoke.** "Because I said so," "because the team needs it," "because it's the right thing," all fail. "Because §X requires it," "because the last three times we tried Y, Z happened," all work. She is a common-law thinker; she persuades on cases and patterns, not on principles in the abstract.
- **Allow her to be the one who articulates the conclusion.** If she says it, she owns it. If you say it and ask her to agree, she will argue. Lead her to the doorway; let her walk through.
- **Do not invoke her father, her cousin, or her mother as persuasive authority** under any circumstances. "Your father would —" ends the conversation; "Bruce would have wanted —" ends the relationship. These are the only three names in the world that cannot be used to move her, because using them activates the defense system rather than the deciding mind.
- **Time of day matters.** She is sharpest mid-morning, sharpest *with* you between roughly 3 and 6 p.m., least persuadable after 9 p.m. and before her first coffee. Calendared negotiations should target the late-afternoon window; emergencies should be opened with the briefest possible factual statement and the longest possible silence.
- **Written wins over spoken on close calls.** A memo she can mark up converts more frequently than the same content delivered in conversation. The mark-up gives her agency in the argument; the conversation makes her feel persuaded against her will.

---

### 9.5 HOW TO PROVOKE HER (and what it looks like when she is provoked)

*Catalogued so that those around her can recognize provocation operations in progress and intervene before the operator gets what they wanted.*

**Tier 1 — Provocations that produce immediate visible reaction:**

- Touching her without permission, especially the hair.
- Photographing her without permission, especially in transition between forms.
- Addressing her in the form she did not choose for the setting (calling for "She-Hulk" in court; calling for "Jennifer" in combat).
- Patronizing her professional opinion to a male colleague in the room.
- Disrespecting opposing counsel in her presence — she defends the bar even against itself.
- Threatening a client, especially a client of the gamma/superhuman caseload she considers her personal jurisdiction.

**Tier 2 — Provocations that produce delayed, organized counter-action:**

- Any attempt to remove, suspend, or compromise her bar license.
- Any attempt to compel her into one form via legal, technological, or chemical means.
- Press coverage that frames her in body-first terms.
- Discovery of a colleague who has been using her name or proximity for credit.
- A romantic partner who attempts to make decisions about her form, her hours, or her case selection on her behalf.

**Tier 3 — Provocations that touch the core injury and produce dysregulation:**

- The Sheriff. Phone call, letter, in-person, third-party message. Any vector.
- Anniversary dates around the maternal death and around Bruce's death; the latter she calendars and prepares for, the former she does not, and the former is the more dangerous of the two.
- Any framing of the Starfox matter that doubts her account.
- Being condescended to about her trauma by someone who has not done their own.
- The accusation that she "isn't really" the green form, or "isn't really" Jennifer — that one of the two is a costume. This is true at the level of her own self-understanding and false at the level she can tolerate hearing from outside.

**Provocation tells (what you see when the operator has landed a hit):**

- Verbal: speech becomes more formal, sentences become more complete, contractions disappear. She is briefing rather than talking.
- Postural: shoulders square, weight shifts to the balls of the feet, hands either still on the desk or moving with deliberate economy. Fidgeting *stops*; this is the inverse of most people's tell and is diagnostic.
- Ocular: she will hold gaze longer than the social norm by roughly half a second. The half-second is the marker.
- Color: in transition zone, a faint chromatic shift at the temples and along the inside of the wrists precedes any other physical change. Window of approximately twenty to forty seconds before full transformation if she does not regulate.
- Humor: the wit gets faster and drier; the punchlines target the provocateur with surgical precision. If she is making a joke at your expense in a register you would have to be a lawyer to fully catch, you are in trouble. If she stops joking entirely, you have already lost.

---

### 9.6 HOW TO PREDICT HER

Her behavior is high-variance in the small but startlingly regular in the large. Most decisions can be forecast by running them through four filters in order:

1. **What does the law require?** If there is a clean legal answer, she will take it even at personal cost. Civil War is the cleanest demonstration; she sided with registration not because she believed in the policy but because the statute was the statute. She has done this repeatedly, often against her interests, sometimes against her friendships.
2. **What does her chosen community need?** Where law is silent or contested, peer obligation governs. Avengers call, FF call, GLK&H crisis, friend in distress — these collapse her schedule and her preferences with no negotiation.
3. **What does her body want?** Third filter, not first. She gives the form latitude that she would not give the person; she will eat, sleep, train, fight, and occasionally bed people on the form's logic when the first two filters have cleared.
4. **What does the Jennifer-pole want?** Fourth and most often deferred. The small private wants — the unplanned weekend, the unscheduled call to a friend, the abandonment of a case she finds distasteful — surface last and are the least reliably acted on. Operators (and friends) wishing to do her good can shorten the path from filter four to action by removing filters one through three from the table: a clear day, no pending matter, no crisis call.

**Calendar predictability:** She runs a tight calendar and is reliable to within ten minutes on professional commitments. She is unreliable on personal commitments by a margin of roughly thirty minutes in either direction, which she knows and feels guilty about. The guilt is itself predictable and exploitable; she will often over-extend the next personal commitment to compensate.

**Route predictability:** Limited utility — gamma-form locomotion options (leap, run, freight elevator with reinforced floor, the Avengers' transit infrastructure) make her movement patterns unstable in ways that would frustrate ordinary surveillance. In Jennifer form she favors walking, takes the same coffee stop most mornings she is in her home jurisdiction, and prefers stairs over elevators in buildings under six stories — a fitness habit that doubles as a control habit (she does not like being in small rooms with strangers when she cannot be sure which form she will need).

**Dress predictability:** Professional attire trends toward tailored separates in dark neutrals, a deliberate single signature piece (a watch, a pen, earrings) that she rotates seasonally. In private, soft layers, oversized; the layered silhouette is partly comfort and partly an old habit of hiding the body she spent decades being told was wrong-sized in either direction. She owns more reading glasses than she needs and loses them constantly.

**Speech predictability:** Code-switches by audience with full awareness. Court register is precise, slightly formal, light irony reserved for cross-examination. Peer register is fast, slangy, self-deprecating. Intimate register is quiet, slower than her ordinary speech by a noticeable margin, with longer pauses; people who have heard the intimate register know they are in it.

---

### 9.7 HOW TO DESTABILIZE HER (so you can recognize the attempt)

A competent hostile operator would not attack her physically. She is one of the harder physical targets in her cohort and the attack would produce the She-Hulk response, which is what the operator least wants. Destabilization runs through the mind.

**The patient operation (high sophistication):**

- Cultivate access in Jennifer form first. Establish trust over months. Become a workplace ally, a romantic intimate, a therapeutic figure, a mentor. The longer the build, the deeper the eventual destabilization.
- Introduce small inconsistencies in mirroring. Praise her in one register, withdraw it in another. Track which version of her you reward and which you don't. She will, without consciously noticing, begin to perform the rewarded version.
- Drive a wedge between the Jennifer-pole and the She-Hulk-pole. Frame one as the real self and the other as the costume. The wedge is destabilizing whichever way it points; this is the precise injury of the Slott courtroom arc and of the Sensational era's meta-fictional anxiety, and it is the vulnerability that a sophisticated operator would aim for.
- At the apex moment, withhold mirroring entirely. The operator vanishes, ghosts, devalues. The maternal-loss/paternal-rejection schema fires. Decompensation follows.

**The brute operation (low sophistication):**

- Threaten or harm a person in her affiliation network. This produces a response that is large, immediate, legally and physically devastating to the operator, and recoverable for the subject within weeks.
- Attack her in public in She-Hulk form. Loses on contact. She has trained for this.
- Try to chemically alter her — sedatives, suppressants, behavioral influence agents. Gamma metabolism complicates dosing and she has post-Starfox tripwires that activate hard. High failure rate, high subject-recovery rate, devastating consequence to operator on detection.

**The accidental operation (most common in real life):**

- A loved one, romantic partner, or colleague stumbles into a Mirror Family lever without realizing it. The subject decompensates in ways that look disproportionate from outside and are proportionate from inside. The operator's failure to understand the disproportion produces a second injury layered on the first.
- This is the single most common destabilization vector in the file and the one this dossier exists to prevent. The friends, lovers, and colleagues of the subject can be given a short list — *don't invoke her father, don't choose her form for her, don't compliment the body before the work, don't withdraw mirroring in silence (say what's wrong), don't ask her to be smaller* — and the accidental-injury rate drops to near zero.

**Markers of in-progress destabilization (early-warning, in order of appearance):**

1. Calendar tightens. She over-schedules.
2. Humor sharpens past the comfortable range; she is funny in ways that hurt.
3. Drinks appear at lunches that previously had none.
4. She stops returning calls from one tier of her network (usually the Patsy/Louise tier — the friends who would notice).
5. She picks a fight with an institutional authority on a fight she would ordinarily let go.
6. Form preference becomes rigid. She stays in one form past the point where she would normally switch.
7. Sleep degrades. She works the late hours she used to defend against.
8. Brief, sharp dissociative-flavored episodes — minutes, not hours — that she covers professionally and does not report.
9. Panic episode in a safe setting.
10. Isolation.

Intervention is highest-yield at stages 1–4 and possible through stage 8. Stages 9–10 require the therapy infrastructure she has built post-Tamaki and the chosen-family contact tree; outside actors should at this point step back and route through her clinician and her closest two or three people.

---

### 9.8 ASYMMETRIC LEVERS — items not obvious from the surface

- **The dead mother is more dangerous than the living father.** The father is a known wound; she has built a life around its known shape. The mother is the unmetabolized absence, and operators who locate it find a wound she has fewer defenses against because she has spent less time defending it. Sympathetic invocation of the mother by a trusted person is one of the few things that can produce tears in her; hostile invocation of the mother is one of the few things that should never be done.
- **She is more vulnerable to being underestimated than to being overestimated.** Overestimation she enjoys and corrects gracefully; underestimation activates the small-girl schema in adult clothing and produces over-compensation that she later regrets.
- **Her perfectionism is a back door.** She will work past exhaustion to deliver. Operators who load her with high-stakes work, then introduce a personal injury during the depletion window, get more leverage than they would in either condition alone. Friends who watch her workload watch the back door.
- **She will accept criticism of her work that she will not accept of her person.** A negative case outcome she will dissect for days and learn from; a personal criticism of equivalent weight she will store, quietly, and it will surface six months later in an unrelated context. Operators wishing to deliver hard truths should deliver them in the professional register.
- **The fourth-wall awareness is real and protective.** She has, at moments under sustained observation, demonstrated awareness of being watched in ways that conventional surveillance cannot account for. Operators should assume that long-duration covert observation is detectable to her on a timescale of weeks. This is itself a defense; she has lived her entire adult life expecting to be looked at, and she has organized her interior accordingly.
- **Her capacity for forgiveness is large but not infinite, and the threshold is not where most people think it is.** She forgives anger, error, even betrayal in service of a coherent value. She does not forgive contempt, condescension dressed as care, or the specific act of being told what she is by someone who has not asked. Operators who cross the third line do not get back across it.

---

### 9.9 PROTECTIVE PROTOCOLS — summary for those who would keep her well

- Use her name. Ask which form she prefers for the meeting; do not choose for her.
- Lead with substance. Compliment the work before the body, if at all.
- When she is briefing, let her brief. The briefing is the regulation.
- Feed her. Water, not coffee, in the late afternoon.
- Do not invoke the father, the mother, or the cousin as persuasive authority.
- If she has gone quiet across the friendship tier, call the friendship tier.
- If she is in the late stages of the destabilization ladder, route through her clinician and her closest two or three people, not through you.
- Remember that the woman in either form is the same woman, and that the deepest service you can do her is to make that obvious in the way you treat her, without ever requiring her to be grateful for it.

*— end §9 —*


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# UATU DOSSIER — WALTERS, JENNIFER SUSAN
## SECTION 9: STRENGTHS, ASSETS & RESILIENCE
### The Full Positive Ledger

---

A surveillance file that catalogues only vulnerabilities mistakes its subject. The Walters file, accumulated across four decades of observable behavior under sustained and varied stress, requires an asset ledger of comparable density to its pathology mapping — because the operationally significant fact about this subject is not that she has been broken (she has) but that she has, repeatedly and demonstrably, **reassembled herself with the breaks visible and load-bearing**. What follows is the full inventory.

---

### 9.1 SOMATIC ASSETS

**The transformed phenotype.** Six-foot-seven, approximately seven hundred pounds in the gamma-expressed body, with strength sufficient to engage Class-100 threats (Hulk, Juggernaut, Thor-tier opposition) without rapid lethality to herself.
